Fasid Masaqah Contract and Compensation: The Hanafi Ruling
Explaining the ruling and compensation for a fasid masaqah contract.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a masaqah contract with uncertain wage is fasid in the Hanafi school and state the compensation due to the planter.

Core Idea
A masaqah contract with uncertain wage is fasid; the planter receives plant value and ujr al-mithl.

In plantation partnerships (masaqah), the compensation must be certain. If the worker's wage is a portion of the future produce, the contract becomes fasid like qafiz al-tahhan. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the compensation mechanism, including the distinction between plant value and labor wage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and defect
Recognize that the masaqah contract under discussion involves a landowner hiring a planter in exchange for half the produce, which is uncertain. This uncertainty (jahalah) triggers fasid.
The defect is in the wage, not the essence of the contract.
2
Apply qiyas to qafiz al-tahhan
Compare the contract to the known fasid contract of qafiz al-tahhan, where a miller is hired with a portion of the flour. Both involve compensation from the product of the worker's own labor, creating uncertainty.
This qiyas is the primary proof in al-Hidayah.
3
Derive the legal consequence (fasid)
Because the contract resembles a prohibited transaction, it is fasid (voidable). The ruling: the trees and fruit belong to the landowner, as ownership remains with the original owner.
Fasid is distinct from batil; the contract may be rectified by removing the defect.
4
Determine compensation for the planter
Since the plants are attached to the land, they cannot be returned. The planter receives the value of the plants (qimat al-gharas) and an equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl) for his labor.
Both are separate: plant value for the material, ujr al-mithl for the service.
5
Understand the separation of plant value and ujr al-mithl
The planter's plants are valuable in themselves, while his labor is an accident that becomes valuable through the contract. Hence, ujr al-mithl is not included in plant value.
This answers the objection that plant value alone sufficies.

فاسد ہے۔
یعنی رب الارض نے نصف زمین کے بدلے وہ آدھے پودے عامل سے خریدے جو وہ لگائے گا اور شن مجہول ہے کیونکہ پودے ابھی معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے مجبول ہیں اسلئے عقد فاسد ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فر ما تے ہیں کہ ان دونوں دلیلوں میں یہ دلیل پختہ ہے جو ہدایہ میں مذکور ہے۔
Book of Masaqah. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary of Bidayah Volume 13. Because in this thing, partnership is a condition which is already existing, i.e., the land in which the worker's action has no input. Also this is in the meaning of qafiz al-tahhan because here it is as if the landowner hired the worker in exchange for something that is produced from his work, in exchange for part of it, and that is half the garden. So when it is at the level of qafiz al-tahhan, the contract is fasid. When the contract is fasid, then how will the division be? He said: all the trees and their fruit belong to the landowner, and the planter will receive the value of his plants and his ujr al-mithl. That is, for the plants he planted, there will be a value, and for the work he did, there will be an equivalent wage. Because here the contract is fasid. The original ruling should have been that the planter uproots his plants entirely, but since the plants have become attached to the landowner's land, returning the plants is impossible, so returning their value is necessary. Question: When the value of the plants is returned, what need remains for the ujr al-mithl? Answer: The plants are self-subsisting, they are valuable in themselves, while the work is an accident, not valuable in itself, but becomes valuable through the contract. Therefore, ujr al-mithl is not included under the plants; rather, his plants were separate and his work was separate, so the value of the plants will be separate and the value of the work will be separate. And in takhrij... i.e., there is another method of takhrij for this issue; in other words, there is another proof for the fasidness of the issue. Summary: The mentioned contract is fasid, whose proof has been stated that the contract is at the level of qafiz al-tahhan, thus it is fasid. And the Shaykh in Kifayat al-Nihayah has stated its second proof, whose gist is the ignorance of the wage, and due to this ignorance, the contract is fasid. That is, the landowner bought from the worker half the plants he would plant in exchange for half the land, and the thing is unknown because the plants are non-existent at the time, thus the contract is fasid. The author of al-Hidayah says: Among these two proofs, the proof that is firm is the one mentioned in al-Hidayah.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage discusses a fasid (voidable) contract in masaqah (plantation partnership). The author first states that the contract is like qafiz al-tahhan—a known invalid contract where the compensation is uncertain. Here, the landowner hires the worker in exchange for half the produce, but the worker's share is uncertain because it depends on future work. Hence the contract is fasid. The ruling: the trees and fruit belong to the landowner, because the contract is void and ownership remains with the owner. The planter is entitled to the value of the plants he planted and an equivalent wage (ujr al-mithl) for his labor. The plants cannot be returned because they are attached to the land, so their value is given. Then a second proof is presented: the contract is also fasid due to jahalah (ignorance) of the subject matter (the future plants) and the wage. Among the two proofs, the one in al-Hidayah is considered firmer. This is a typical Hanafi analysis of fasid contracts in sharecropping arrangements.

Key Terms
قفيز الطحان (qafiz al-tahhan): A type of fasid contract where a miller is hired with a portion of the flour as wage, which is uncertain.
اجر مثل (ujr al-mithl): The standard market wage for similar work.
عقد فاسد (aqd fasid): A contract that is valid in essence but defective in description (e.g., due to uncertainty).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid masaqah contract, what does the planter receive?
A) Only the value of plants
B) Only ujr al-mithl
C) Value of plants and ujr al-mithl
D) Nothing, because the contract is void

Key Takeaway
In a fasid masaqah, ownership of trees remains with landowner; planter gets plant value and ujr al-mithl due to impossibility of returning plants.

The Ruling on Forgetful Omission of Tasmiyah during Slaughter
Responding to Maliki and Shafi'i arguments on forgetfulness in tasmiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on forgetful omission of tasmiyah during slaughter, identify the proofs from the passage, and contrast the Maliki and Shafi'i positions.

Core Idea
Forgetfulness excuses the omission of tasmiyah — meat remains halal because Shariah removes hardship.

Forgetting to say Bismillah while slaughtering an animal is common. The Hanafi school uniquely holds that such forgetfulness does not render the meat haram, based on the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj) and implicit consensus of the Companions. This passage responds to the arguments of Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, who disagree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What is the exact legal question? The passage deals with whether forgetting to say tasmiyah (Bismillah) during slaughter makes the meat haram.
The dispute is about the effect of forgetfulness, not the requirement itself.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
The Hanafis say the meat is halal. Their basis is that requiring tasmiyah even when forgotten would cause excessive hardship, which the Shariah aims to remove. Also, if the apparent meaning of the Quran were against forgetfulness, the Companions would have settled the dispute.
The principle of raf' al-haraj is key.
3
Analyze the Maliki argument and Hanafi response
Imam Malik argues the Quran and Sunnah do not distinguish between intentional and forgetful, so both make the meat haram. The Hanafis respond that this interpretation leads to hardship and that the Companions' ongoing dispute proves the ayah does not address forgetfulness.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i argument and Hanafi response
Imam Shafi'i analogizes that tawhid (the religion of monotheism) substitutes for tasmiyah in forgetfulness, so it should also substitute intentionally. The Hanafis distinguish: the forgetful person has an excuse, the intentional does not. The hadith cited is specific to forgetfulness.
The qiyas fails because of the difference in excuse.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: Hanafis permit the meat; Malikis and Shafi'is prohibit it. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view, supported by the global Hanafi tradition.
In fatwa, forgetfulness excuses tasmiyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ آپ نے جو آیت اور حدیث پیش کی ہے اس کا ظاہر بتاتا ہے کہ اگر تسمیہ نہ کہا جائے خواہ عمداً یا نسیاناً تو ذبیحہ حرام ہے کھایا نہیں جائے گا کیوں کہ ان میں عمد ونسیان کی کوئی تخصیص بیان نہیں کی گئی ہے ہم نے کہا اگر نسیان کے عذر کو عذر شمار نہ کیا جائے تو حرج کثیر لازم آئے گا حالانکہ شریعت حرج کو دور کرتی ہے اور انسان بھولتا بہت ہے تو پھر عظیم نقصان لازم آئے گا جیسا کہ ظاہر ہے۔ نیز اگر آیت کے ظاہری معنی مراد ہوتے تو صحابہ میں سے جو حضرات متروک التسمیہ ناسیاً کی حرمت کے قائل تھے وہ دوسرے حضرات پر اس آیت سے حجت پکڑتے۔ اور چونکہ یہ نص قطعی ہے دوسرا اس سے انکار نہیں کر سکتا تھا اور تسلیم کرتا اور جھگڑا صحابہ کے دور میں ختم ہو گیا ہوتا۔ معلوم ہوا کہ آیت سے ظاہری معنی مراد نہیں ہے۔
امام شافعی کے استدلال کا جواب
والاقامة في حق الناس وهو معذور لا يدل عليها في حق العامد ولا عذر وما رواه محمول على حالة النسيان۔ ترجمہ: اور رکھ دینا (ملت کو تسمیہ کی جگہ) ناسی کے حق میں حالانکہ وہ معذور ہے، دلالت نہیں کرتا اقامت میں عامد کے حق میں حالانکہ کوئی عذر نہیں ہے، اور جس کو شافعی نے روایت کیا ہے وہ نسیان کی حالت پر محمول ہے۔
تشریح: امام شافعی نے فرمایا تھا کہ جیسے نسیان کی صورت میں ملت توحید تسمیہ کے قائم مقام ہوگئی ہے ایسے ہی عمد کی صورت میں ملت توحید تسمیہ کے قائم مقام ہو جائے گی۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ناسی تو معذور ہے اور عامد معذور نہیں ہے اور اقامت مذکورہ عذر کی وجہ سے ہوئی تھی تو جہاں عذر نہیں وہاں نیابت بھی نہ ہوگی، اور امام شافعی نے جو دلیل ذکر کی تھی یعنی احادیث وہ نسیان کی حالت پر محمول ہے، کیوں؟ اجماع کی دلیل۔
Explanation: Imam Malik says that the apparent meaning of the verse and hadith you presented indicates that if tasmiyah is not said, whether intentionally or forgetfully, the slaughtered animal is forbidden and cannot be eaten, because no distinction between intentional and forgetful is mentioned in them. We said: If forgetfulness is not considered an excuse, great hardship would follow, whereas the Shariah removes hardship, and man forgets much; then great harm would necessarily follow, as is apparent. Also, if the apparent meaning of the verse were intended, then among the Companions those who held the prohibition of one who forgetfully omits tasmiyah would have argued against others with this verse, and since it is a decisive text, the other could not deny it and would accept, and the dispute would have ended in the era of the Companions. It is understood that the apparent meaning of the verse is not intended. Response to Imam Shafi'i's argument: 'And the substitution (of the religion) for the forgetful person, who is excused, does not indicate it for the intentional person with no excuse, and what he narrated is applied to the case of forgetfulness.' Translation: And placing the religion in place of tasmiyah for the forgetful, while he is excused, does not indicate this for the intentional, while there is no excuse. And what Shafi'i narrated is applied to the state of forgetfulness. Explanation: Imam Shafi'i had said that just as in the case of forgetfulness the religion of tawhid has substituted for tasmiyah, so too in the case of intention the religion of tawhid would substitute for tasmiyah. The response to this is that the forgetful is excused while the intentional is not, and the aforementioned substitution occurred due to the excuse; so where there is no excuse, there will be no substitution. And the proof that Imam Shafi'i mentioned, i.e., the hadith, is applied to the state of forgetfulness. Why? The evidence of consensus.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage presents two inter-madhhab disputes regarding the ruling on forgetting tasmiyah during slaughter. First, Imam Malik argues that since the Quranic and hadith texts mention no distinction between intentional and forgetful omission, the meat is haram in both cases. The Hanafi response is that this interpretation would cause excessive hardship, which the Shariah seeks to remove. Furthermore, if the apparent meaning were correct, the Companions who held this view would have settled the dispute decisively, but the disagreement persisted, indicating the ayah does not mean what the Malikis claim. Second, Imam Shafi'i analogizes that just as the religion of tawhid substitutes for tasmiyah in forgetfulness, it should also substitute intentionally. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the forgetful person has an excuse; the intentional does not. The hadith cited by Shafi'i is interpreted to apply only to forgetfulness. The Hanafi position is that forgetting tasmiyah does not prohibit the meat; this is the relied-upon view, supported by the principle of removal of hardship and implicit consensus of the Companions.

Key Terms
تسمیہ (tasmiyah): The act of saying 'Bismillah' (In the name of Allah) at the time of slaughter.
نسیان (nisyan): Forgetfulness, an excuse that exempts one from the requirement of tasmiyah.
حرج (haraj): Hardship or difficulty that the Shariah aims to remove, used here as a basis for the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, why is meat from an animal slaughtered without tasmiyah due to forgetfulness considered halal?
A) Because the Quranic verse specifically exempts forgetfulness.
B) Because the Shariah removes hardship and the Companions did not settle the dispute.
C) Because the animal was not intended for consumption.
D) Because the tasmiyah can be said after slaughter.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, forgetting tasmiyah during slaughter does not render the meat haram, due to the removal of hardship and implicit consensus of the Companions.

Tasmiyah Placement: Voluntary Slaughter vs. Hunting
Ruling on tasmiyah placement with rational proof and furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for tasmiyah placement in voluntary slaughter and hunting, and apply it to the five subsidiary cases given.

Core Idea
Tasmiyah is placed where the person has power: on the animal in slaughter, on the tool in hunting.

This passage explains a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: where exactly the tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) must be recited during slaughter and hunting. The ruling is based on the principle that obligation is according to ability (التكليف بقدر الوسع). In voluntary slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari), the person has direct control over the animal, so tasmiyah is said on the animal. In hunting (dhabh idtirari), the person only controls the release of the tool, so tasmiyah is on the arrow, dog, or falcon. The text then derives five furu' cases that test this principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of slaughter
Recognize that voluntary slaughter (of domestic animals) and involuntary slaughter (hunting) have different conditions because of differing levels of control.
Voluntary = full control; involuntary = only control over the tool.
2
Understand the ability principle
The central proof: 'Man is obligated according to his capacity.' Since tasmiyah is required at an action one can perform, it must be placed where the person has power: on the animal in slaughter, on the tool in hunting.
This is a rational (aqli) proof based on fairness.
3
Apply to voluntary slaughter cases
In voluntary slaughter, tasmiyah is on the animal. If tasmiyah is said on one animal but another is slaughtered, it is invalid because the tasmiyah was not on the slaughtered animal.
Case 1: misidentification invalidates. Case 4: changing the knife does not affect because the tool is not the locus.
4
Apply to hunting cases
In hunting, tasmiyah is on the tool. If the tool hits unintended game, it is still lawful because the tasmiyah was on the tool. But if a different tool is used without tasmiyah, it is unlawful.
Cases 2,3,5 confirm the rule.
5
Extract the general rule
Summarize: The locus of tasmiyah is determined by the action the person can perform at the moment of slaughter or release.
This rule distinguishes Hanafi position from other schools.

ثم التسمية في ذكاة الاختيار تشترط عند الذبح وهو على المذبوح وفي الصيد تشترط عند الإرسال والرمي وهو على الآلة لأن المقدور له في الأول الذبح وفي الثاني الرمي والإرسال دون الإصابة فيشترط عند فعل يقدر عليه حتى إذا أضجع شاة وسمى فذبح غيرها بتلك التسمية لا يجوز ولو رمى إلى صيد وسمى وأصاب غيره حل وكذا في الإرسال ولو أضجع شاة وسمى ثم رمى بالشفرة وذبح بأخرى أكل ولو سمى على سهم ثم رمى بغيره صيدا لا يؤكل.
تشریح: ذکاۃ کی دو قسمیں اختیاری اور اضطراری ماقبل میں گزر چکی ہیں اور یہ بھی مسلم ہے کہ انسان بقدر وسعت مکلف ہوتا ہے۔ تو اب فرماتے ہیں کہ ذکاۃ اختیاری میں تسمیہ ذبح کے وقت کہا جائے گا اور کہاں محل تسمیہ مذبوح ہے۔ اور ذکاۃ اضطراری میں تیر پھینکنے کے وقت یا کتا اور باز چھوڑتے وقت تسمیہ کہا جائے گا یعنی یہاں محل تسمیہ آلہ ہے نہ کہ مذبوح ہے اور یہی قدرت کا مقتضاء ہے کیونکہ پہلی صورت میں اس کو ذبح پر قدرت ہے۔ اور دوسری صورت میں اس کو مذبوح پر قدرت نہیں یعنی شکار پر قدرت نہیں صرف تیر پھینکنے اور کتے اور باز کے چھوڑنے پر قدرت ہے نہ کہ شکار کے پکڑنے پر۔ جب اصول یہ مقرر ہوا کہ اول میں محل تسمیہ مذبوح ہے اور ثانی میں آلہ ہے تو پھر اس پر چند جزئیات متفرع ہوئی ہے۔
- بکری کو ذبح کے لئے لٹایا اور تسمیہ کہا پھر دوسری مرتبہ تسمیہ کے بغیر بجائے اس بکری کے دوسری بکری ذبح کر دی تو جائز نہیں کیوں کہ یہ ذکاۃ اختیاری ہے اور یہاں محل تسمیہ مذبوح ہے اور تسمیہ اس نے پہلی بکری پر پڑھا ہے نہ کہ دوسری پر۔
- کسی شکار پر تسمیہ کہہ کر تیر پھینکا اور وہ تیر بجائے اس شکار کے دوسرے کو لگا تو وہ حلال ہے کیوں کہ یہ ذکاۃ اضطراری ہے جس میں محل تسمیہ تیر ہے اور تیر پر اس نے تسمیہ کہا ہے لہذا جس کو بھی وہ لگے وہ حلال ہوگا۔
- کتے اور باز میں بھی یہی حکم ہوگا یعنی تسمیہ کہہ کر چھوڑا کسی شکار پر اور اس نے پکڑ لیا دوسرا شکار تو حلال ہے۔
- بکری ذبح کے لئے لٹائی اور تسمیہ کہا پھر ہاتھ میں جو چھری تھی اس کو پھینک دیا اور دوسری چھری سے ذبح کیا تو جائز ہے کیوں کہ محل تسمیہ مذبوح ہے اور مذبوح وہی ہے جس پر تسمیہ کہا ہے۔
- کسی تیر پر تسمیہ کہا پھر اس تیر کو رکھ لیا اور دوسرا تیر شکار کو مارا تو حلال نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ جس تیر سے مارا ہے اس پر تسمیہ نہیں کہا ہے۔
Then tasmiyah in voluntary slaughter is required at the time of slaughter, and it is upon the slaughtered animal. In hunting, it is required at the time of releasing and shooting, and it is upon the tool, because what is within his power in the first is the slaughter, and in the second is the shooting and releasing, not the hitting. So it is required at an action he has power over. Thus, if he laid down a sheep and said tasmiyah, and then slaughtered another with that tasmiyah, it is not permissible. If he shot an arrow at game and said tasmiyah and hit another, it is lawful. Similarly, in releasing. If he laid down a sheep and said tasmiyah, then threw the blade and slaughtered with another, it is eaten. If he said tasmiyah on an arrow, then shot another arrow at game, it is not eaten.
Explanation: The two types of slaughter, voluntary and involuntary, have passed previously, and it is also established that man is obligated according to his capacity. So now he says: In voluntary slaughter, tasmiyah is said at the time of slaughter, and the place of tasmiyah is the slaughtered animal. In involuntary slaughter, tasmiyah is said at the time of shooting the arrow or releasing the dog or falcon; i.e., here the place of tasmiyah is the tool, not the slaughtered animal, and this is required by ability because in the first case he has power over slaughter, and in the second he has no power over the game, only over shooting and releasing, not catching. When this principle is established—that in the first, the place of tasmiyah is the slaughtered animal, and in the second, the tool—then several subsidiary cases branch from it.
- He laid down a goat for slaughter and said tasmiyah, then without repeating tasmiyah he slaughtered another goat instead: not permissible, because this is voluntary slaughter and the place of tasmiyah is the slaughtered animal, and he said tasmiyah on the first, not the second.
- He shot an arrow at game while saying tasmiyah, and the arrow hit another game: it is lawful, because this is involuntary slaughter where the place of tasmiyah is the arrow, and he said tasmiyah on the arrow, so whatever it hits is lawful.
- Similarly for dog and falcon: if he released them with tasmiyah and they caught other game, it is lawful.
- He laid down a goat for slaughter and said tasmiyah, then threw the knife in his hand and slaughtered with another knife: it is permissible, because the place of tasmiyah is the slaughtered animal, and it is the same animal on which he said tasmiyah.
- He said tasmiyah on an arrow, then put that arrow away and shot another arrow at game: not lawful, because he did not say tasmiyah on the arrow he used.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with supporting reasoning on the requirement of tasmiyah (saying Bismillah) in two types of slaughter: voluntary (dhabh of domestic animals) and involuntary (hunting with arrows, dogs, falcons). The key principle is that tasmiyah must be said at the moment of the action one has control over. In voluntary slaughter, the person controls the act of cutting the throat, so tasmiyah is required at that moment and is placed on the animal being slaughtered. In hunting, the person controls only the release of the arrow or the release of the trained animal, not the hitting or catching; so tasmiyah is required at the point of release and is placed on the tool (arrow, dog, etc.). The passage then derives five subsidiary cases applying this principle: 1) If one says tasmiyah over one sheep but slaughters a different one, the meat is not halal because the tasmiyah was not on the slaughtered animal. 2) In hunting, if one aims at a specific game but the arrow hits another, the meat is still halal because the tasmiyah was on the arrow. 3) Same for trained dogs and falcons. 4) If one says tasmiyah over a sheep then uses a different knife, it is still halal because the tasmiyah is on the animal, not the tool. 5) If one says tasmiyah over an arrow but uses a different arrow, the meat is not halal because the tool used was not the one on which tasmiyah was said. These rulings are consistent with the Hanafi principle of ability and the distinction between voluntary and involuntary slaughter.

Key Terms
ذکاۃ اختیاری (dhabh ikhtiyari): Voluntary slaughter of a domestic animal that one has control over, such as sheep, goats, cows, etc.
ذکاۃ اضطراری (dhabh idtirari): Involuntary slaughter, such as hunting with arrows, dogs, or falcons, where the person does not have direct control over the death of the animal.
محل تسمیہ (mahall al-tasmiyah): The object or tool upon which the tasmiyah is recited; in voluntary slaughter it is the animal, in hunting it is the tool.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person says tasmiyah on one arrow, then shoots a different arrow at game, what is the ruling?
A) The game is halal because tasmiyah was said during the hunting process.
B) The game is halal because the intention was for that game.
C) The game is not halal because the arrow used did not have tasmiyah recited over it.
D) The game is not halal unless the hunt was successful.

Key Takeaway
Tasmiyah must be placed where the person has control: on the animal in voluntary slaughter, on the tool in hunting.

Mentioning Other Names Alongside Allah at Slaughter is Makruh
Stating the ruling on mentioning other names alongside Allah at slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mawsul and ma'tuf in tasmiyah at slaughter and state the Hanafi ruling for each.

Core Idea
Mentioning another name alongside Allah at slaughter is makruh but halal if mawsul; ma'tuf may be haram.

This lesson unpacks a specific ruling from Imam Muhammad about what one should say at the time of slaughter. The key is the grammatical connection between Allah's name and another name. The Hanafi school distinguishes between conjunctive (mawsul) and coordinated (ma'tuf) forms, which changes the ruling from merely makruh to possibly haram. Understanding this nuance clarifies when the meat remains permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is mentioning something other than Allah alongside Allah's name at slaughter. The ruling given in the text is makruh (disliked).
This ruling is specifically for when the names are connected conjunctively (mawsul).
2
Distinguish mawsul vs. ma'tuf
Mawsul means the names are directly attached without a coordinating conjunction (e.g., 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah'). Ma'tuf means a conjunction like 'wa' is used (e.g., 'Bismillah wa Muhammad Rasul Allah'). The text only discusses mawsul.
The grammatical distinction is crucial; ma'tuf could imply partnership and may lead to haram.
3
Understand why it is not haram
The slaughter is still performed for Allah; no actual partnership (shirk) is intended. The mere verbal conjunction in form does not change the object of the slaughter.
The meat remains halal; the prohibition is only for the resemblance to shirk.
4
Apply to the example given
The example 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah' is mawsul. According to the text, this is makruh but the animal is halal.
This example clarifies the scope of the ruling.
5
Recognize the scope and limitations
The passage notes three sub-issues but details only one (mawsul). The other forms (ma'tuf and others) may have different rulings, but they are not elaborated here.
For a complete fatwa, one would need to consult further sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويكره ان يذكر مع اسم الله تعالى شيئا غيره وان يقول عند الذبح اللهم تقبل من فلان وهذه ثلث مسائل إحداهن ان يذكر موصولاً لا معطوفا فيكره ولا تحرم الذبيحة وهو المراد بما قال ونظيره ان يقول بسم الله محمد رسول الله لان الشركة لم توجد فلم يكن الذبح واقعا له الا انه يكره لوجود القران صورة فيتصور بصورة المحرم.
ترجمہ: امام محمد نے فرمایا، اور مکروہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے نام کے ساتھ اس کے علاوہ کسی شئی کا ذکر کرے اور مکروہ ہے یہ کہ وہ ذبح کے وقت کہے اے اللہ فلاں کی جانب سے قبول فرمالے اور تین مسائل ہیں ان میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ وہ موصلاً ذکر کرے نہ کہ معطوف بنا کر پس یہ مکروہ ہے اور ذبیحہ حرام نہیں ہے اور امام محمد نے جو فرمایا ہے (متن میں) اس سے یہی مراد ہے اور اس کی نظیر ہے یہ کہ وہ کہے بسم اللہ محمد رسول اللہ (یعنی مکروہ ہے حرام نہیں ہے) اس لئے کہ شرکت نہیں پائی گئی تو ذبیح آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے لئے نہ ہوگا مگر یہ مکروہ ہے صورۃ قرآن (ملاپ) کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے تو یہ حرام کی صورت میں متشکل ہوگا۔
He said: It is makruh to mention anything other than Allah along with the name of Allah, and it is makruh that at the time of slaughter he says: O Allah accept from so-and-so. These are three issues: one of them is that he mentions it conjunctively (mawsulan) not coordinately (ma'tufan), so it is makruh and the slaughtered animal is not prohibited. This is what is intended by what he said. Its example is that he says: 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah' because no partnership has occurred, so the slaughter was not done for him (the Prophet), but it is makruh due to the occurrence of conjunction (quran) in form, so it appears in the form of the prohibited. Explanation: Imam Muhammad said: And it is makruh to mention anything other than Allah along with the name of Allah, and it is makruh that at the time of slaughter he says: O Allah accept from so-and-so. There are three issues: one of them is that he mentions it conjunctively, not with a coordinating conjunction. So this is makruh and the slaughtered animal is not haram. And what Imam Muhammad said (in the text) is intended. Its example is that he says: 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah' (i.e., it is makruh, not haram) because no partnership has occurred, so the slaughter is not done for him (the Prophet), but it is makruh due to the presence of conjunction (qiran) in form, so it takes the form of the prohibited.
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling explaining the Hanafi position on mentioning other names alongside Allah during slaughter. Imam Muhammad states that it is makruh (disliked) to do so, but the meat is not haram. The key distinction is how the names are connected: if they are joined in a conjunctive manner (mawsulan, without a coordinating conjunction like 'and'), it is merely makruh. The example given is saying 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah' instead of 'Bismillah wa Muhammad Rasul Allah'. In the former, there is no explicit partnership (shirk) because the names are not grammatically coordinated; the slaughter is still for Allah only. However, it is makruh because the form resembles what is prohibited (shirk). The text also mentions that saying 'O Allah accept from so-and-so' is makruh. Three sub-issues are indicated, but only one is detailed. The Hanafi school holds that as long as the slaughter is not directed to other than Allah, the meat remains halal, but such wording should be avoided due to its resemblance to shirk.

Key Terms
موصولاً (mawsulan): Mentioning another name directly connected without a coordinating conjunction, e.g., 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah' rather than 'Bismillah wa Muhammad Rasul Allah'.
معطوف (ma'tuf): Mentioning with a coordinating conjunction (like 'and'), which would imply partnership and could make the meat haram.
قرآن (qiran): Conjunction or joining of words in form; here it means bringing Allah's name and another name together in utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if someone says 'Bismillah Muhammad Rasul Allah' at the time of slaughter?
A) The meat is haram.
B) The meat is halal but it is makruh.
C) The slaughter is invalid and the meat is not eatable.
D) The tasmiyah is nullified and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
When mentioning another name alongside Allah at slaughter, the Hanafi school holds it is makruh but halal if the connection is conjunctive (mawsul) without a coordinating conjunction.

Cutting Three of Four Veins: Abu Hanifa vs. Abu Yusuf on Slaughter
Intra-Hanafi dispute on minimum cut for dhabh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum cut required for halal slaughter and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, including their proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Cutting any three of four neck structures suffices for halal slaughter in the Hanafi school.

Slaughter (dhabh) requires cutting specific structures in the neck. The Hanafi school agrees there are four: the windpipe (halqum), the esophagus (mari'), and the two jugular veins (wadaj). However, a well-known intra-madhhab dispute arises on the minimum number. Abu Hanifa holds that any three suffices based on the principle that the majority takes the place of the whole. Abu Yusuf insists that the windpipe and esophagus must both be cut because they serve distinct vital functions, while the two jugulars can substitute for each other. This lesson unpacks both arguments and identifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four structures
List the four structures that must be considered in dhabh: halqum (windpipe), mari' (esophagus), and the two wadaj (jugular veins). Understand their functions: windpipe carries breath, esophagus carries food/water, jugulars carry blood.
The text notes a terminological confusion but states the ruling does not depend on correct naming.
2
Understand Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that the windpipe and esophagus cannot substitute for each other because one is for breath and the other for food; both are necessary for life. However, the two jugulars both carry blood, so one can substitute for the other. Therefore, he requires at least three cuts: the windpipe, the esophagus, and at least one jugular.
This view is considered ahwat (more precautionary).
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa invokes the principle 'al-akthar bi manzilat al-kull' (the majority takes the place of the whole). Cutting any three of the four constitutes the majority. The purpose is to spill blood and hasten death; cutting three achieves this while minimizing the animal's suffering. Additionally, the animal cannot survive after cutting the breath or food passage, and blood flows from one jugular.
This principle is applied in other areas, e.g., wiping part of the head in wudu.
4
Note the tarjih and practical difference
The commentator states that Abu Yusuf's view is more precautionary, but the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's: any three suffices. The practical difference arises when the cut includes both jugulars and the esophagus but NOT the windpipe: Abu Hanifa allows it (three structures cut), Abu Yusuf does not (because the windpipe is missing).
This thamarah al-khilaf affects whether the meat is considered halal in such a scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بي يوسف ان المقصود من قطع الودجين إنها والدم فينوب احدهما عن الاخراذ كل واحد منهما مجرى الدم اما الحلقوم يخالف المرى فانه مجرى العلف والماء والمرى مجرى النفس فلا بد من قطعهما

ترجمہ اور ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مقصود دونوں و د جوں کو کاٹنے سے خون بہانا ہے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک دوسرے کی نیابت کرے گی اس لئے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے خون جاری ہونے کی جگہ ہے بہر حال حلقوم نرخرہ کے مخالف ہے اس لئے کہ حلقوم گھاس اور پانی کی نالی ہے اور نرخرہ سانس کی نالی ہے تو ان دونوں کا کا مناضروری ہے۔

تشریح یہ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل ہے جس کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ حلقوم اور نرخرہ ایک دوسرے کی نیابت نہ کر سکے گا کیوں کہ ان میں سے ایک کھانا اور پانی کی نالی ہے اور ایک سانس کی۔
مگر دونوں و رج میں خون ہے تو اگر ایک پر اکتفا کر لیا جائے تو جائز ہے تو کیوں کہ خون اب بھی نکل جائے گا بس اتنی سی بات ہے کہ کچھ دیر سے نکل جائے گا اور دونوں کو کاٹنے کی صورت میں جلدی نکل جاتا۔
تنبیہ یہاں حلقوم گھاس اور پانی کی نالی کہا ہے اور مرئی کو سانس کی حالانکہ مسئلہ اس کے برعکس ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل

ولابي حنيفة ان الاكثر يقوم مقام الكل في كثير من الاحكام واى ثلث قطعها فقد قطع الاكثر منها وما هو المقصود يحصل بها وهو إنها الدم المسفوح والتوجيه فى إخراج الروح لانه لا يحى بعد قطع مجرى النفس والطعام ويخرج الدم بقطع احد الودجين فيكتفى تحرزا عن زيادة التعذيب بخلاف ما اذا قطع النصف لان الاكثر باق فكانه لم يقطع شيئا احتياطا لجانب الحرمة .

ترجمہ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بہت سے احکام میں اکثر کل کے قائم مقام ہوتا ہے اور جون سی تین کو اس نے کاٹ دیا تو اس نے چار میں سے اکثر کو کاٹ دیا اور جو مقصود ہے وہ تین کے کاٹنے سے حاصل ہو جائے گا اور وہ (مقصود ) دم مسفوح کو نکالنا اور جان کے نکالتے میں جلدی کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ جانور زندہ نہیں رہے گا سانس کھانے کی نالی کٹنے کے بعد اور دونوں دوج میں سے ایک کے کٹنے سے خون نکل جائے گا تو اس پر اکتفا کر لیا جائے گا زیادہ عذاب دینے سے بچنے کے لئے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ اس نے نصف کو کا نا ہو ( یعنی دوکو ) اس لئے کہ اکثر باقی ہیں تو گویا کہ اس نے کچھ نہیں کاٹا ہے حرمت کی جانب کی وجہ سے احتیاط کے طور پر۔ تشریح یہ امام صاحب کی دلیل ہے کہ بہت سے احکام میں اکثر کو کل کے قائم قائم مقام کر دیا جاتا ہے جیسے مسح راس میں ، اور نماز میں بستر عورت میں۔
تو اسی طرح یہاں بھی اکثر کوکل قائم مقام کر دیا جائے گا اور لا على التعيين جونی تین رگوں کو کاٹ دیا گیا تو اکثر کٹ گئیں اور

كتاب الذبائح
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
مقصود خون نکالنا ہے اور یہ ہے کہ روح جلدی نکل جائے اور یہ مقصد حاصل ہے کیوں کہ جب گھاس یا سانس کی نالی کٹ گئی تو اب جانور زندہ نہیں رہے گا اور دونوں و رج میں سے جون سی کٹ گئی تو خون سارا نکل جائے گا تو تین پر اکتفا جائز ہے تا کہ جانور کو زیادہ
تکلیف نہ ہو سکے۔
ہاں اگر چار میں سے دور گئیں کائیں تو اب ذبیحہ حلال نہ ہوگا کیوں کہ اکثر کو نہیں کا نا تو گویا اس نے کچھ نہیں کاٹا۔
سوال آدھی رگیں کاٹ چکا ہے تو کچھ نہ کاٹنے کا کیا مطلب؟ جواب یہاں دو پہلو جمع ہو گئے ایک حلت کا اور ایک حرمت کا، اور حرمت کے پہلو کوترجیح ہوئی ہے اس وجہ سے حرمت کے پہلو کو ترجیح دیتے ہوئے کہا گیا ہے کہ کچھ نہیں کا ٹا۔
تنبیہ امام ابو یوسف کا قول احوط معلوم ہوتا ہے کیوں کہ روح اور خون نکالنا ہی مقصود نہیں یہاں تک کہ بکری کے دو ٹکڑے کرنے سے بھی یہ مقصود حاصل ہوسکتا تھا بلکہ ذکاۃ شرعی مقصود ہے اور وہ اوراج ہیں اور اوراج میان بر بناء تغلیب چاروں داخل ہیں (كما صرح في الدر المختار ) تو بہتر تو یہ ہے کہ چاروں کو کاٹا جائے لیکن اگر تین پر اکتفا ہو حلقوم اور مرئی میں مخالفت کی وجہ سے ان کو الگ الگ اعتبار کیا جائے گا اور ود جان میں ایک دوسری کی نیابت کر سکتی ہے اور امام صاحب نے جو یہ کل یہ ارشاد فرمایا کہ اکثر کے لئے کل کا حکم ہے تو یہ کوئی قاعدہ کلیہ نہیں ورنہ سورہ فاتحہ کی سات آیتوں میں سے پانچ پر اکتفا جائز ہونا چاہیئے ۔ حالانکہ ہوا ایسا کرنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم آتا ہے بہر حال جہاں دلیل نہ ہو وہاں اکثر کو کل کے قائم مقام نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
And the evidence of Abu Yusuf is that the purpose of cutting the two jugular veins is the flowing of blood, so one of them substitutes for the other because each of them is a channel for blood. As for the windpipe (halqum), it differs from the esophagus (mari') because the windpipe is the passage for grass and water, and the esophagus is the passage for breath. So it is necessary to cut both. ... And the evidence of Abu Hanifa is that the majority takes the place of the whole in many rulings. Whichever three he cuts, he has cut the majority, and the intended purpose is achieved, which is the flowing of poured-out blood and hastening the exit of the soul. Because the animal cannot live after cutting the passages of breath and food, and blood flows by cutting one of the two jugulars. So it is sufficient to avoid additional torture, unlike if he cuts half (i.e., two), because the majority remains, so it is as if he cut nothing, as a precaution on the side of prohibition.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the minimum number of structures that must be cut for a valid slaughter (dhabh). The four structures are: the windpipe (halqum), the esophagus (mari'), and the two jugular veins (wadaj). Abu Yusuf argues that the windpipe and esophagus cannot substitute for each other because they serve different functions (food vs. breath), so both must be cut. However, the two jugular veins can substitute for each other since both carry blood. Thus, the minimum for him is three: both the windpipe and esophagus plus at least one jugular vein. Abu Hanifa, on the other hand, argues that cutting any three of the four suffices because the majority takes the place of the whole in many Islamic rulings (e.g., wiping part of the head in wudu). The purpose is to spill blood and hasten death; cutting three achieves this while avoiding prolonged suffering. The commentary notes a clarification about the names: here the text refers to halqum as the food passage and mari' as the breath passage, but the actual assignment is the opposite. A question arises: if half (two) are cut, why is it as if nothing is cut? The answer: because two out of four creates equal probability of permissibility and prohibition, and the prohibition side is given preference (ihtiyat). The note concludes that Abu Yusuf's view is more precautionary (ahwat), but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, allowing any three.

Key Terms
حلقوم (halqum): The windpipe; the passage for breath.
مری (mari'): The esophagus; the passage for food and drink.
ودج (wadaj): One of the two jugular veins on the sides of the neck.
أكثر (akthar): Majority; here meaning three out of four structures.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum number of structures that must be cut for a valid slaughter?
A) All four structures: windpipe, esophagus, and both jugulars.
B) Any three of the four structures.
C) At least the windpipe and one jugular vein.
D) Both the windpipe and esophagus.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi dhabh, cutting any three of the four specific structures (windpipe, esophagus, and two jugulars) renders the meat halal, based on Abu Hanifa's principle that the majority takes the place of the whole.

Slaughter with Detached Nails, Teeth, Horns: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on using detached nails, teeth, or horns for slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on slaughter with detached nails, teeth, or horns, and explain the condition of detachment as the key differentiating factor.

Core Idea
Detached nails/teeth/horns are valid tools for slaughter; the hadith prohibition applies only when attached.

This passage tackles a classic inter-madhhab dispute: is it permissible to slaughter an animal using a nail, tooth, or horn that has been detached from the body? The Hanafi school allows it with dislike, while Imam al-Shafi'i considers the animal carrion. The debate hinges on interpreting the Prophet's hadith and the legal analogy. Let's examine the proofs and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from the matn: slaughter with detached nail, tooth, or horn is permissible (ja'iz) but makruh tanzihi. The meat is halal.
The condition 'detached' (munzai') is critical – attached parts invalidate the slaughter.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that such slaughter renders the animal carrion (maytah). His ruling is based on two proofs.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
First proof: the hadith '...except for nail and tooth, for they are the knives of the Abyssinians.' Second proof: qiyas – slaughter with detached parts is an illegitimate action, analogous to using attached parts.
The hadith is a dalil naqli, the qiyas is a rational extension.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith as referring to attached nails/teeth, since Abyssinians used their own attached nails. When detached, the prohibition does not apply; the object becomes a permissible sharp tool. The karahah is due to resemblance to a disliked practice, not prohibition.
The key is the distinction between attached and detached – the 'illa (effective cause) of prohibition is attachment.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If someone slaughters with a detached nail, Hanafis consider the meat halal (though makruh); Shafi'is consider it carrion (haram).
This affects actual consumption and liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ويجوز الذبح بالظفر والسن والقرن اذا كان منزوعا حتى لا يكون بأ كله باس الا انه يكره هذا الذبح وقال الشافعى المذبوح ميتة لقوله عليه السلام كل ما انهر الدم وافرى الأوداج ماخلا الظفر والسن فانها مدى الحبشة ولانه فعل غير مشروع فلا يكون ذكاة كما اذا ذبح بغير المنزوع

ترجمہ محمد نے فرمایا اور جائز ہے ذبح کرنا ناخن اور دانت اور سینگ سے جب کہ یہ جدا ہوں یہاں تک اس کے کھانے میں کچھ حرج نہیں ہے مگر یہ ذبح مکروہ ہے اور شافعی نے فرمایا کہ مذبوح مردار ہے نبی کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ ان جانوروں کو کھاؤ جن کا خون نکال دیا گیا ہو اور اوراج کاٹ دی گئی ہوں علاوہ ناخن اور دانت کے اس لئے کہ یہ حبشیوں کی چھری ہے اور اس لئے کہ یہ ( ناخن وغیرہ سے ذبح) فعل غیر مشروع ہے تو یہ ذکاۃ نہ ہوگی جیسا کہ غیر منزوع سے ذبح کیا ہو۔ تشریح جانور کو کن چیزوں سے ذبح کرنا جائز ہے اور کن سے نہیں یہاں ان کو بیان کیا جائے گا اگر جانور کا سینگ جانور سے جدا ہواور اوراج کو کاٹ سکتے ہوں تو پھر ان سے ذیح جائز ہوگا اور وہ ذبیہ حلال ہوگا اور اس کا کھانا مباح ہوگا یہ ہمارا مذ ہب ہے۔ اور امام شافعی ایسے ند بوح کو مر دار قرار دیتے ہیں جس پر امام شافعی نے دو دلیلیں بیان کی ہیں اول حدیث اور دوسری دلیل عقلی ۔ حدیث تو ظاہر ہے اور دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ ناخن وغیرہ سے ذبح کرنا غیر مشروع ہے تو پھر یہ طریقہ ذکاۃ نہ بنے گا جیسے جب کہ ناخن
He (Muhammad) said: It is permissible to slaughter with a nail, tooth, or horn when they are detached, so that there is no harm in eating it, except that this slaughter is disliked (makruh). Imam al-Shafi'i said: The slaughtered animal is carrion, because of the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Eat from what causes blood to flow and cuts the jugular veins, except for nail and tooth, for they are the knives of the Abyssinians.' And because it is an illegitimate action, so it is not a valid slaughter (dhabh), just as if one slaughtered with a non-detached (part).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the permissibility of using detached nails, teeth, or horns as instruments for slaughter. The Hanafi position, as stated by Imam Muhammad (the narrator of the matn), is that such slaughter is permissible (ja'iz) and the meat is halal, but it is makruh tanzihi (disliked). The condition is that the instrument must be detached (munzai') from the animal's body, because if attached, it would be like slaughtering with a part of the animal's own body, which is not valid. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and considers the slaughtered animal carrion (maytah). He bases his view on the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ which excludes nails and teeth because they are the 'knives of the Abyssinians' (a practice of non-Muslims). Additionally, Shafi'i argues that slaughter with such instruments is an illegitimate (ghayr mashru') act and therefore cannot constitute valid dhabh, analogous to slaughtering with an attached bone or horn. The Hanafi response, implied in the text, is that the hadith refers to attached nails and teeth, not detached ones. When detached, they become sharp tools like iron blades. The dislike (karahah) is due to resemblance to the practice of the Abyssinians or because it is not the usual method. The commentary also notes that the Shafi'i view is based on two proofs: the hadith and rational analogy (qiyas).

Key Terms
ظفر (zufr): Nail; the hard covering at the tip of fingers/toes, but here referring to animal nail or claw.
سن (sinn): Tooth; a bone-like structure used for cutting; if detached, considered a tool.
قرن (qarn): Horn; a bony outgrowth on the head of animals; permissible if detached.
منزوع (munzai'): Detached; separated from the animal, not attached.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering an animal with a detached tooth?
A) It is permissible and the meat is halal, but it is makruh.
B) It is forbidden and the animal becomes carrion.
C) It is permissible without any dislike.
D) It is valid only if the tooth is from a pig.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits slaughter with detached nails, teeth, or horns as valid tools, but the Shafi'i school prohibits it, basing their view on the same hadith with a different interpretation.

Ruling on Cutting the Spinal Cord During Slaughter
Ruling on reaching the spinal cord or beheading before death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nukha' and identify which actions are disliked without affecting the lawfulness of the meat.

Core Idea
Extra pain during slaughter is disliked but does not make the meat haram.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: actions that cause unnecessary pain to the animal during slaughter are disliked (makruh), but they do not invalidate the slaughter or render the meat unlawful. The source passage from Al-Hidayah explains the basis for this ruling, grounded in a hadith and a general principle that only corruption of the animal's soul (through improper cutting) affects permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting or reaching the spinal cord (al-nukha') during slaughter. The Hanafi ruling is that this act is makruh tanzih (slightly disliked), but the meat remains halal.
Also includes cutting the head before the animal stops moving, and other painful acts.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith in which the Prophet ﷺ forbade reaching the spinal cord in a goat when slaughtered. This prohibition indicates dislike.
The hadith is cited without chain but is accepted in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition is not absolute because the essence of slaughter (cutting the jugular veins) is still valid. The dislike arises from the extra pain (ziyadat al-alam), which is an extra meaning that does not corrupt the dhabihah.
Hanafi principle: Only factors that corrupt the animal's soul (e.g., cutting the spinal cord alone) make meat haram.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Malik) may consider such acts haram or affecting permissibility. The Hanafi view is that the meat is lawful.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Apply the general principle
The passage states: 'Every action that is not needed in slaughter and causes pain is disliked.' This principle governs five specific disliked acts listed.
The five acts: cutting spinal cord, pulling head, separating neck before cooling, dragging by leg, skinning before cooling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ النخع والسلخ ان الكراهة لمعنى زائد وهو زيادة الالم قبل الذبح او بعده فلا يوجب التحريم فلهذا قال تؤكل ذبيحته.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا کہ اور جس نے چھری کو نخاع تک پہنچایا یا سرکاٹ دیا تو یہ اس کے لئے مکروہ ہے اور اس کا ذبیحہ کھایا جائے گا اور بعض نسخوں میں بلغ کے بجائے قطع ہے اور نخاع گردن کی ہڈی میں ایک سفید رگ ہے بہر حال کراہت پس اس وجہ سے ہے کہ نبی علیہ السلام سے مروی ہے کہ آپ نے بکری کے اندر نخاع تک پہنچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے جب کہ وہ ذبح کی جائے اور اس کی تفسیر وہی ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اور کہا گیا کہ مخاع کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ مذبوح کا سر کھینچا جائے یہاں تک کہ اس کا مذبح ظاہر ہو جائے اور کہا گیا کہ (اس کی تفسیر یہ ہے کہ ) اس کی گردن الگ کی جائے اس سے پہلے کہ وہ اضطراب سے سکون میں ہو اور یہ تمام باتیں مکروہ ہیں اور یہ اس لئے کہ ان تمام باتوں میں سر کاٹنے میں حیوان کو بلا فائدہ کے زیادہ تکلیف دینا ہے اور یہ منہی عنہ ہے ( یعنی اس سے منع کر دیا گیا ہے ) اور اصول کلی یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ کام جس میں زیادہ تکلیف دینا ہو جس کی جانب ذکاۃ میں کوئی حاجت نہیں ہے تو وہ مکروہ ہے اور مکروہ ہے یہ کہ اس بکری کو جس کے ذبح کا ارادہ کرتا ہے اس کے پیر سے مذبح کی جانب ( جس جگہ ذبح کیا جائے ) اور ( مکروہ ہے ) یہ کہ بکری کا سرا لگ کیا جائے اس سے پہلے کہ وہ ٹھنڈی ہو یعنی اضطراب سے سکون میں آئے اور اس کے بعد کوئی تکلیف نہیں ہے تو سرا الگ کرنا اور کھال اتارنا کچھ مکروہ نہ ہوگا مگر تحقیق کہ کراہت ایک زائد معنی کی وجہ سے ہے اور وہ ذبح سے پہلے یا ذبح کے بعد تکلیف کی زیادتی ہے تو یہ تحریم کو واجب نہیں کرے گا اسی وجہ سے قدوری نے فرمایا تو کل ذبيحته ( یعنی اس کا کھایا جائے گا )۔ تشریح ہر وہ کام جس کی ذبح میں ضرورت نہ ہو اور اس سے مذبوح کو تکلیف پہنچے وہ مکروہ ہے لیکن ذبیحہ حلال ہوگا چونکہ یہاں خرابی نفس ذیح میں نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک زائد معنی کی وجہ سے خرابی آئی ہے اور وہ بلا وجہ ایلام ہے تو یہ ذبیحہ کی حرمت کا ثابت ہیں کرے گا بلکہ ذبیحہ حلال ہے البتہ یہ فعل مکروہ ہے۔
پھر وہ کیا افعال ہیں جو مکروہ ہیں :
- حرام مغز تک بوقت ذبح کا نا۔ - سر کو کھینچنا تا کہ مذبوح کا مذبح ظاہر ہو جائے۔ - ٹھنڈا ہونے سے پہلے گردن الگ کرنا۔ ۴- پاؤں پکڑ کر مدیح تک لے جانا۔ -۵- ٹھنڈا ہونے سے پہلے کھال اتارنا۔ اول ذکر کردہ تینوں کو نخاع کی تفسیر میں بیان کیا گیا ہے۔
Book of Slaughterings. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 13. Reaching the spinal cord and skinning: Dislike is due to an extra meaning, which is increasing pain before or after slaughter, so it does not necessitate prohibition, hence he said: His slaughtered animal is eaten. Translation: Quduri said: And whoever made the knife reach the spinal cord or cut off the head, then it is disliked for him, and his slaughtered animal will be eaten. In some manuscripts, instead of 'reached' it is 'cut'. And al-nukha' is a white vein in the bone of the neck. In any case, the dislike is due to what is narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him, that he forbade reaching the spinal cord in a goat when it is slaughtered, and its interpretation is what we have mentioned. And it was said that the meaning of 'mukha'' is that the head of the slaughtered animal be pulled until its slaughter place becomes apparent. And it was said that its interpretation is that its neck be separated before it calms down from agitation. And all these things are disliked, because in all these things there is giving extra pain to the animal without benefit in cutting the head, and it is prohibited. And the general principle is that every action in which there is giving extra pain for which there is no need in slaughter, it is disliked. And it is disliked to drag the goat intended for slaughter by its leg towards the slaughter place, and it is disliked to cut off the head of the goat before it cools down, i.e., becomes calm from agitation. After that there is no pain, so separating the head and skinning will not be disliked at all. But indeed the dislike is due to an extra meaning, and that is the increase of pain before or after slaughter, so it will not necessitate prohibition. For this reason Quduri said: 'His slaughtered animal is eaten', i.e., it will be eaten. Explanation: Every action that is not needed in slaughter and causes pain to the slaughtered animal is disliked, but the slaughtered animal will be lawful, because here the corruption is not in the soul of the animal but due to an extra meaning, and that is pain without cause, so it will not establish the prohibition of the slaughtered animal; rather the slaughtered animal is lawful, but this action is disliked. Then what are the actions that are disliked: 1. Reaching the spinal cord at the time of slaughter. 2. Pulling the head so that the slaughter place becomes apparent. 3. Separating the neck before it cools. 4. Dragging by the leg to the slaughter place. 5. Skinning before it cools. The first three have been mentioned in the interpretation of al-nukha'.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh of Al-Hidayah explains the ruling on actions that cause extra pain during slaughter, specifically cutting the spinal cord (al-nukha') or beheading before the animal dies. The text follows Quduri's matn: such acts are makruh (disliked) but the meat remains halal. The proof is a hadith prohibiting reaching the spinal cord. The passage clarifies that dislike arises from an extra meaning (ziyadat al-alam) which does not affect the validity of the dhabihah itself. It then lists five disliked acts: (1) cutting the spinal cord, (2) pulling the head to expose the throat, (3) separating the neck before the animal stops moving, (4) dragging the animal by the leg, and (5) skinning before the body cools. The principle is that any unnecessary pain is makruh, but since the actual slaughter (cutting of the jugular veins) is valid, the meat is lawful. This is a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh: actions may be prohibited/makruh but do not necessarily render the slaughtered animal haram unless the soul is corrupted (like improper slaughter).

Key Terms
النخع (al-nukha'): Cutting or reaching the spinal cord during slaughter, specifically a white vein in the neck bone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person slaughters a goat by cutting through the spinal cord before the veins are fully cut. The goat dies. What is the ruling on the meat?
A) Haram, because the slaughter was invalid.
B) Halal but the act is disliked.
C) Halal and the act is recommended.
D) Makruh tahrimi, cannot be eaten.

Key Takeaway
Cutting the spinal cord or causing unnecessary pain during slaughter is disliked, but as long as the proper jugular cut is made, the meat remains halal.

Ruling on Slaughtering from the Back of the Neck
Ruling on slaughtering from the back and its effect on permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on slaughtering from the back of the neck and distinguish the two scenarios that determine permissibility.

Core Idea
Slaughter from the back is valid only if the animal lives until the veins are cut; otherwise it is carrion.

The proper method of Islamic slaughter (dhabh) requires cutting the throat in a specific manner. But what if someone cuts from the back of the neck? This lesson examines Quduri's ruling, which balances the validity of the act against the dislike of unnecessary pain. The ruling hinges on whether the animal remains alive until the jugular veins (awdāj) are cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the text and note that the ruling splits into two cases: (1) the animal lives until the veins are cut, (2) the animal dies before the veins are cut.
The key variable is the animal's vitality at the moment of vein cutting.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
In the first scenario, the meat is halal because death occurs by a valid slaughter act. In the second, it is haram because death occurs by an invalid means (the back cut alone).
The text explicitly states 'حل' and 'لم توكل'.
3
Note the ruling on the act itself
In both scenarios, the act of cutting from the back is makruh tanzih (disliked) because it inflicts extra pain without necessity.
The dislike applies regardless of the outcome.
4
Understand the qiyas (analogy)
The text compares this case to wounding the animal first and then cutting the veins: both involve unnecessary pain, but the slaughter is valid if the veins are cut while alive.
This analogy clarifies that the validity depends on the actual slaughter act, not the preceding wound.
5
Recognize the underlying principle
The core principle is that the act of slaughter (cutting the awdaj) must be performed on a living animal. The method of reaching the veins is secondary but disliked if painful.
This aligns with the Hanafi emphasis on the timing of the slaughter cuts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بکری کو گدی کے پیچھے سے ذبح کرنے کا حکم
قال وان ذبح الشاة من قفاها فبقيت حية حتى قطع العروق حل لتحقق الموت بما هو ذكاة ويكره لان فيه زيادة الالم من غير عاجة فصار كما اذا جرحها ثم قطع الأوداج وان ماتت قبل قطع العروق لم توكل

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر بکری کو ذبح کیا اس کی گردن سے پس وہ زندہ باقی رہی، یہاں تک کہ تمام رگیں کاٹی گئیں تو حلال ہے موت کے متحقق ہونے کی وجہ سے اس چیز سے جو کہ ذکاۃ ہے اور یہ مکروہ ہے اس وجہ سے کہ اس میں بغیر ضرورت کے زیادہ تکلیف دینا ہے پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جبکہ اس کو زخمی کیا پھر رگوں کو کا نا ہو اور اگر وہ رگوں کو کاٹنے سے پہلے مرگئی تو نہیں کھائی جائے گی موت کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اس چیز سے جو کہ بکری میں ذکاۃ نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر بکری کو گڈی کے پیچھے سے ذبح کیا تو اب یہ دیکھا جائے گا کہ ذبح کی رگوں کے کٹنے تک وہ زندہ ہے یا اس سے پہلے ہی مرگئی ۔ اول صورت میں وہ حلال ہے اور دوسری صورت میں حلال نہیں ہے البتہ بہر دو صورت یہ فعل مکروہ ہے اس لئے کہ یہ بلا ضرورت زیادہ تکلیف دینا ہے۔
Ruling on slaughtering a goat from the back of its neck.
He said: And if he slaughters a goat from its back (qafa), and it remains alive until the veins are cut, it is permissible (halal) due to the verification of death by what is slaughter (dhakāt), and it is disliked because in it there is extra pain without need, so it becomes as if he wounded it then cut the jugular veins. And if it dies before cutting the veins, it is not eaten due to the occurrence of death by what is not slaughter in it.
Translation: Quduri said: And if he slaughters a goat from its neck, then it remained alive until all the veins were cut, then it is halal due to the verification of death by that which is slaughter (dhakāt), and it is disliked because in it there is extra pain without need, so it becomes as if he wounded it then cut the veins. And if it died before cutting the veins, then it will not be eaten due to the occurrence of death by that which is not slaughter in the goat. Explanation: If a goat is slaughtered from the back of the neck, then it will be seen whether it remains alive until the veins of slaughter are cut or dies before. In the first case, it is halal, and in the second case, it is not halal. However, in both cases the action is disliked, because it is giving extra pain without need.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage presents Quduri's ruling on slaughtering an animal from the back of the neck (min qafā), rather than the proper throat area. The Hanafi position distinguishes two scenarios: (1) If the animal survives the initial wound and remains alive until the jugular veins (awdāj) are cut, then the slaughter is valid and the meat is halal—because death is achieved by a valid slaughter (dhakāt). (2) If the animal dies from the back wound before the veins are cut, then it is carrion (maytah) and not permissible—because death occurred by an invalid means. In both cases, the act of cutting from the back is makruh (disliked) because it inflicts unnecessary pain. The text analogizes this to a case where one wounds the animal and then later cuts the veins—similar ruling. This reinforces the general principle that unnecessarily painful methods are disliked but do not necessarily forbid the meat if the proper slaughter act (cutting the veins) is completed while the animal is alive.

Key Terms
ذبح من قفاها (dhabh min qafāhā): Slaughtering from the back of the neck, a disliked method.
الأوداج (al-awdāj): The jugular veins and carotid arteries on both sides of the neck, which must be cut in proper slaughter.
مايتة (maytah): Carrion; an animal that dies without proper Islamic slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person stabs a goat in the back of the neck; the goat dies immediately. What is the ruling?
A) Halal, because intention was slaughter.
B) Haram, because death occurred by invalid means.
C) Makruh but halal.
D) Halal after skinning.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of meat from back-of-neck slaughter depends on whether the animal is alive when the jugular veins are cut; the method itself is disliked but not prohibitive.

Optional vs. Emergency Slaughter: The Hanafi–Maliki Dispute on the Role of Inability vs. Rarity
Expansion of the rule on slaughter methods based on tameness/wildness, with a rational dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when emergency slaughter ('aqr) is allowed and evaluate the Maliki objection based on rarity.

Core Idea
Emergency slaughter is permissible when inability to perform optional slaughter is realized, regardless of rarity.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between tame and wild animals for the method of slaughter. A tame animal must be slaughtered by throat cutting (dhabh), while a wild animal can be killed by wounding ('aqr). But what if a tame animal becomes wild, or a wild animal becomes tame? The rule follows the current state of tameness or wildness, not the origin. Furthermore, if a domestic animal falls into a well and cannot be slaughtered normally, emergency slaughter is allowed. Imam Malik disagrees, arguing such situations are too rare to permit an alternative. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi response and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories and their default methods
First, note that slaughter (dhakāt) has two modes: optional (ikhtiyārī) by throat cutting (dhabh) and emergency (idtirārī) by wounding ('aqr). The default is: tame animals require dhabh; wild animals require 'aqr. The passage applies this rule regardless of origin: a wild animal that becomes tame shifts to dhabh, and a tame animal that becomes wild shifts to 'aqr.
This is the base rule established in previous sections.
2
Understand the principle: emergency slaughter is a substitute
Emergency slaughter is only resorted to when one is unable to perform optional slaughter. This principle is derived from the general rule that necessary permits what is normally forbidden (necessity overrides prohibition). Here, inability ('ajz) is the effective cause ('illa) that triggers the substitute.
The substitute ('aqr) is valid if inability is realized.
3
Apply to the case of a camel falling into a well
If a camel or other quadruped falls into a well and cannot be slaughtered by dhabh, then inability is realized. Therefore, emergency slaughter by wounding suffices. This is the Hanafi position.
The text explicitly mentions this scenario.
4
Analyze the Maliki objection
Imam Malik holds that emergency slaughter is not permissible in either case (tame becoming wild or domestic animal in well) because such situations are rare (nādir). He argues that rarities are not given legal consideration.
Malik's argument is based on frequency, not inability.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: the criterion is inability ('ajz), not rarity. Since inability has occurred, the substitute must be used. Moreover, Hanafis do not concede rarity—such incidents are common (ghālib). Even if rare, the principle of inability overrides; rarity alone does not negate the ruling.
This shows the Hanafi focus on the effective cause ('illa) rather than incidental frequency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن جانوروں میں ذبح اختیاری اور کن میں ذبح اضطراری ہوگی
قال وما استانس من الصيد فذكاته الذبح وما توحش من النعم فذكاته العقرو الجرح لان ذكاة الاضطرار انما يصار اليه عند العجز عن ذكاة الاختيار على ما مرو العجز متحقق في الوجه الثاني دون الاول ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جو شکار مانوس ہو گیا تو اس کی ذکاۃ ذبح ہے اور جو چوپاؤں میں سے وحشی ہو گیا تو اس کی ذکاۃ کو نچ کائنا اور زخمی کرنا ہے اس لئے کہ ذکاۃ اضطراری اس کی جانب رجوع کیا جاتا ہے ذکاۃ اختیاری سے عاجزی کے وقت اس تفصیل کے مطابق جو گذرگئی اور عاجزی متحقق ہے دوسری صورت میں نہ کہ پہلی میں۔
تشریح ماقبل میں بیان کیا جا چکا ہے کہ ذکاۃ کی دو قسمیں ہیں:
اختیاری
اضطراری
یہ دونوں کہاں کہاں مشروع ہیں یہ بھی معلوم ہو چکا ہے۔
اب یہ بتاتے ہیں کہ پالتو جانور ہے جیسے بھینس وغیرہ لیکن وہ بدک کر وحشی ہو گیا تو اب یہاں ذکاۃ اضطراری جائز ہے اور اگر وحشی جانور پالنے کی وجہ سے مانوس ہو گیا، تو اب یہاں ذکاۃ اختیاری سے کام لیا جائے گا۔
اونٹ یا کوئی اور چو پایہ کنویں میں گر جائے اور ذبح اختیاری سے عمر متحقق ہو جائے تو ذکاۃ اضطراری کافی ہے
وكذا ما تردى من النعم في بيرو وقع العجز عن ذكاة الاختيار لما بينا وقال مالك لا يحل بذكاة الاضطرار في الوجهين لان ذالك نادر ونحن نقول المعتبر العجز وقد تحقق فيصار الى البدل كيف وانا لا نسلم الندرة بل هو غالب
In which animals is optional slaughter and in which emergency slaughter?
He said: And what becomes tame from game, its slaughter (dhakāt) is dhabh (throat cutting), and what becomes wild from cattle, its slaughter is 'aqr (wounding) and injury, because emergency slaughter is only resorted to when unable to perform optional slaughter, according to what has passed. Inability is realized in the second case, not the first. Translation: Quduri said: And what becomes tame from game, its slaughter is dhabh, and what becomes wild from cattle, its slaughter is 'aqr and wounding, because emergency slaughter is resorted to at the time of inability to perform optional slaughter, according to the detail that has passed. Inability is realized in the second case, not the first.
Explanation: It has been previously stated that slaughter (dhakāt) has two types: optional and emergency. Where each is legislated has also been known. Now it is being stated: if a domestic animal, like a buffalo etc., becomes wild due to fright, then emergency slaughter is permissible. And if a wild animal becomes tame due to domestication, then optional slaughter will be used.
And likewise, if a camel or other quadruped falls into a well and inability to perform optional slaughter is realized, then emergency slaughter suffices.
And likewise, what falls from cattle into a well, and inability to perform optional slaughter occurs, due to what we have explained. Malik said: It is not permissible by emergency slaughter in both cases, because that is rare. And we say: What matters is inability, and it has occurred, so the substitute is resorted to. Moreover, we do not concede rarity; rather it is common.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage deals with the distinction between optional (ikhtiyārī) and emergency (idtirārī) slaughter methods. The general principle: tame animals (whether originally wild or domestic) should be slaughtered by dhabh (cutting the throat). Wild animals (whether originally domestic or wild) may be slaughtered by 'aqr (wounding/hunting). The text applies this to cases where a domestic animal becomes wild and a wild animal becomes tame. If a camel falls into a well and cannot be slaughtered normally, emergency slaughter (like stabbing) suffices. The passage includes a dispute with Imam Malik, who holds that emergency slaughter is not permissible in either case because the situation is rare. The Hanafi response: the criterion is inability (al-‘ajz), not rarity. Since inability exists, the substitute is resorted to. Moreover, Hanafis argue such falls are common, not rare. This shows the Hanafi method of focusing on the effective cause (illa) of inability rather than frequency.

Key Terms
ذكاة اضطراري (dhakāt idtirārī): Emergency slaughter, performed by wounding ('aqr) when unable to perform regular throat cutting.
العقر (al-'aqr): Wounding an animal to kill it, a valid method of slaughter in emergencies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The rarity of the situation
B) The inability to perform optional slaughter
C) The size of the animal
D) The type of wound inflicted

Key Takeaway
Emergency slaughter is valid when inability to perform optional slaughter is realized, regardless of rarity, because the effective cause is 'ajz, not nudra.

Nahr for Camels, Dhabh for Cows: The Recommended Method of Slaughter
States the recommended slaughter methods and the effect of violating them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended slaughter method for camels, cows, and goats, and explain why violating it is still permissible but disliked.

Core Idea
Opposing the sunnah in slaughter method does not make the meat haram; it remains halal but is disliked.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the Matn of al-Quduri on the recommended methods of slaughter for different animals. While the sunnah prescribes nahr for camels and dhabh for cows and goats, doing the opposite is still valid. Understanding the distinction between permissible (ja'iz) and disliked (makruh) is crucial to avoid overreacting to minor violations of sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rulings for Each Animal
State what is recommended (mustahabb) for camels (nahr) and for cows/goats (dhabh). Also note the ruling if the opposite method is used (ja'iz but makruh).
The passage explicitly mentions both rulings.
2
Recognize the Proof: Sunnah Mutawarithah
The recommendation is based on the continuously transmitted practice (sunnah mutawarithah). This is the primary dalil for the ruling.
The phrase 'al-sunnah al-mutawarithah' indicates a strong transmitted practice, though not mutawatir in the sense of necessity.
3
Understand the Wisdom (Hikmah)
The gathering of the main blood vessels in the recommended location (nahr for camels, dhabh for cows/goats) provides a practical wisdom that facilitates complete blood drainage. This supports the sunnah but is not the basis of the ruling.
This wisdom is mentioned in the text (li ijtimaa' al-'uruq).
4
Analyze the Nature of the Dislike (Karaha)
The karaha is due to opposing the sunnah but it is karaha tanzihiyyah (disliked but not prohibited). It does not affect permissibility or the meat's lawfulness because it is li ma'nan fi ghayrihi (for a reason external to the act itself).
The passage explicitly says 'la tamna' al-jawaz wa al-hill'.
5
Contrast with the Maliki Position
Imam Malik holds that using the opposite method makes the meat unlawful (la yahillu). The Hanafi response refutes this, insisting on the validity of the slaughter as long as the essential act is performed.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that Malik declares the meat haram, while Hanafis say it is halal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والمستحب في الابل النحر فان ذبحها جاز ويكره والمستحب في البقرو الغنم الذبح فان نحرهما جاز وبكره اما الاستحباب فيه لموافقة السنة المتوارثة ولا جتماع العروق فيها في المنحرو فيهما فى المذبح والكراهة لمخالفة السنة وهى لمعنى في غيره فلا تمنع الجواز والحل خلافا لما يقوله مالك انه لا يحل
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اونٹ میں نحر مستحب ہے پس اگر اس کو ذبح کیا تو جائز ہے اور مکروہ ہے اور مستحب گائے اور بکری میں ذبح ہے پس اگر ان دونوں کو نحر کیا تو جائز ہے اور مکروہ ہے بہر حال اس میں استحباب سنت متوارثہ کی موافقت کی وجہ سے ہے اور اونٹ میں رگوں کے اجتماع کی وجہ سے نحر میں اور گائے اور بکری میں مذبح میں اور کراہت سنت کی مخالفت کی وجہ سے ہے اور یہ کراہت ایسے معنی کی وجہ سے ہے جو ذبح کے غیر میں ہے تو یہ کراہت جواز اور حلت کو نہیں روکے گی بخلاف اس کے جو مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ حلال نہیں ہوگا۔
تشريح نجر اور ذبح کی تفصیل ماقبل میں گذر چکی ہے اب فرماتے ہیں کہ بکری ہو یا اونٹ ہو یا گائے ہر ایک میں ذبح اور نحر جائز ہے اور ذبیحہ حلال ہے مگر اونٹ میں نحر مستحب اور ذبح مکروہ ہے اور بکری اور گائے میں ذبح مستحب اور نحر مکروہ ہے وجہ استحباب یہ ہے کہ یہی سنتِ متوارثہ ہے۔
اور اونٹ میں تمام رگوں کا اجتماع نحر میں ہے اور گائے اور بکری میں مذبح میں ہے اور حسب سابق یہ کراہت حلت اور جواز کو نہیں روکے گی ۔
He said: The recommended (mustahabb) for camels is nahr (slaughter at the base of the neck). If one slaughters by dhabh (cutting the throat), it is permissible but disliked (makruh). The recommended for cows and sheep is dhabh. If one performs nahr on them, it is permissible but disliked. As for the recommendation, it is for conforming to the transmitted sunnah and because of the gathering of the veins in the place of nahr for camels and in the place of dhabh for cows and sheep. The dislike is for opposing the sunnah, and it is due to a meaning in something else, so it does not prevent permissibility and being lawful, contrary to what Malik says that it is not lawful.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the Matn of al-Quduri, explained in sharh style. It addresses the recommended method of slaughter for different animals. For camels, nahr (cutting the throat at the upper chest near the neck base) is recommended, while for cows and goats, dhabh (cutting the throat at the neck) is recommended. However, doing the opposite is still permissible (ja'iz) but disliked (makruh tanzihi). The reason for the recommendation is that this is the continuous practice of the sunnah (al-sunnah al-mutawarithah) and also because the main blood vessels gather conveniently in the nahr area for camels and in the dhabh area for cows/goats. The dislike is due to opposing the sunnah, but this dislike does not render the meat impermissible. This refutes the view of Imam Malik who considers it absolutely impermissible. The Hanafi position is clear: the act is makruh but the meat is halal.

Key Terms
نحر (nahr): Slaughtering an animal by cutting the throat at the upper chest near the base of the neck, specifically recommended for camels.
ذبح (dhabh): Slaughtering by cutting the throat at the neck, recommended for cows and goats/sheep.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; doing it earns reward, omitting it is not sinful but may be disliked if it contradicts sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a camel is slaughtered by dhabh (cutting the throat) instead of nahr, the meat is:
A) Haram because it opposes the sunnah.
B) Halal but it is disliked (makruh) to do so.
C) Halal and there is no dislike.
D) Only permissible if done accidentally.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that slaughtering an animal by the opposite method is permissible but disliked; the meat is halal, contrary to the Maliki position.

Ruling on Dead Fetus in Slaughtered Animal: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fetus being halal after mother's slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the ruling of a dead fetus found in a slaughtered animal, identify the evidence for the Sahibayn view, and explain the practical consequence of the ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
A dead fetus is not eaten according to Abu Hanifa, but is eaten if fully formed according to Sahibayn — the hadith is the key proof.

When a pregnant animal is slaughtered, a dead fetus may be found in its belly. Is that fetus halal to eat? The Hanafi school contains two positions: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it is not eaten at all, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, rule it is halal if fully formed. This lesson unpacks the evidence for both views and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Issue and Two Positions
Read the opening lines: the matn states Abu Hanifa's view (not eaten) and then the Sahibayn's view (eaten if fully formed). Note the condition: 'idha tammat khilqatuhu' (when his creation is complete).
The third position from Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad agrees with Abu Hanifa.
2
Examine the Naqli Dalil (Hadith)
The text provides the hadith: 'dhabahu al-janin dhabahu ummihi' — the slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother. This is the primary proof for the Sahibayn. Consider that its transmission is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
Abu Hanifa may consider this hadith weak or interpret it differently, though the text does not state his counter-proof.
3
Understand the Aqli Dalil (Rational Argument)
The commentator argues the fetus is a part of the mother in both physical and legal terms. Physically: it is connected, nourished, breathes with her. Legally: it is included in the sale of the mother and freed upon her emancipation. Therefore, the wound in the mother suffices as slaughter for the fetus when independent slaughter is impossible.
This is a qiyas (analogy) to the case of game where incapitating slaughter by wounding is accepted.
4
Compare Abu Hanifa's Position
Although the text does not give Abu Hanifa's proof, we can infer: he likely views the fetus as a separate entity not included in the mother's slaughter, especially if it is dead (carrion). The mother's slaughter does not extend to it.
Later Hanafi works often adopt the Sahibayn view as mufta bihi due to the strength of the hadith.
5
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: If a fully formed dead fetus is found, Abu Hanifa says it is haram (carrion), while Sahibayn and Shafi'i say it is halal. This affects whether the meat can be consumed or sold.
In contemporary practice, many Hanafi fatwa bodies adopt the Sahibayn view.

تشریح یہ صاحبین اور امام شافعی کی دلیل ہے ایک دلیل نقلی اور دوسری دلیل عقلی ۔ دلیل نقلی یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے کہ ماں کی ذکاۃ جنین کی ذکاۃ ہے اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ماں کو ذبح کرنا بچہ کا ذبح کرنا ہے لہذا پھر اس کو کھانا جائز ہو گیا۔
