He said: Whoever performs nahr on a she-camel or dhabh on a cow and finds in its belly a dead fetus, it is not eaten, whether its hair has grown or not. This is according to Abu Hanifa, and it is the saying of Zufar and al-Hasan ibn Ziyad (may Allah have mercy on them). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) said: When its creation is complete, it is eaten, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i. Their proof: Because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother.' And because it is a part of the mother in reality, for it is connected to her until it is separated with scissors, and it is nourished by her food, and breathes with her breath. And similarly in legal terms, it enters into the sale of the mother and is freed by her emancipation. And when it is a part of her, the wound in the mother is a slaughter for it when unable to slaughter it, as in the case of game.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on a dead fetus found in the belly of a slaughtered animal. The matn presents two positions: (1) Imam Abu Hanifa, supported by Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, hold that the fetus is not eaten regardless of whether it has hair or is fully formed. (2) The two primary disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), along with Imam al-Shafi'i, hold that if the fetus is fully formed (tamm al-khilqah), it is halal to eat. The text then provides the proof for the second position, which includes both a hadith (naqli) and rational analogy (aqli). The hadith states: 'The slaughter of the fetus is the slaughter of its mother.' The rational proof argues that the fetus is a part of the mother in both a physical and legal sense (connected, nourished, breathes, included in sale and emancipation), and since it cannot be slaughtered independently, the mother's slaughter suffices for it, analogous to a wounded animal that cannot be slaughtered properly. The text does not provide the proof for Abu Hanifa's position, nor does it specify which view is mufta bihi, leaving the ikhtilaf unresolved in this passage.

Key Terms
جنين (janin): The fetus in the womb of the slaughtered animal, whether stillborn or dead.
تمت خلقته (tammat khilqatuhu): When the fetus's creation is complete and fully formed, e.g., hair has grown.
ذكاة الجنين ذكاة أمه (dhabahu al-janin dhabahu ummihi): Hadith meaning the slaughter of the fetus is accomplished by the slaughter of its mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, what is Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on eating a dead fetus found in a slaughtered cow?
A) It is halal if the fetus is fully formed.
B) It is halal regardless of formation.
C) It is not halal, whether hair has grown or not.
D) It is halal only if the mother was slaughtered by nahr (not dhabh).

Key Takeaway
When a dead fetus is found in a slaughtered animal, the Hanafi school has two positions: Abu Hanifa says it is not eaten, while Sahibayn (and Shafi'i) say it is eaten if fully formed, based on the hadith 'dhabahu al-janin dhabahu ummihi'.

Ruling on Predators and Carrion Birds with Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute and rulings on various animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on eating various predators and carrion birds, and evaluate the Shafi'i position on hyena and fox using the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Predators with fangs are haram; carrion birds are makruh tahrimi; the elephant is makruh because it does not kill prey.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, Al-Marghinani presents the Hanafi position on which animals are prohibited or disliked, with a specific dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the hyena and fox. The ruling is based on the hadith 'كل ذي ناب من السباع فأكله حرام' (Every predator with fangs is forbidden). The passage also covers the moral wisdom behind the prohibition and provides distinct rulings for other animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: eating specific animals. Determine the hukm level (haram, makruh tahrimi) for each animal mentioned: hyena, fox, elephant, jerboa, weasel, vulture, baghath.
The passage gives explicit rulings; note that some are haram and some makruh tahrimi.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith prohibiting predators with fangs is the primary evidence. Understand its implication: it includes all animals that hunt with their fangs.
The hadith is cited indirectly; its full text is 'كل ذي ناب من السباع فأكله حرام'.
3
Understand the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i permits hyena and fox. The Hanafi school argues they are predators (sabu') and thus included in the hadith prohibition.
The passage calls the hadith a 'proof against al-Shafi'i'.
4
Apply the ruling to each animal
Distinguish between haram (hyena, fox, jerboa, weasel) and makruh tahrimi (elephant, vulture, baghath) based on the animal's characteristics and behavior.
The elephant has a tusk but does not kill prey; carrion birds eat dead meat.
5
Reflect on the wisdom (hikma)
The commentary explains that prohibiting predators preserves human dignity by preventing the transfer of evil traits through consumption.
This is not the cause (illa) but the wisdom behind the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الذبائح
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳ فيه الضبع والثعلب فيكون الحديث حجة على الشافعى فى اباحتهما والفيل ذوناب فيكره واليربوع وابن عرس من السباع الهوام وكره أكل الرخم والبغاث لأنهما يأكلان الجيف.
ترجمہ اور تحریم کی وجہ واللہ اعلم بنی آدم کی کرامت ہے تا کہ ان اوصاف ذمیمہ میں سے کچھ انسانوں کی جانب سرایت نہ کر جائیں ان کو کھانے سے اور درندہ میں بجو اور لومڑی داخل ہیں تو حدیث شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہوگی ان دونوں کو جائز قرار دینے میں اور ہاتھی ذوناب ہے تو مکروہ ہے اور جنگلی چوہا اور نیولا ان درندوں میں سے ہیں جو زمین پر رینگنے والے ہیں اور فقہاء نے مکرر قرار دیا ہے گدھ اور بغاث کے کھانے کو اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں گندگی کھاتے ہیں۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ درندوں کو حرام کرنے کی شاید یہ وجہ ہے کہ ان میں خباثت اور شرارت ہے اگر ان کو حلال کر دیا جاتا تو انسان جو اشرف المخلوقات ہے ان کو کھاتا اور ان کے اندر بھی ان کے برے خصائل پیدا ہوتے جو تکریم انسانی کے خلاف تھا اس لئے ان کو حرام قرار دیا گیا تا کہ تکریم انسانی مجروح نہ ہو جائے ۔ نیز درندہ میں بجو اور لومڑی بھی داخل ہے اور امام شافعی نے ان دونوں کو حلال قرار دیا ہے حالانکہ حدیث میں درندہ سے منع فرمایا گیا ہے اور یہ بھی درندہ ہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ حدیث مذکور امام شافعی کے خلاف حجت ہے۔ ہاتھی بھی ذوناب ہے اور درندہ کے سارے اوصاف اس میں موجود ہیں البتہ وہ مار کر کھاتا نہیں ہے تو اس کا کھانا مکروہ تحریمی ہوگا۔ اور جنگلی چوہا اور نیول بھی درندے ہیں مگر یہ ایسے درندہ ہیں جو زمین میں بل بنا کر رہتے ہیں۔ اور گدھ جس کو کر گس بھی کہتے ہیں مکروہ تحریمی ہے اور اسی کی شکل کا کچھ اس سے چھوٹا اور جانور ہے جس کو بغاث کہتے ہیں اس کا بھیجا ہی حکم ہے کیوں کہ یہ دونوں گندگی کھاتے ہیں۔
Book of Slaughtered Animals. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidaya, volume 13. In it: the hyena and the fox, so the hadith is a proof against al-Shafi'i regarding their permissibility. The elephant has a tusk, so it is disliked. The jerboa and weasel are from the predators that crawl. And the eating of vulture and baghath is disliked because they eat carrion. Translation: And the reason for prohibition, and Allah knows best, is the honor of the children of Adam so that none of these blameworthy characteristics infiltrate humans from eating them. And among predators, badger and fox are included, so the hadith will be proof against al-Shafi'i in declaring both permissible. And the elephant has a tusk, so it is disliked. And the jerboa and weasel are among the predators that crawl on the ground. And the jurists have repeatedly decided the dislikedness of eating vulture and baghath because both eat carrion. Commentary: The author of Hidaya says that perhaps the reason for prohibiting predators is that they have wickedness and mischief. If they were made permissible, then humans, who are the noblest of creatures, would eat them and the evil traits within them would develop in them, which is against human honor. Therefore, they were declared prohibited so that human honor is not harmed. Also, among predators, badger and fox are included, and Imam al-Shafi'i has declared them permissible, even though the hadith prohibits predators, and they are predators, so it becomes clear that the mentioned hadith is proof against Imam al-Shafi'i. The elephant also has a tusk, and all the characteristics of predators are present in it, except it does not kill and eat, so its eating will be makruh tahrimi. And the jerboa and weasel are also predators, but they are predators that live in burrows in the ground. And the vulture, also called kargas, is makruh tahrimi, and a slightly smaller bird of similar shape called baghath has the same ruling because both eat carrion.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute and also contains rulings on various animals. The matn states the ruling: the hyena (dabu') and fox (tha'lab) are included among predators, and the hadith prohibiting predators is a proof against Imam al-Shafi'i who allows them. The elephant (fil) has a tusk (dhu nab) but is not a true predator because it does not kill with its fangs; hence it is makruh tahrimi. The jerboa (yarbu') and weasel (ibn irds) are from the crawling predators (sabu' hawaam), so they are also haram. The eating of vulture (rakham) and baghath (a type of crow-like bird) is disliked because they eat carrion. The commentary explains the wisdom behind prohibiting predators: to preserve human dignity by preventing the transfer of evil traits. It reiterates that the hadith is proof against al-Shafi'i. For the elephant, it clarifies that since it does not kill prey with its tusk, it is only makruh tahrimi, not haram. The jerboa and weasel are predators that burrow, so they remain haram. Vulture and baghath are makruh tahrimi due to carrion consumption.

Key Terms
السباع (al-sibā'): Wild predators that attack and kill with their fangs.
ذو ناب (dhū nāb): Having a canine tooth or tusk used for predation.
الهوام (al-hawāmm): Crawling creatures, often insects or small animals that burrow.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because it has no fangs.
B) Because it eats carrion.
C) Because it does not kill prey with its tusk.
D) Because it is a domesticated animal.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits eating predators with fangs and considers carrion birds disliked, with the elephant as a unique case due to its non-predatory nature.

Ruling on Field Crow (Ghurab al-Zar')
Ruling that field crow is permissible to eat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating field crow and explain the two reasons for its permissibility, distinguishing it from other crows.

Core Idea
A crow that feeds only on grain is halal; it is neither a carrion-eater nor a predator.

This lesson addresses a specific fiqh ruling regarding the permissibility of eating a type of crow known as ghurab al-zar' (field crow). The source text from al-Quduri provides a clear ruling based on two key characteristics: its diet and its nature. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between different types of birds and the underlying principles of tahara and halal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The text rules on 'ghurab al-zar'. What is the ruling? 'La ba'sa' (no harm, permissible).
2
Analyze the rationale
The text gives two reasons: it eats grain (not carrion) and it is not a predatory bird.
These two conditions are the basis for the ruling.
3
Contrast with other crows
Understand that other crows that eat carrion or are predatory are not included in this ruling.
The ruling is specific to field crows.
4
Check the madhhab position
Confirm that this is the Hanafi position as stated by al-Quduri.
No other schools are mentioned in this text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كھیتی کا کوا کھانے کا حکم
قال ولا باس بغراب الزرع لانه ياكل الحب ولا ياكل الجيف وليس من سباع الطير
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور کھیتی کے کونے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ دانہ کھاتا ہے اور گندگی نہیں کھا تا وہ پرندوں میں سے پھاڑنے والوں میں سے نہیں ہے۔
تشریح جوکوا فقط کھیت کے دانے کھاتا ہے اور نا پا کی نہیں کھا تا اس کے کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے کیوں کہ وہ ناپا کی بھی نہیں کھاتا اور وہ درندوں میں بھی شمار نہیں ہوتا۔
Ruling on eating the field crow. He said: There is no harm in the field crow because it eats grain and does not eat carrion, and it is not from the predatory birds. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And there is no prohibition in the crow of the field because it eats grain and does not eat carrion, and it is not among the birds that tear. Commentary: The crow that only eats grains of the field and does not eat impurity—there is no prohibition in its eating because it does not eat impurity and it is not counted among predators.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from al-Quduri, stating the permissibility of eating a field crow (ghurab al-zar'). The reason given is that this crow eats only grain, not carrion, and it is not a bird of prey. The commentary confirms that such a crow is halal and without any blame.

Key Terms
غراب الزرع (ghurāb al-zar'): A crow that feeds on grain in fields, not carrion.
سباع الطير (sibā' al-ṭayr): Predatory birds that tear and eat meat.

Key Takeaway
The field crow that eats grain and is not a predator is halal to eat according to the Hanafi school.

Three Types of Crows: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Makruh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a mixed-diet crow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each type of crow based on diet and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding the mixed-diet crow.

Core Idea
A crow's diet determines its ruling, but when diet is mixed, the two imams differ on which habit to weigh.

This short note (tanbeeh) classifies crows into three dietary categories and presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf disagree on the third type – a crow that eats both grain and carrion. Understanding the basis of their disagreement teaches us how Hanafi scholars prioritise different aspects of an animal's nature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Read the Arabic text and list the three types of crows based on their diet: pure grain, pure impurity, and mixed diet.
The first two types are agreed upon; the dispute is only on the third.
2
Extract the ruling for each category
For each type, note whether the text says it is makruh (disliked) or not. Type 1: not makruh. Type 2: makruh. Type 3: two views.
The text uses 'مکروہ نہیں ہے' (not disliked) for type 1, 'مکروہ ہے' (disliked) for type 2.
3
Locate the disagreement on type 3
Focus on the third type. The text states that according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is not makruh, and according to Imam Abu Yusuf it is makruh.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf directly reported in the source.
4
Analyse the basis for each view
Think about why each imam ruled as he did. Abu Hanifa seems to consider that since it eats grain sometimes, it resembles the first type. Abu Yusuf gives weight to its carrion-eating habit as dominant.
The text does not provide explicit proofs, but the reasoning is inferred from similar rulings.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf: what does this mean for a person following the Hanafi school today? The lesson should note that the operative view may be the more lenient (Abu Hanifa) unless otherwise specified.
Tarjih is not given here; in practice many later texts adopt Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text

Commentary
This is a cautionary note (tanbeeh) that classifies crows into three categories based on diet. The first type eats only grain and is halal. The second eats only carrion or impurity and is makruh. This is a direct intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific case.

Key Terms

مکروہ (makrūh): Legally disliked; in Hanafi fiqh usually refers to makruh tanzihi (abstention recommended).
تنبیہ (tanbīh): A cautionary note or warning appended to a text.

Ruling on Abqa' and Ghurab (Carrion-Eating Crows)
Ruling statement on two types of carrion-eating crows

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for abqa' and ghurab crows and explain why they are not eaten.

Core Idea
A crow that eats carrion is not eaten – diet overrides species.

This passage from al-Quduri presents a clear ruling on two types of crows: abqa' and ghurab. Both are considered makruh to eat because they consume carrion. Understanding this ruling helps distinguish between permissible and impermissible birds in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two birds
Read the text to identify the two specific crows mentioned: abqa' (black-and-white crow) and ghurab (a crow that comes in hot weather).
Abqa' has a white neck; ghurab has heavy feet.
2
State the ruling for each
The text says 'لا يوكل' (not eaten) for both. Understand that the ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but not haram).
3
Identify the cause
Both birds are not eaten because they eat carrion (jifah). The cause is their diet, not their species.
Grain-eating crows like ghurab al-zar' are halal.
4
Apply the principle
The general Hanafi principle: any bird that eats carrion or filth is makruh. This ruling applies directly.
This is a straightforward application of the rule against consuming filthy animals.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Eating 'Aq'aq (Magpie)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'aq'aq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on eating 'aq'aq, explain their respective reasoning (illa), and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the two views.

Core Idea
A bird that mixes its diet is permissible by Abu Hanifa, but makruh by Abu Yusuf if most of its food is carrion.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute over the permissibility of eating the 'aq'aq (magpie). While both Imams agree on the general principle that a bird's diet determines its ruling, they differ on which aspect of the diet is decisive. Abu Hanifa focuses on the fact that the bird mixes its diet (grain and carrion), making it analogous to a permissible chicken. Abu Yusuf considers the predominant food (carrion) and thus deems it makruh. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to detect how the same usul principle can lead to different rulings depending on how the 'illa is identified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Read the passage carefully and note the rulings of Abu Hanifa (permissible) and Abu Yusuf (makruh).
The text uses 'la ba'sa' (no harm) for Abu Hanifa and 'yukrah' (it is disliked) for Abu Yusuf.
2
Extract the 'illa (effective cause) for each Imām
Determine the reasoning each Imām uses to reach his ruling. Abu Hanifa points to the bird's mixing (yukhlit) of its diet, resembling a chicken. Abu Yusuf points to the predominance of carrion (ghālib akluh al-jīfaf).
The 'illa is the characteristic that connects the case to the ruling in qiyas.
3
Analyse the qiyas structure
Map out the qiyas for each Imām. For Abu Hanifa: asl = chicken (permissible), far' = 'aq'aq, illa = mixing diet, hukm = permissible. For Abu Yusuf: asl = crow or carrion eater (makruh/haram), far' = 'aq'aq, illa = predominant carrion, hukm = makruh.
The difference lies in how the 'illa is defined: mixing vs. predominance.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is whether a follower may eat 'aq'aq. Those following Abu Hanifa consider it halal; those following Abu Yusuf avoid it as makruh.
Note that the text does not give a tarjih (preferred view), so both are operative within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عقعق کے کھانے کے حکم ، اقوال فقہاء
قال ابو حنيفة لا باس باكل العقعق لانه يخلط فاشبه الدحاجة وعن ابى يوسف انه يكره لان غالب اكله الجيف.
ترجمہ ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ عقیق کے کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ وہ خلط کرتا ہے تو وہ مرغی کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ یہ مکروہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی غالب خوراک ناپاکی ہے۔
تشریح علامہ طحطاوی نے اسکو عقعق بروزن جعفر کہا ہے جو کبوتر کے برابر به شکل غراب لمبی دم کا سیاہ وسفید ایک پرندہ ہے۔ قاموس میں لکھا ہے کہ عقعق بروزن قند ابلق (سیاہ وسفید) پرندہ ہے جس کی آواز میں مین اور قاف معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ یہ وہ ہے جس کو ہمارے یہاں مہو کھا کہتے ہیں اور اسی کو ہمارے دیہاتوں میں ہو کچھ کہتے ہیں۔ بہر حال امام صاحب نے اس کو مرغی کے حکم میں رکھا ہے اور اس کے کھانے کو جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف نے اس کو مکروہ کہا ہے کیونکہ یہ عموما گندگی کھاتا ہے۔
Ruling on eating 'aq'aq, statements of jurists. Abu Hanifa said: There is no harm in eating 'aq'aq because it mixes, so it resembles a chicken. And from Abu Yusuf that it is disliked because most of its food is carrion. Translation: Abu Hanifa said that there is no prohibition in eating 'aq'aq because it mixes, so it became similar to a chicken. And it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that it is disliked because its predominant food is impurity. Commentary: Allamah al-Tahtawi said that 'aq'aq (on the pattern of ja'far) is a bird equal to a pigeon, shaped like a crow, with a long tail, black and white. In the Qamus, it is written that 'aq'aq (on the pattern of qand) is a black-and-white bird whose call contains 'meem' and 'qaf'. It is what we call 'mahokha' and in our villages 'ho kuch'. In any case, Imam Abu Hanifa placed it under the ruling of chicken and declared its eating permissible. Imam Abu Yusuf said it is disliked because it generally eats filth.

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the 'aq'aq bird (magpie). Imam Abu Hanifa declares it permissible (la ba'sa) because it 'mixes' (yukhlit) in its diet, meaning it eats both grain and carrion, similar to a domestic chicken, which is also mixed. Therefore it is halal. Imam Abu Yusuf, however, considers it makruh because the majority of its diet consists of carrion (ghalib akluh al-jifaf). The commentary describes the bird's physical appearance and confirms that the dispute hinges on whether its diet is predominantly carrion or varied.

Key Terms
عقعق ('aq'aq): A black-and-white bird resembling a crow with a long tail, known as magpie.
خلط (khalata): To mix; here, the bird mixes its diet (grain and carrion).

Key Takeaway
The ruling on 'aq'aq differs between Abu Hanifa (permissible) and Abu Yusuf (makruh) based on whether the mixed diet or the predominant carrion is taken as the effective cause.

Ruling on Makruh Animals: Dabu', Dabb, Turtle, Wasp, Insects
Ruling with proof on disliked animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the listed animals and explain the proof for the dislikedness of dabb.

Core Idea
Eating dabb is makruh because the Prophet forbade it; all crawling insects follow by analogy.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar lists animals whose consumption is considered makruh tanzihi or tahrimi in the Hanafi school. The primary proof comes from a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade Aisha from eating dabb. The passage also highlights a point of ikhtilaf with the Shafi'i school, which permits dabb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the animals and the ruling
List the animals mentioned: dabu' (hyena), dabb (lizard), turtle, wasp, and all insects. The ruling for all is makruh.
2
Locate the primary proof
The proof for dabb is the hadith where the Prophet forbade Aisha from eating it. This is a dalil from Sunnah.
The hadith is ahad, making the ruling zanni al-thubut, hence makruh rather than haram.
3
Analyze the legal implication
According to Hanafi usul, a prohibition (nahy) indicates karahah tanzihiyyah unless there is evidence for tahrim. Here it is karahah.
The passage uses this hadith as proof against the Shafi'i position of ibaha.
4
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school permits dabb. The Hanafi school argues that the Prophet's prohibition is evidence of dislike.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; both schools have valid methodological approaches.
5
Understand the qiyas to other insects
All insects (hasharat) are makruh by analogy with dabb, as they share the common characteristic of being creeping creatures.
The turtle and wasp are included as they are considered from the same category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کن جانوروں کا کھانا مکروہ ہے
قال ويكره أكل الضبع والضب والسلحفاة والزنبور والحشرات كلها اما الضبع فلما ذكرنا واما الضب فلان النبي عليه السلام نهى عائشة حين سالته عن اكله وهو حجة على الشافعي في اباحته والزنبور من الموذيات والسلحفاة من خبائث الحشرات ولهذا لا يجب على المحرم بقتله شئى وانما تكره الحشرات كلها استدلا لا بالضب لانه منها .
تر جمہ ... قدوری نے فرمایا اور بہو اور گوہ اور کچھو اور بھڑ اور تمام زمین پر رینگنے والے کیڑے مکوڑے کھانا مکروہ ہے۔ بہر حال بجواس
Which animals' eating is disliked? He said: The eating of hyena, dabb (lizard), turtle, wasp, and all insects is disliked. As for the hyena, due to what we mentioned. As for the dabb, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade Aisha when she asked him about eating it, and it is proof against al-Shafi'i in his permissibility. The wasp is from harmful things, and the turtle is from the filthy insects. For this reason, no compensation is obligatory on the one in ihram for killing it. And all insects are disliked, using the dabb as evidence because it is from them.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. Al-Quduri states that hyena (dabu'), dabb (a type of lizard), turtle (sulahfaa), wasp (zanbur), and all crawling insects (hasharat) are makruh. The proof for dabb is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade Aisha from eating it, and this hadith is cited as proof against al-Shafi'i who permits it. The wasp is disliked because it is harmful. The turtle is from filthy creatures. No atonement is required for killing them in ihram, indicating they are not hunted game. All insects are disliked by analogy with dabb.

Key Terms
الضب (al-dabb): A type of lizard, known as dabb.
الحشرات (al-hasharāt): Crawling insects and small creatures that creep on the ground.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that certain animals are makruh to eat, relying on prophetic prohibition and analogy.

Hanafi Position on Sea Creatures: Only Fish Halal
Inter-madhhab dispute on sea creatures: Hanafi ruling and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sea creatures, identify the key proofs from Quran and Hadith, and evaluate the opposing Maliki/Shafi'i arguments and the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Only fish is halal from sea creatures; all else is haram because it falls under 'khabaith' (impure things) which Allah has forbidden.

This passage presents the Hanafi position that only fish from sea creatures is permissible, and contrasts it with the more permissive views of the Maliki and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafis base their ruling on the general prohibition of 'khabaith' (impure things) in Quran 7:157, and interpret the permissive verses (5:96) and hadith on sea animals as referring specifically to fish. Understanding this dispute reveals how different schools weigh textual evidence and apply usul principles.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that only fish is halal; all other sea creatures are haram. This is the established position in the matn of al-Quduri and is relied upon in the school.
The ruling applies to eating and selling; the same prohibition applies to both.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Malikis and Shafi'is have multiple views: some permit all sea creatures absolutely, others except pig, dog, human, or frog. The text reports three Shafi'i views.
The opposition relies on general texts without restricting to fish.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their evidence includes: (1) Quran 5:96 'Uhilla lakum saydu al-bahr' — general permission for sea game; (2) Hadith 'the sea's water is purifying and its dead are halal'; (3) Rational analogy: sea creatures lack blood, so they are like fish which is halal.
The opponent's arguments appear strong but are interpreted differently by Hanafis.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis counter: (1) The verse refers to the act of hunting (istiyad), not the edibility of all hunted; (2) The hadith is interpreted to mean only fish, supported by the hadith 'two dead things are halal: fish and locust'; (3) The analogy fails because non-fish sea creatures are classified as 'khabith' per Quran 7:157, and specific hadith forbid frog and crab.
The Hanafi response reinterprets the opponent's proofs and provides additional evidence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafis consider shellfish, crab, lobster, shrimp, squid, etc. haram; Malikis and Shafi'is generally allow them (with exceptions). This affects daily practice, especially for Hanafis living near coasts or in communities where seafood is common.
The dispute is ongoing; Hanafis follow their relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دریائی جانوروں میں سے کون سا جانور کھانا حلال ہے، اقوال فقہاء
كتاب الذبائح
قال ولا يوكل من حيوان الماء الا السمك وقال مالك وجماعة من اهل العلم باطلاق جميع مافي البحر واستثنى بعضهم الخنزير والكلب والانسان وعن الشافعى انه اطلق ذالک کله والخلاف فی الاكل والبيع واحد
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور پانی کے جانوروں میں مچھلی کے علاوہ کچھ نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور مالک اور اہل علم کی ایک جماعت ان تمام جانوروں کی اباحت کے قائل ہیں جو دریا میں ہیں اور ان میں سے بعض نے خنزیر اور کتے اور انسان کا استثناء کیا ہے اور شافعی سے منقول ہے کہ انہوں نے ان تمام کو جائز قرار دیا ہے اور کھانے اور بیع میں اختلاف ایک ہے۔
تشریح حنفیہ کے نزدیک دریائی جانوروں میں سے صرف مچھلی جائز ہے اور کچھ جائز نہیں ہے۔
اور امام مالک، ابن ابی لیلی اور اصحاب الظواہر اور امام شافعی کے ایک قول میں دریا کا ہر جانور حلال ہے خواہ وہ دریائی خنزیر اور کتا اور انسان ہی کیوں نہ ہو۔ امام شافعی کا ایک قول یہ ہے کہ سب جانور حلال ہیں مگر دریائی خنزیر اور کتا اور انسان جائز نہیں ۔ یہی لیٹ کا قول ہے۔ اور امام شافعی کا تیسرا قول یہ ہے کہ مینڈک کے علاوہ سب جانور حلال ہیں۔
فریق مخالف کی دلیل
لهم قوله تعالى احل لكم صيد البحر من غير فصل وقوله عليه السلام في البحر هو الطهور ماؤه والحل ميتته ولانه لادم في هذه الاشياء اذا الدموى لايسكن الماء والمحرم هو الدم فاشبه السمك
ترجمہ ان سب کی دلیل فرمانِ باری تعالیٰ احل لكم الصيد البحر ہے بغیر تفصیل کے اور دریا کے بارے میں نبی علیہ السلام کا فرمان ہے کہ اس کا پانی پاک کرنے والا ہے اور اس کا مردار حلال ہے اور اسلئے کہ ان چیزوں میں خون نہیں ہوتا اسلئے کہ خون والا پانی میں نہیں رہ سکتا اور حرام کرنے والا وہ خون ہے تو یہ سب مچھلی کے مشابہ ہو گئے ۔
تشریح یہ فریق مخالف کی دلیل ہے جو تین اجزاء پر مشتمل ہے۔ - آیت احل لكم الصيد البحر تمہارے لئے دریا کا شکار حلال کر دیا گیا ہے۔ اس میں تفصیل نہیں کہ کون سا حلال کیا گیا ہے اور کون سانہیں تو معلوم ہوا کہ مطلقاً دریائی شکار حلال ہے تو اس میں سب جانور حلال ہو گئے ۔ -۲- حدیث، دریا کا پانی خوب پاک کرنے والا ہے اور اس کا مردار حلال ہے۔ اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ دریائی مردار حلال ہے لہذا مذکورہ تمام دریائی جانور حلال ہوں گے۔ - اصل حرام کرنے والی چیز وہ خون ہے اور دریائی جانوروں میں خون نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اگر ان میں خون ہوتا تو یہ پانی میں ہمیشہ نہ رہ پاتے تو یہ تو مچھلی کے حکم میں ہوں گے۔ پھر جس نے کھانے کو جائز کہا اس نے بیع کو بھی جائز کہا ہے لہذا بیع میں بھی یہی اختلاف
(مذکور جاری ہوگا۔)
كتاب الذبائح
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۳
ولنا قوله تعالى ويحرم عليهم الخبائث وما سوى السمك خبيث ونهى رسول الله عليه السلام عن دواء يتخذ فيه الضفدع ونهى عن بيع السرطان والصيد المذكور فيما تلا محمول على الاصطياد وهو مباح فيما لا يحل الميتة المذكورة فيما روى محمولة على السمك وهو حلال مستثنى من ذالك لقوله عليه السلام احلت لنا میتتان و دمان اما الميتتان فالمسك والجراد واما الدمان فالكبد والطحال
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل فرمان باری تعالیٰ ہے اور حرام کرتا ہے وہ ان پر خبائث کو اور مچھلی کے علاوہ سب خبیث ہیں اور نبی علیہ السلام نے ایسی دواء سے منع فرمایا ہے جس میں مینڈک ڈالا گیا ہو اور وہ صید (شکار) جو مذکور ہے اس آیت میں جس کو فریق مخالف نے تلاوت کی وہ اصطياد (شکار) کرنے پر محمول ہے۔ اور شکار کرنا اس کا بھی جائز ہے جو حلال نہیں ہے اور وہ میتہ (مردار ) جو مذکور ہے اس حدیث میں جس کو فریق مخالف نے روایت کی وہ مچھلی پر محمول ہے اور مچھلی حلال ہے جو تمام مرداروں سے مستثنیٰ ہے۔ نبی علیہ السلام کے فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ ہمارے لیئے دو مردار اور دو خون حلال کر دیے گئے ۔ بہر حال دو مردار پس وہ مچھلی اور ٹڈی ہے اور بہر حال دوخون پس وہ کلیجہ اور تلی ہے۔ تشریح یہ ہماری دلیل ہے جس میں ایک آیت اور دو حدیث ہیں پھر فریق مخالف کے مستدلات کا جواب ہے۔ ا آیت ويحرم عليهم الخبائث تو معلوم ہوا کہ خبائث حرام ہیں اور مچھلی کے علاوہ جتنے بھی دریائی جانور ہیں سب خبیث ہیں سب کی طبیعتوں میں خبائث ہیں۔
لم
حدیث اول، جس دواء میں مینڈک ڈالا گیا ہو ایسی دواء سے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے منع فرمایا ہے۔ اگر مینڈک جائز ہوتا تو دواء سے منع کیوں فرمایا جاتا۔
-۳- حدیث ثانی، حدیث میں کیکڑے کی بیچ سے ممانعت فرمائی گئی ہے اور ماقبل میں معلوم ہو چکا ہے کہ بیچ اور اکل دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے۔
-۴- فریق مخالف نے جس آیت سے استدلال کیا ہے اس میں حمید اصطیار کے معنی میں ہے اور مطلب یہ ہے کہ دریا میں شکار کرنا حلال ہے اور شکاران جانوروں کا بھی جائز ہوتا ہے جو حلال نہیں ہوتے لہذا اس سے استدلال نام نہیں ہے۔ -- فریق مخالف نے جس حدیث سے استدلال کیا ہے اس میں مردار سے مراد مچھلی ہے اور مچھلی حلال ہے یعنی تمام دریائی مرداروں میں سے صرف مچھلی حلال ہے۔ اس کی کیا دلیل ہے کہ مچھلی مردار ہے ؟
حدیث میں ہے کہ ہمارے لئے دومر دار حلال ہیں اور دو خون حلال ہیں اور مردار سے مراد مچھلی اور ٹڈی ہے اور خون سے مراد کلیجہ اور تلی ہے تو اس حدیث کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مچھلی جو مردار ہے اس کے بعد بھی حلال ہے اس کو والحل ميتتہ نے تعبیر فرمایا ہے۔
From sea animals, only fish is eaten. Malik and a group of scholars permitted all sea creatures absolutely; some excepted pig, dog, and human. From al-Shafi'i, he permitted all. The dispute is the same for eating and selling. Hanafis: only fish is permissible. Malik, Ibn Abi Layla, Zahiris, and one Shafi'i view: all sea animals are halal, even sea pig, dog, human. Another Shafi'i view: all except sea pig, dog, human. A third Shafi'i view: all except frog. Opponent's proof: verse 'He allowed you sea game' without specification; hadith 'its water is purifying and its dead is halal'; and because these creatures have no blood, so they are like fish. Our proof: verse 'And He forbids them the impure things (khabaith)'; everything besides fish is impure. Hadeeth forbids medicine containing frog; prohibits selling crab. The 'game' in the verse refers to hunting (istiyad) which is permissible but not necessarily for eating; the 'dead' in the hadith refers to fish, which is excepted from the general prohibition of carrion by the hadith: 'Two dead things and two bloods are allowed: fish and locust, liver and spleen.' Commentary: The Hanafi evidence includes one verse and two hadiths, and a refutation of the opponent's arguments.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the permissibility of eating sea creatures. The Hanafi position is strict: only fish is halal. The text begins by stating the ruling from the matn (Quduri): 'ولا يوكل من حيوان الماء الا السمك' — no sea creature is eaten except fish. It then presents the Maliki view allowing all sea animals, and three reported views from al-Shafi'i: one permitting all, one excepting pig/dog/human, and one excepting frog. The opponent's (Maliki/Shafi'i) proof is threefold: (1) Quran 5:96 'احل لكم صيد البحر' — hunting sea game is made lawful unconditionally; (2) Hadith 'البحر هو الطهور ماؤه والحل ميتته' — sea water is pure and its dead are halal; (3) Rational argument: the forbidden element is blood, but sea creatures have no blood (if they did, they could not live in water), so they are analogous to fish. The Hanafi response counters each point: (1) The Quranic verse refers to 'istiyad' (hunting) which is allowed as an act, not necessarily that every hunted creature is edible. (2) The hadith about dead of the sea being halal is interpreted to mean fish specifically, supported by another hadith that only two dead things are halal: fish and locust. (3) The analogy fails because the Hanafis classify many sea creatures as 'khabith' (impure/unwholesome) based on Quran 7:157 'ويحرم عليهم الخبائث' — and everything besides fish is khabith. Additional Hanafi proofs include hadith forbidding frog in medicine and selling crab. The commentary emphasizes that the Hanafi position is the relied-upon one.

Key Terms
خبيث (khabith): Impure or unwholesome; in this context, anything besides fish from sea creatures is classified as khabith and thus prohibited.
صيد البحر (sayd al-bahr): Hunting or catching sea creatures; used in Quran 5:96 as a general permission for the act of fishing/hunting at sea.
ميتة (maytah): Carrion; dead animal not slaughtered properly. In the hadith, the sea's 'maytah' is claimed to be halal, but Hanafis restrict this to fish.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following sea creatures is halal according to the Hanafi school based on this passage?
A) Crab
B) Lobster
C) Fish
D) Frog

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits only fish from sea creatures; all others are prohibited due to the Quranic prohibition of 'khabaith'.

Qiyas and Istihsan in Mutual Sacrifice Without Permission
Introduces the issue and connects it to Zufar's dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi istihsan ruling for slaughtering another's sacrificial animal without explicit permission and explain how it differs from Zufar's qiyas.

Core Idea
Implicit permission justifies the sacrifice, making it valid and requiring only compensation for meat consumed.

This passage connects a specific case from al-Quduri's text to an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Zufar (qiyas) and the majority Hanafi scholars (istihsan). Understanding the role of implicit permission (dalalat al-ijaz) is key to seeing why the Hanafi school prefers leniency in these sacrificial matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core case
Two individuals each slaughter the other's sacrificial animal without explicit verbal permission. This is the exact scenario from the text.
The animals are udhiyah (sacrificial), not ordinary property.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
The text states this is exactly the disputed issue of Imam Zufar. Zufar applies strict qiyas (analogy to usurpation), while the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) adopt istihsan.
Both views are within the Hanafi school; the dispute is methodological.
3
Understand the two methods
Qiyas: Without explicit permission, the slaughter is unlawful, akin to usurpation, requiring full compensation. Istihsan: Implicit permission (dalalat al-ijaz) is sufficient to validate the sacrifice, with compensation only for meat consumed.
Implicit permission arises from common practice or circumstances.
4
Grasp the role of implicit permission
Dalalat al-ijaz is recognized by the Hanafi school as a valid basis for agency in certain contexts. Here, it transforms the act from usurpation to a valid sacrifice.
This is the key factor that differentiates istihsan from qiyas.
5
Note the practical difference
Under istihsan, the sacrifice is valid; if meat is consumed, the parties must compensate or forgive. Under qiyas, the sacrifice is invalid and full value of the animal is due.
This thamarah al-khilaf has real consequences for the owner's rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اذا ثبت هذا نقول في مسالة الكتاب ذبح كل منهما اضحية غيره بغير اذنه صريحا فهي خلافية زفر بعينها ويتاتى فيها القياس والاستحسان كما ذكرنا
ترجمہ جبکہ یہ بات ثابت ہو گئی تو ہم کتاب کے مسئلہ میں کہتے ہیں کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نے ایک غیر کی قربانی بغیر اس کی صریح اجازت کے ذبح کیا ہے تو یہ بعینیہ زفر کا اختلافی مسئلہ ہے اور اس میں قیاس اور استحسان جاری ہوگا جیسا کہ ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب یہ چاروں استحسانی مسائل معلوم ہو گئے تو کتاب قدوری کے مسئلہ کو سمجھنا سہل ہو گیا کیوں کہ اس میں بھی زید نے خالد کی بکری خالد کی صریحی اجازت کے بغیر ذبح کی ہے۔
البتہ دلالہ اجازت موجود ہے تو اس میں وہی حکم ہوگا جو مذکور ہوا ہے یعنی قیاس کا تقاضمہ کچھ اور ہو گا جیسا کہ امام زفر کا قول ہے اور استحسان کا تقاضہ کچھ اور ہے جس کی تفصیل گذر چکی ہے۔
When this is established, we say regarding the issue of the book: Each of the two slaughtered the sacrificial animal of the other without his explicit permission. This is exactly the disputed issue of Zufar, and qiyas and istihsan are applicable therein as we have mentioned. Translation: When this matter is established, we say in the issue of the book that each of the two slaughtered the other's sacrificial animal without his explicit permission, so this is exactly the disputed issue of Zufar, and qiyas and istihsan will operate as we have mentioned. Commentary: The author of Hidayah says that when these four istihsani issues are known, understanding the issue of Quduri's book becomes easy, because therein Zayd also slaughtered Khalid's goat without Khalid's explicit permission. However, implicit permission exists, so the same ruling applies: qiyas requires something different, as is the saying of Imam Zufar, and istihsan requires something else, the details of which have passed.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage begins by linking the specific case in the book (two people each slaughtering the other's sacrificial animal without explicit permission) to a known intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar. The author states that both qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference) apply here, as previously explained in the four istihsani issues. The commentary clarifies that once those four cases are understood, this case becomes easy: qiyas (Zufar's view) would require one ruling, while istihsan (the preferred Hanafi position) requires another. The difference hinges on whether implicit permission (dalalat al-ijaz) is considered sufficient.

Key Terms
دلالة الاجازة (dalalat al-ijaz): Implicit permission inferred from circumstances or common practice, as opposed to explicit verbal permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relationship between this issue and Imam Zufar's dispute?
A) This issue is completely unrelated.
B) This issue is exactly the same as Zufar's dispute.
C) This issue opposes Zufar's view.
D) This issue is a new one not discussed by Zufar.

Key Takeaway
Implicit permission (dalalat al-ijaz) suffices to validate the mutual slaughter of sacrificial animals in the Hanafi school, a position upheld by istihsan over Zufar's qiyas.

Returning the Skinned Animal: No Compensation under Istihsan
Ruling on swapping skinned sacrificial animals before eating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two persons inadvertently slaughter each other's sacrificial animals and skin them without eating, and explain why no compensation is required using the principle of agency by indication (dalalat al-ijaz).

Core Idea
Istihsan validates the sacrifice; implied agency eliminates liability for the skin.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in sacrifice (udhiyah) where a mix-up occurs after slaughter. The Hanafi school, through istihsan, upholds the validity of the sacrifice and resolves the exchange based on the principle of implied agency (dalalat al-ijaz). Understanding this ruling clarifies how the school balances strict qiyas with equitable reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two persons each slaughter the other's animal, skin it, but have not yet eaten the meat. The animals are now skinned carcasses belonging to the original owner by ownership.
The skinning is significant because it alters the property.
2
State the ruling
Each person takes his own skinned animal from the other, and no one pays compensation for the skin or any change in condition.
The sacrifice is valid (jā'iz) under istihsan.
3
Understand the justification
Each person is considered the other's agent by implication (dalalat al-ijaz) in the act of slaughter and skinning. An agent is not liable for actions within the scope of his agency.
This is a key principle: implicit permission creates agency.
4
Recognize the usul principle
Istihsan overrides the strict qiyas that would require compensation for the removed skin. The ruling balances equity and social custom.
Without istihsan, the skin would be a loss requiring damān.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فياخذ كل واحد منهما مسلوخة من صاحبه ولا يضمنه لانه وكيله فيما فعل دلالة. 
ترجمہ پیس لے گا ان میں سے ہر ایک اپنے ساتھی سے اپنی مسلوقہ بکری اور ساتھی کو ضامن نہیں ٹھہرائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ دلالتہ اپنے کام میں اس کا وکیل ہے ۔
تشریح بہر حال استحسانا قربانی تو جائز ہوگئی اب کیا ہوگا ؟ تو فرمایا کہ ان دونوں نے ابھی گوشت نہیں کھایا بلکہ دونوں نے کھال اتار دی ہے اور معلوم ہو گیا کہ صورتِ حال ایسی ہے تو حکم یہ ہے زید خالد سے اپنی بکری لے لے اور خالد زید سے اپنی بکری لے لے۔مسلوخہ جس کی کھال اتار دی گئی ہے یعنی جس حال میں ہے اسی حال میں لے لے اور کوئی کسی سے ضمان نہیں لے گا کیوں کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک اپنے کام میں دوسرے کا وکیل ہے اور وکیل پر منمان نہیں ہوا کرتا۔
Then each takes his own skinned animal from his companion and does not make him liable for it, because he is his agent in what he did by indication. Translation: Each will take from his companion his skinned goat and will not hold the companion liable because by indication he is his agent in his action. Commentary: In any case, by istihsan the sacrifice has become valid. Now what happens? He said that these two have not yet eaten the meat; rather, both have skinned the animals. When the situation is known, the ruling is: Zayd takes his goat from Khalid, and Khalid takes his goat from Zayd. 'Maslukha' means the skin has been removed, i.e., take it in its current condition. And no one will take compensation from anyone because each is the other's agent in his action, and an agent does not incur liability.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when both persons have slaughtered each other's animal and skinned it, but not yet eaten the meat. Under istihsan, the sacrifice is valid. Since each acted as an agent for the other by implicit permission (dalalat al-ijaz), they simply swap the skinned animals as they are. No one is liable for any deficiency (e.g., the skin removed) because an agent is not liable for actions within his agency. This ruling is based on the principle of agency by implication.

Key Terms
مسلوخة (maslūkha): An animal whose skin has been removed after slaughter.
وكيل دلالة (wakīl dalālatan): An agent appointed by implication or indication, without explicit verbal appointment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does each person take his own skinned animal without compensation?
A) Because the animals are equal in value.
B) Because each is the other's agent by indication.
C) Because they had eaten the meat.
D) Because the sacrifice was invalid.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan and implied agency combine to validate a sacrificial mix-up without compensation for the skin.

Accepting the Report of a Non-Muslim in Transactions
Ruling with proof on non-Muslim reports in transactions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting a non-Muslim agent's report in meat purchases and explain the reasoning based on the concept of khabar sahih and necessity.

Core Idea
A non-Muslim's report is accepted in transactions because need and reason override the default of suspicion.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's al-Jami' al-Sagheer about the report of a non-Muslim servant in a common transaction: buying meat. Understanding this ruling reveals a key Hanafi principle: in transactional matters (mu'amalat), the statement of any sane person—Muslim or not—is prima facie accepted, unlike in formal testimony (shahadat). The reasoning balances practical necessity with the presumption of truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the passage carefully: a person sends a Majusi servant to buy meat, and the servant reports buying it from a Jew, Christian, or Muslim. The ruling: it is permissible (yasi'u akaluhu) to eat the meat.
Note that the servant is a non-Muslim, but the seller could be any religion.
2
Locate the dalil (proof) in the text
The text gives the reason: 'because the statement of the non-Muslim is accepted in transactions, for it is a valid report (khabar sahih), coming from one who possesses reason and a religion that considers lying forbidden, and need compels its acceptance due to the frequent occurrence of transactions.'
The proof is a rational argument (dalil aqli) based on qiyas.
3
Analyze the components of the dalil
Break down the reasoning: (1) khabar sahih – a reliable report; (2) comes from a person with 'aql (reason) and din (religion that prohibits lying); (3) haja (need) – because transactions happen so often, requiring verification would cause hardship.
The Hanafi school considers a non-Muslim's report in transactions as trustworthy unless proven otherwise.
4
Distinguish from shahadat (testimony)
Contrast this rule with the rules for courtroom testimony (shahadat), where non-Muslims are generally not accepted. The distinction is based on the nature of the matter: mu'amalat vs. 'ibadat or judicial proceedings.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and avoids unnecessary restrictions in daily dealings.
5
Apply the principle to other transactions
Extend the ruling: if a non-Muslim agent reports any transactional detail (e.g., price, quantity, or source), his statement is accepted. The key is that the report pertains to a transaction and the reporter is sane and has a moral code.
The principle applies to all mu'amalat, not just meat purchases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجوسی مزدور اور خادم کی خبر کا حکم
قال ومن ارسل اجيراله مجوسيا او خادماً فاشترى لحما فقال اشتريته من يهودی او نصرانی او مسلم وسعه اكله لان قول الكافر مقبول فى المعاملات لانه خبر صحيح لصدوره عن عقل ودين يعتقد فيه حرمة الكذب والحاجة ماسة الى قبوله لكثرة وقوع المعاملات
ترجمہ فرمایا محمد نے (جامع صغیر میں ) اور جس نے بھیجا اپنے مجوسی ملازم یا خادم کو پس اس نے خریدا گوشت پس کہا میں نے اس کو خریدا ایک یہودی یا نصرانی یا مسلمان سے تو اس کو کھانا وسیع ہے کیونکہ کافر کا قول معاملات میں مقبول ہے کیونکہ وہ ایک صحیح خبر ہے اس کے صادر ہونے کی وجہ سے عقل اور دین سے (یعنی دین میں کذب کو حرام سمجھتا ہو) اور حاجت اس کو قبول کرنے کی بہت ہے کثرت وقوع معاملات کی وجہ سے۔
The ruling on the report of a Majusi (Zoroastrian) servant or worker: He (Imam Muhammad) said in al-Jami' al-Sagheer: Whoever sends his Majusi worker or servant, and he buys meat and says 'I bought it from a Jew, Christian, or Muslim', it is permissible for him to eat it because the statement of a non-Muslim is accepted in transactions, for it is a valid report, coming from one who possesses reason and a religion that considers lying forbidden, and need compels its acceptance due to the frequent occurrence of transactions.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in al-Jami' al-Sagheer regarding the report of a non-Muslim agent in a transactional matter. The scenario: a person sends a Majusi (Zoroastrian) servant or worker to purchase meat. The servant returns and says he bought it from a Jew, Christian, or Muslim. The question is whether the meat can be eaten (i.e., is it halal? Or more precisely, can we trust the servant's statement that the meat is from a permissible source? The ruling: it is permissible (yasi'u akaluhu). The reasoning: the statement of a non-Muslim is accepted in transactions because it is a reliable report (khabar sahih) — it emanates from someone who has reason (aql) and a religion (din) that holds lying to be forbidden. Moreover, there is a pressing need (haja) to accept such reports because transactions occur frequently and we cannot always verify the source. This ruling is based on the principle that in mu'amalat (transactions), the statements of all people, including non-Muslims, are prima facie accepted unless there is evidence of dishonesty. The Hanafi school applies this principle to avoid hardship.

Key Terms
خبر صحيح (khabar sahih): A report that is considered reliable because the reporter has the capacity (reason) and a religious incentive not to lie.
مقبول فى المعاملات (maqbul fi al-mu'amalat): Accepted in transactional matters; the statement is taken as true without requiring external verification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Sagheer, what is the ruling on eating meat purchased by a Majusi servant who claims he bought it from a Muslim?
A) It is not permissible because the servant is a non-Muslim.
B) It is permissible because the report of a non-Muslim is accepted in transactions.
C) It is permissible only if the servant is known to be truthful.
D) It is not permissible until a Muslim witness confirms.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the report of a non-Muslim in transactions based on the concepts of khabar sahih, rationality, religious deterrence, and necessity (haja).

Accepting the Word of Slaves, Maid-Servants, and Children in Gifts and Permission
Ruling with proof on accepting statements of slaves, maids, and children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting the word of slaves, maid-servants, and children in matters of gifts and permission, and explain the custom-based (urf) and hardship (haraj) proofs that support it.

Core Idea
To avoid hardship, Hanafis accept the word of slaves, maids, and children for gifts and permission based on custom.

Imagine a child sent to buy snacks or a maid carrying a gift. Can you trust their word? The Hanafi school says yes, but only in specific contexts—gifts and permission—to avoid everyday hardship. This rule is rooted in custom (urf) and the principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and the acts
The passage specifies three categories: slaves (abd), maid-servants (jariya), and children (sabi). The acts are accepting a gift (hadiya) and granting permission (idhn) for entry or transactions. Start by noting these exactly as given.
The ruling does not extend to all statements from these persons—only those concerning gifts and permission.
2
Locate the proofs: custom and hardship
The text gives two proofs: first, 'urf (custom) that gifts are carried by such persons; second, hardship if their word were rejected, as they cannot always produce witnesses. Distil these proofs from the Arabic: 'li-anna al-hadaya tub'athu 'alayhim' and 'yuddi ila al-haraj'.
These proofs are aqli (rational) not naqli (textual), based on social reality.
3
Apply to the specific case of the maid as gift
From al-Jami' al-Saghir: if a maid says her master sent her as a gift, her word is accepted whether the gift is herself or another item. No difference. Note the ruling's scope includes self-gifting (hiba of the person).
This case is cited separately to emphasize that the ruling covers both corporeal and personal gifts.
4
Expand to other scenarios from Durr and Shami
The commentary adds: a child reporting permission to enter, or a child buying food with coins from parents—their word is accepted. These are applications of the same principle to avoid hardship.
The later authorities confirm and extend the earlier rulings, showing continuity in Hanafi fatwa.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position and its limits
The ruling is mubah (permissible to accept) and is from Zahir al-Riwayah. Conflict: other schools might require witnesses, but Hanafis rely on custom. Note that the mufta bihi is as stated.
This is a mukhtalaf fih issue but the tarjih is clear due to necessity.

Judgment on accepting the report of a slave, maid-servant, and child regarding gift and permission. He said: It is permissible to accept in gift and permission the word of the slave, maid-servant, and child, because gifts are customarily sent by their hands. Similarly, they cannot take witnesses with them for permission when traveling in the land and trading in the market. So if their word were not accepted, it would lead to hardship. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: When a maid-servant says to a man, 'My master sent me to you as a gift,' it is permissible for him to take her, because there is no difference between her reporting that the master gifted someone else or herself, due to the reason we mentioned. Translation: Al-Quduri said: It is permissible to accept in gift and permission the word of a slave, maid-servant, and child, because gifts are customarily sent by their hands. Similarly, they cannot keep witnesses with them for permission when traveling in the land and trading in the market. So if their word were not accepted, it would lead to hardship. In al-Jami' al-Saghir: When a maid-servant says to a man, 'My master sent me to you as a gift,' it is permissible for him to take her, because there is no difference between her reporting that the master gifted someone else or herself, due to the reason we mentioned. Explanation: A child, slave, or maid-servant bring a gift saying, 'My master or father sent it,' or they go to the market to buy something saying, 'We have permission to buy and sell,' then their word is accepted, because custom is that gifts are sent by their hands, and it is not possible for them to carry witnesses of permission everywhere. So if their word were not considered, great hardship would follow. Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: When a maid-servant says to a man, 'My master sent me to you as a gift,' her word is accepted and it is permissible to keep her. The proof is the same as mentioned, and there is no difference between the master sending something else or sending the maid-servant herself as a gift. Note: If someone knocks on a door and asks for permission to enter, and a child comes and conveys permission, his word is accepted. From Durr al-Mukhtar, vol. 5, p. 220. Note: A small child goes to the market to buy food and drink for himself; it is permissible to hand it over to him, because nowadays the common custom is that parents give them some coins to buy and eat, so this is permission. See Shami, vol. 5, p. 220.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kitab al-Karahiyah regarding acceptance of statements from slaves, maid-servants, and children in the context of gifts (hadiya) and permission (idhn). The ruling: Their word is accepted in these matters because it is customary for them to be the carriers of gifts and to act on permission. The proof is based on 'urf (custom) and hardship (haraj) — if their word were not accepted, people would face difficulty since they cannot always bring witnesses. The text also cites a specific case from al-Jami' al-Saghir where a maid-servant herself is sent as a gift; her word is accepted, and the recipient may keep her. This applies whether the master sent another item or the maid herself. Additionally, the author notes that a child's report of permission to enter a house or to buy food in the market is accepted due to prevailing custom. The authority weight is from the Hanafi mutun and later commentaries.

Key Terms
ہدیہ (hadiya): A gift, present, either an item or a person (e.g., a slave girl) given by a master.
اذن (idhn): Permission, especially from a master or parent for a slave or child to engage in transactions or actions.

Touching a Slave Woman When Buying
Refinement of a permissive ruling by later scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on touching and looking at a slave woman when purchasing, and identify the condition that differentiates permissibility.

Core Idea
When buying a slave woman, looking is always allowed; touching is only allowed if no desire is present.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the permissibility of touching a slave woman during a purchase. The earlier texts (Mukhtasar, Jami' al-Saghir) gave an absolute permission, but later scholars refined it based on the presence of desire. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of interaction with non-mahram women in commercial contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Read the passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and al-Jami' al-Saghir. They state that touching is permissible without any qualification.
2
Understand the later refinement
The masha'ikh (later scholars) introduced a distinction: looking is always permissible due to necessity, but touching is only allowed when desire is absent.
3
Distinguish looking from touching
Note that looking is given broader latitude because it is necessary for inspection, whereas touching carries the risk of pleasure (istimta').
4
Apply the conditions
Apply the rule to two scenarios: (a) buyer has desire – touching impermissible, looking permissible; (b) buyer has no desire – both permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا باس بان يمس ذلك اذا اراد الشراء وان خاف ان يشتهي كذا ذكر فى المختصر واطلق ايضا في الجامع الصغير ولم يفصل قال مشائخنا رحمهم الله يباح النظر في هذه الحالة وان اشتهى للضرورة ولا يباح المس اذا اشتهى او کان اکبر رائه ذلك لانه نوع استمتاع وفى غير حالة الشراء يباح النظر والمس بشرط عدم الشهوة
He (al-Quduri) said: There is no harm in touching that (i.e., the permissible parts) when he intends to buy, even if he fears he may desire. Thus it is mentioned in al-Mukhtasar, and it is also stated absolutely in al-Jami' al-Saghir without detail. Our scholars (may Allah have mercy on them) said: Looking is permissible in this situation even if he desires, due to necessity, but touching is not permissible if he desires or if his predominant opinion is that (he will desire), because it is a type of enjoyment. And in other than the case of purchase, looking and touching are permissible on condition of absence of desire.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on touching a slave woman when one intends to buy her. The base text from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar states that it is permissible to touch the permissible areas (as defined earlier) even if the buyer fears he might feel desire. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, the ruling is mentioned absolutely without qualification. However, the later scholars (masha'ikh) of the Hanafi school elaborated: looking is permissible in this situation even if desire is present, due to the necessity of inspection for purchase. But touching is only permissible if there is no desire; if desire is present or the buyer's predominant opinion is that desire will arise, then touching is not permissible because it constitutes enjoyment (istimta'), which is not necessary. In other situations (not buying), both looking and touching are permissible only on condition of no desire. Thus, the ruling is nuanced: necessity allows looking despite desire, but touching is more restricted.

Key Terms
مس (mass): Touching with the hand.
استمتاع (istimta'): Enjoyment or pleasure; here, touching that leads to sexual arousal.
اشتهى (ishtaha): To desire sexually; in this context, to feel arousal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Always, even if desire is present
B) Only if the buyer has no desire or his predominant opinion is that he will not desire
C) Only if the seller allows it
D) Never permissible

Key Takeaway
When buying a slave woman, looking is always permitted due to necessity, but touching is only permitted when desire is absent.

Presenting a Baligha Slave-Girl for Sale in One Garment
Explains that a baligha slave-girl must not be displayed in only one garment when selling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on presenting a baligha slave in a single izar and identify the conditions that trigger the prohibition.

Core Idea
A baligha slave must not be shown in only one garment; her back and belly are 'awrah and must be covered.

In the Hanafi school, the covering requirements for a female slave change upon puberty or desirability. This lesson examines a specific ruling from al-Hidayah: when presenting a female slave for sale, she must be modestly covered. The matn states that a baligha slave should not be displayed in a single izar because her back and belly are considered 'awrah. Imam Muhammad adds that if she is fit for intercourse, she is treated like a baligha even before menstruation. Understanding this ruling clarifies the school's emphasis on modesty in trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is presenting a female slave for sale. The matn states it is not permissible to present a baligha slave in a single garment. The ruling is makruh tahrimi (prohibited, close to haram).
2
Determine the trigger
The trigger is puberty (baligha) indicated by menstruation. Imam Muhammad adds an additional trigger: being fit for intercourse (desirable and can be copulated with).
This extends the ruling to cover more cases.
3
Identify the reason
The reason is that her back and belly are considered 'awrah. In Hanafi fiqh, the 'awrah of a female slave is normally from navel to knee, but when she is baligha or desirable, the back and belly become 'awrah for the purpose of sale presentation to avoid fitnah.
This is specific to the context of display for sale.
4
Determine the required covering
She must be covered with an izar (lower garment) and a shirt (qamis) over it to cover the back and belly.
Simply wearing an izar alone is insufficient.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a merchant with a young slave girl who is physically mature but has not menstruated, the ruling from Imam Muhammad applies: she is treated as baligha and must be covered accordingly.
This shows the scope of the ruling beyond explicit puberty.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالغہ باندی کو بوقت فروخت ایک ازار میں نہ لے جائے قال واذا حاضت الامة لم تعرض فى ازار واحد ومعناه بلغت وهذا لما بينا ان الظهر والبطن منها عورة وعن محمد انها اذا كانت تشتهى و تجامع مثلها فهى كالبالغة لاتعرض فى ازار واحد لوجود الاشتهاء. ترجمہ محمد نے ( جامع صغیر میں ) فرمایا ہے اور جب باندی بالغہ ہو جائے تو ایک ازار میں پیش نہ کی جائے اور اس کے معنی بلغت کے ہیں اور یہ اس دلیل کی وجہت ہے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ اس کی پیٹھ اور پیٹ عورت ہے اور محمد سے منقول ہے کہ باندی جب کہ قابل شہوت ہو اور اس کے مثل سے جماع کیا جا سکتا ہے تو وہ بالغہ کے مثل ہے اشتہاء کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے وہ ایک ازار میں پیش نہیں کی جائے گی۔ تشریح باندی کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ عورت ہے لہذا جب وہ بالغ ہو جائے تو اس کو منڈی میں جب فروخت کرنے کے لئے جائے تو ایک ازار میں نہ لے جائے بلکہ اس کے اوپر قمیص ڈالے تا کہ اس کا پیٹ اور پیٹھ چھپ جائے ، یعنی فقط اس ایک کپڑے میں نہ لے جائے جس سے صرف مادون السرة الى الركبة چھپے ہوئے ہوں اور باقی بدن کھلا ہوا اور جب وہ جماع کے قابل ہوگئی تو وہ بالغہ کے حکم میں ہے۔ تفصیل کے لئے ملاحظہ ہو شامی ص ۲۳۶ ج ۵ -
He said: And when the female slave menstruates, she should not be displayed in one garment – meaning she has reached puberty. This is due to what we have explained: that her back and belly are 'awrah. And it is narrated from Muhammad that if she is desired and one like her is copulated with, then she is like a baligha and should not be displayed in one garment due to the presence of desire. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And when a female slave reaches puberty, she should not be presented in one garment. And the meaning is that she has reached puberty. And this is due to the proof we have stated: that her back and belly are 'awrah. And it is narrated from Muhammad that if a female slave is desirable and can be copulated with, then she is like a baligha and will not be presented in one garment due to the presence of desire. Explanation: The belly and back of a female slave are 'awrah. Therefore, when she reaches puberty, when she is taken to the market for sale, do not take her in only one garment, but put a shirt over her so that her belly and back are covered. That is, do not take her in only one garment that covers only from below the navel to the knee, leaving the rest of the body uncovered. And when she becomes fit for intercourse, she is in the ruling of a baligha. For details, see Shami vol.5 p.236.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage deals with the proper presentation of a female slave for sale. The matn states that a menstruating (i.e., baligha) slave should not be displayed in a single garment (izar). The commentator explains that this is because her back and belly are considered 'awrah. Imam Muhammad adds that even if she has not menstruated but is fit for intercourse (i.e., desirable and can be copulated with), she is treated like a baligha. The explanation clarifies that when taking a slave girl to the market, she must be covered with a shirt over the izar to conceal her belly and back. This additional covering is necessary to avoid fitnah. The ruling underscores the importance of modesty in commercial transactions involving female slaves.

Key Terms
عورت (awrat): parts of the body that must be covered in front of non-mahram
ازار (izar): a lower garment covering from waist to below knees
بالغہ (baligha): a female who has reached puberty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A baligha slave-girl must be covered with more than a single izar when presented for sale; her back and belly must be concealed.

Istibra' Requires Both Ownership and Possession
Rulings on istibra' when ownership exists but possession is incomplete

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school requires a second menstruation after possession even if the womb was known empty, and apply the ruling to scenarios involving incomplete acquisition.

Core Idea
Istibra' is wajib only after complete acquisition—both ownership and possession—not earlier.

This passage addresses a key question: does a slave girl's menstruation or childbirth before physical possession fulfill the requirement of istibra'? The Hanafi school insists that the cause ('illa) of istibra' is the full acquisition of both milk and yad. Therefore, any indication of emptiness before possession is legally irrelevant. We will explore the text's application of this principle and the disagreement of Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? (istibra') What is the hukm? (wajib) Note the conditions that trigger this obligation.
2
Locate the cause ('illa)
The text states the cause is acquisition of both ownership and possession. Why must both be present? The ruling follows the complete cause.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
What does Imam Abu Yusuf argue? (certainty of emptiness suffices) What is the Hanafi majority response? (the cause is the new acquisition, not mere emptiness) Identify the underlying principle.
4
Apply the rule to additional cases
How does the same 'illa resolve the fuduli case and the fasid sale case? What element is missing in each?
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is operative for fatwa and why? (Majority view: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) Note the tarjih authority.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳

كتاب الكراهية
-۲- شراء یا دوسرے اسباب ملک کے بعد حیض آیا ہے لیکن ابھی تک قبضہ نہیں ہوا تھا تو یہ حیض کافی نہیں بلکہ دوسرے حیض سے استبراء واجب ہے اسلئے کہ سبب وہ ثبوت ملک اور یہ دونوں ہیں تو بغیر قبضہ کے سبب نام نہیں ہوا تو ابھی سبب اور حکم بھی ثابت نہیں ہوگا۔ -- اسباب ملک کے بعد باندی کو بچہ ہوا۔ لیکن ابھی تک قبضہ نہیں ہوا تھا تو یہ ولادت نا کافی ہے بلکہ اس کے بعد حیض سے استبراء واجب ہے۔ اس باب میں امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ رحم یقینا فارغ ہو چکا ہے تو اسی پر اکتفاء جائز ہے جیسے اگر قبل الدخول طلاق دیدی ہو تو اسی وجہ سے عدت واجب نہیں ہے تو یہاں استبراء نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ مگر ہماری دلیل وہی ہے جو بار ہا گذر چکی ہے کہ وجوب استبراء کا سبب استحداث ملک وید ہے اور حکم سبب کے بعد آیا کرتا ہے نہ کہ سبب سے پہلے ۔ ۴- ایک فضولی نے کسی کیلئے باندی خریدی تو یہ بیچ اصیل کی اجازت پر موقوف ہے ابھی تک اصیل نے اجازت نہیں دی تھی کہ باندی کو حیض آگیا تو یہ حیض کافی نہیں ہے اسی دلیل سابق سے اور اگر یہ باندی پہلے سے اصیل کے قبضہ میں ہو تب بھی یہی حکم ہے کیونکہ وہ قبضہ امانت کا تھا یا اجازت وغیرہ کا۔ -۵- زید نے ایک باندی نشراء فاسد کے ساتھ خریدی اور اس کو حیض آگیا پھر زید نے از سرنوشراء صحیح کے ساتھ اس باندی کوخریدا تو پہلا حیض کافی نہیں بلکہ دوسرے حیض سے استبراء واجب ہے اسی دلیل سابق سے۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 13. On the Book of Disliked Acts. -2- A slave girl menstruates after purchase or other means of ownership but before possession has been taken. This menstruation is not sufficient; rather, istibra' is wajib through a second menstruation because the cause is the establishment of ownership and possession. Without possession, the cause is not complete, so the cause and ruling are not established. -- After the cause of ownership, the slave gives birth, but possession has not been taken. This birth is not sufficient; rather, istibra' is wajib through a subsequent menstruation. In this chapter, Imam Abu Yusuf says: When it is known that the womb is definitely empty, relying on this is permissible, just as if divorce occurred before consummation, for which 'iddah is not required; thus, istibra' should not be required here. But our proof is what has been repeatedly stated: the cause of the obligation of istibra' is the acquisition of ownership and possession, and the ruling comes after the cause, not before it. 4- A fuduli bought a slave girl for someone; this sale is suspended on the principal's permission. The principal has not yet permitted, and the slave menstruates. This menstruation is not sufficient, by the same proof. And if the slave was already in the principal's possession, the same ruling applies because that possession was for trust or permission, etc. 5- Zayd bought a slave girl through an invalid sale, and she menstruated. Then Zayd bought the same slave girl anew through a valid sale. The first menstruation is not sufficient; rather, istibra' is wajib through a second menstruation, by the same previous proof.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute. It establishes that the obligation of istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle to ensure a slave girl's womb is empty) is contingent upon both ownership (milk) and possession (yad). The text first addresses three scenarios: (1) a slave girl menstruates after ownership transfer but before physical possession — that menstruation does not fulfill istibra'; rather, a second menstruation after possession is required. (2) Similarly, if she gives birth before possession, that birth does not count; post-possession menstruation is needed. (3) The proof is that the cause ('illa) of istibra' is the acquisition of both milk and yad; the ruling follows the complete cause. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees: if the womb is known empty, istibra' is unnecessary, analogous to divorce before consummation. The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) maintain that istibra' is wajib regardless, because the cause is the new acquisition, not mere emptiness. The text then applies this principle to two additional cases: a fuduli (unauthorized agent) buying a slave — the purchase is suspended on the principal's permission; any menstruation before permission does not count because possession and definitive ownership are absent. Even if the slave was already in the principal's possession as a trust, that possession does not suffice for istibra' since it is not the new acquisition. Finally, an invalid sale followed by a valid sale: the first menstruation (during the invalid sale) is not counted; only the menstruation after the valid sale (with complete cause) qualifies.

Key Terms
استحداث ملک وید (istihdaath al-milk wa al-yad): The acquisition of both ownership (milk) and physical possession (yad) as a combined cause for istibra'.
استبراء (istibra'): Waiting for one menstrual period to ensure a slave girl's womb is empty before sexual intercourse.
فضولی (fuduli): A person who acts without authorization on behalf of another.
شراء فاسد (shira' fasid): An invalid sale that is defective in some condition (e.g., unknown price) but not fundamentally void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave girl is purchased via an invalid sale, then later purchased via a valid sale. She menstruates during the invalid sale period and again after the valid sale with possession. Which menstruation fulfills istibra'?
A) The first menstruation during the invalid sale.
B) The second menstruation after the valid sale and possession.
C) Either one suffices.
D) Neither suffices; a third menstruation is required.

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is wajib only after the complete cause of ownership and possession is established; prior signs of emptiness do not suffice.

Istibra' When Barriers Are Lifted: Majusiyya, Mukataba, and Partial Ownership
Ruling on istibra' with causal reasoning and three case examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istibra' when a temporary barrier to intercourse exists, and apply the principle that the ruling is attributed to the complete cause.

Core Idea
Istibra' is judged by the presence of the complete cause, not by temporary barriers.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in Hanafi fiqh: when a man acquires full ownership of a slave girl after having a share, or when the slave girl is a Majusiyya or a mukataba. The key legal insight is that the obligation of istibra' attaches to the complete acquisition of milk and yad. Temporary barriers that prohibit intercourse—such as disbelief or the kitabah contract—do not invalidate the istibra' already performed. We will explore how the principle 'al-hukm yudaf ila tamam al-illa' governs these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal cause (sabab) for istibra'
Istibra' becomes wajib when the buyer acquires complete ownership and physical possession (milk and yad) of the slave girl. This is the completed cause.
Partial ownership does not trigger the obligation; only full acquisition completes the cause.
2
Distinguish the cause from preventive factors (mawani')
The cause may be present even if a separate factor temporarily blocks the permissibility of intercourse. Examples include the slave's religion (Majusiyya) or a kitabah contract.
The barrier does not affect the validity of the cause; it only delays the permissibility of the effect.
3
Apply to the three scenarios in the text
Analyze each case: (1) partial ownership then full purchase—only menstruation after full purchase counts; (2) Majusiyya slave menstruates then converts—the menstruation after purchase suffices; (3) mukataba slave menstruates then fails to pay—the menstruation during kitabah suffices.
In all cases, the barrier was removed after the menstruation, but the cause was complete at the time of menstruation.
4
Extract the general principle
The ruling (istibra') is attributed to the complete cause. Once the cause is present, subsequent changes in permissibility do not require repeating the istibra'.
This principle can be extended to other areas where a legal effect is linked to a cause.

Source Text
