اس باندی میں استبراء واجب ہے، جس میں مشتری کا کچھ حصہ ہو پھر وہ باقی خریدے
ويجب في جارية للمشترى فيها شقص فاشترى الباقى لان السبب قد تم الآن والحكم يضاف الى تمام العلة ويجتزاً بالحيضة التى حاضتها بعد القبض وهى مجوسية او مكاتبه بان كاتبها بعد الشراء ثم اسلمت المجوسية اوعجزت المكاتبة لوجودها بعد السبب وهو استحداث الملك واليد اذهو مقتض للحل والحرمة لمانع كما فى حالة الحيض.
ترجمہ اور استبراء واجب ہے اس باندی میں کہ مشتری کا اس میں کچھ حصہ ہو پھر وہ باقی کو خریدے اسلئے کہ سبب اب پورا ہوا ہے اور حکم کی اضافت پوری علت کی جانب ہوتی ہے اور اکتفاء کیا جائے گا اس حیض پر جو باندی کو آیا ہے قبضہ کے بعد حالانکہ وہ مجوسیہ ہے یا مکاتبہ ہے اس طریقہ پر کہ اس کو مولیٰ نے مکاتبہ بنا دیا ہو شراء کے بعد پھر مجوسیہ مسلمان ہو گئی یا مکاتبہ عاجز ہوگئی ہو حیض کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے سبب کے بعد اور سبب ملک اور ید کا استحداث ہے اسلئے کہ سبب علت کو مقتضی ہے اور حرمت ایک مانع کی وجہ سے ہے جیسے حیض کی حالت میں ۔
تشریح اگر باندی میں زید کا کچھ حصہ وہ تو ابھی زید کیلئے جائز نہیں کہ اس سے وطی کرے۔ کیونکہ ابھی سبب نام نہیں ہے پھر زید نے باقی کو خرید لیا تو اب سبب تام ہوا ہے اس کے بعد والے حیض سے استبراء واجب ہے اس سے پہلے جو حیض گذرا ہے اس سے استبراء حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔
زید نے ایک باندی خریدی جو مجوسیہ ہے پھر اس کو ایک حیض آگیا کہ وہ مسلمان ہوگئی تو جو حیض گذر چکا ہے اس سے استبراء ہو گیا کیونکہ وہ حیض استحداث ملک وید کے بعد آیا ہے وہ دوسری بات تھی کہ اس کے مجوسیہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اس کیلئے اس سے ولی جائز نہیں
كتاب الكراهية
۵۴
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۳
تھی۔ جیسے اپنی بیوی سے حالت حیض میں وطی جائز نہیں ہوتی تو استحداث ملک و ید ولی کو حلال کرنے والا ہے مگر یہاں ایک مانع کی وجہ سے حلت نہیں ہوئی تھی اب وہ مانع زائل ہو گیا اور وہ مسلمان ہو گئی تو اب وطی جائز ہوگئی اسی طرح زید نے ایک باندی خریدی اور اس کو مکاتبہ بنا دیا اسی کے دوران اس کو حیض آگیا پھر اس نے بدل کتابت کو ادا کرنے سے اپنی عاجزی ظاہر کر کے عقد کتابت کو فسخ کر دیا تو مولی کیلئے جائز ہے کہ اس سے وطی کرے اور جدید استبراء نہ کرائے ۔ کیونکہ جو حیض مکاتبہ ہونے کی صورت میں آچکا ہے وہ استحداث ملک وید کے بعد آیا ہے تو ایک مانع کی وجہ سے ولی حلال نہیں تھی اور وہ اس کا مکاتبہ ہونا تھا اب وہ مانع زائل ہو گیا اور وطی جائز ہوگئی ۔
خلاصہ کلام مکاتبہ اور مجوسیہ کا اس باب میں ایک ہی حکم ہے۔
Istibra' is wajib for a slave girl in which the buyer had a share and then he bought the rest. The Arabic matn: It is incumbent to perform istibra' for a slave girl in whom the buyer had a share and then he bought the rest, because the cause has now been completed, and the ruling is attributed to the complete cause. The menstruation that she experienced after possession is sufficient, even if she is a Majusiyya or a mukataba, in the sense that he made her a mukataba after purchase, then the Majusiyya converted to Islam or the mukataba became incapable (of paying the kitabah). This is because the menstruation occurred after the cause, which is the acquisition of ownership and possession. For this cause is the effective factor for permissibility, and prohibition is due to a preventive factor, as in the case of menstruation. Commentary: If Zayd has a share in the slave girl, it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her because the cause is not yet complete. Then Zayd buys the remaining share; now the cause is complete. Istibra' is wajib from the menstruation that occurs after that. The previous menstruation does not fulfill istibra'. Zayd bought a slave girl who was a Majusiyya. Then she had a menstruation and then converted to Islam. That menstruation fulfills istibra' because it occurred after the acquisition of ownership and possession. It is a separate matter that intercourse was not permissible due to her being a Majusiyya. Just as it is not permissible to have intercourse with one's wife during menstruation, similarly, the acquisition of ownership and possession is what makes intercourse permissible, but here it was not permitted due to a preventive factor. When the preventive factor was removed and she became Muslim, then intercourse became permissible. Similarly, Zayd bought a slave girl and made her a mukataba. Meanwhile, she menstruated. Then she showed inability to pay the kitabah and the contract of kitabah was annulled. It is then permissible for the master to have intercourse with her without performing a new istibra'. Because that menstruation occurred after the acquisition of ownership and possession, but intercourse was not halal due to the preventive factor of the kitabah. When that preventive factor was removed, intercourse became permissible. Summary: The ruling for the mukataba and the Majusiyya is the same in this chapter.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling with proof from the Arabic matn followed by Urdu commentary. It addresses three scenarios. First: a man buys a share in a slave girl (e.g., he co-owns her) and then later buys the remaining share. The cause for istibra' is the complete acquisition of ownership and possession, which is only fulfilled when he owns the entire slave and takes possession. Any menstruation that occurred before the purchase of the remaining share does not count. Only the menstruation after the complete acquisition suffices. Second: a man buys a Majusiyya (Zoroastrian) slave girl. She menstruates after possession and then converts to Islam. The menstruation is valid for istibra' even though intercourse was initially prohibited due to her religion (a preventive factor). The prohibition was not because of incomplete cause; the cause (ownership and possession) was complete from the start, but a preventive barrier (mujib) existed. When she converts, the barrier lifts and intercourse becomes halal without a new istibra'. Third: a slave is made a mukataba (contracting for freedom) after purchase. She menstruates during the period of kitabah. Afterwards, she fails to pay and the contract is annulled. The menstruation during kitabah counts for istibra' because the cause (acquisition) was already complete. The kitabah was a preventive factor that made intercourse impossible. When the kitabah is annulled, intercourse is permissible without repeating istibra'. The summary equates the ruling for Majusiyya and mukataba: both are cases where the cause exists but a temporary preventive factor blocks permissibility; once the factor is removed, the previous istibra' remains valid.

Key Terms
شقص (shiqs): A share or portion of a slave girl.
مجوسیہ (majusiyya): A Zoroastrian female slave.
مکاتبہ (mukataba): A female slave who has a written contract (kitabah) to earn her freedom by paying installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man buys a slave girl and makes her a mukataba. She menstruates after the kitabah contract. Later, she fails to pay and the contract is annulled. Does the master need to perform a new istibra' before intercourse?
A) Yes, because the kitabah invalidated the previous istibra'.
B) No, because the menstruation occurred after the cause (ownership) was complete, and the kitabah was only a preventive factor.
C) Yes, because the annulment of kitabah is a new event requiring a fresh start.
D) No, but only if the menstruation occurred before the kitabah.

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is wajib based on the complete cause of acquisition; temporary barriers do not require repeating it.

Istibra' Not Required for Returned Runaway, Usurped, Leased, or Pawned Slave
Ruling that istibra' is not wajib for returned slaves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that istibra' is not wajib when a slave returns from specific situations and explain why the cause of new acquisition is absent.

Core Idea
Istibra' requires new acquisition; no new acquisition, no istibra'. Possibility of intercourse is irrelevant.

This passage clarifies a key exception to the general rule that istibra' is wajib upon acquiring a female slave. When a slave girl returns to her original owner after running away, being usurped, leased, or pawned, the owner does not need to observe istibra', even if there is a genuine possibility that someone else had intercourse with her while she was away. The text explains the underlying legal cause (sabab) and how it governs the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening sentence: istibra' is not wajib in four cases: runaway, usurped, leased, and pawned slave returning to the owner.
The ruling is a negation of obligation.
2
Locate the Cause (Sabab)
Find the phrase 'li'idam al-sabab' and note that the cause is 'istihdaath al-milk wa al-yad' (new acquisition of ownership and possession).
The cause is specific (mut'ayyin) and singular.
3
Apply the Cause to Each Case
For each of the four cases, confirm that the owner never lost ownership; hence, no new acquisition occurs. Even if the slave was physically absent, ownership remained with the original owner.
Runaway: ownership unchanged. Usurped: possession wrongfully taken, but ownership remains. Leased: lease transfers only usufruct. Pawned: pawnor retains ownership.
4
Extract the General Principle
The author states 'yaduru al-hukm 'alayhi wujoodan wa 'adaman' – the ruling revolves around the cause. Use this to articulate that when the cause exists, the ruling applies; when it is absent, the ruling is absent.
This is a core Hanafi legal maxim: al-hukm yaduru ma'a al-'illah wujoodan wa 'adaman.
5
Contrast with Cases Where Istibra' Is Wajib
Consider a purchase or a gift of a female slave – here, the owner acquires her for the first time, so istibra' is wajib. This contrast reinforces the centrality of the cause.
Review earlier lessons on istibra' if needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولا يجب الاستبراء اذا رجعت الابقة اوردت المغصوبة او المواجرة او فكت المرهونة لانعدام السبب وهو استحداث الملك واليدوهو سبب متعين فادير الحكم عليه وجودا وعدما ولها نظائر كثيرة كتبنا ها في كفاية المنتهى

کسی نے اپنی باندی کسی دوسرے کو اجارہ پر دی پھر مستاجر نے اس کو واپس کر دیا تو اگر چه احتمال ہے کہ متاجر نے اس باندی کے ساتھ ولی حرام کر لی ہو اس کے باوجود مولی پر استبراء واجب نہیں ہے۔ کسی نے اپنی باندی گروی رکھی پر قرض اداء کر کے چھڑالی گئی تو اگر چہ اس میں احتمال ہے کہ جس کے پاس رکھی گئی تھی اس نے اس سے وطی کرلی ہو اس کے باوجود مولی پر استبراء واجب نہیں کیونکہ استبراء کا سبب ایک ہی متعین ہے یعنی استحداث ملک وید اور یہ یہاں مقصود ہے کیونکہ وہ پہلے ہی سے اس کی ملکیت میں ہے تو سبب نہیں پایا گیا لہذا حکم بھی نہیں پایا جائے گا کیونکہ جب سبب ہوگا تو حکم ہوگا اور جب سب نہ ہوگا تو حکم بھی نہ ہو گا اس کو مصنف نے قادير الحكم عليه وجوداً او عدما “ سے تعبیر کیا ہے۔
If a runaway slave returns, istibra' is not incumbent. The Arabic matn: Istibra' is not required when the runaway slave returns, or the usurped slave is returned, or the leased slave is returned, or the pawned slave is redeemed, due to the absence of the cause, which is the acquisition of ownership and possession. And it is a specific cause, so the ruling revolves around it in terms of existence and non-existence. There are many parallels to this, which we have written in Kifayat al-Muntaha. Commentary: A slave girl had run away and then returned to her master. Even if there is a possibility that someone had intercourse with her, istibra' is not wajib. If someone usurped another's slave girl and then returned her, even if there is a possibility that the usurper or someone else had intercourse with her, istibra' is not incumbent upon the master. If someone gave his slave girl on lease to another and the lessee returned her, even if there is a possibility that the lessee had unlawful intercourse with her, istibra' is not wajib. If someone pawned his slave girl, and after repaying the debt she is redeemed, even if there is a possibility that the pawnholder had intercourse with her, istibra' is not wajib because the cause of istibra' is a single specific thing: the acquisition of ownership and possession. And here the intended [cause] is absent because she has been in his ownership from before. So the cause is not found, and thus the ruling is not found either. For when the cause exists, the ruling exists; when the cause does not exist, the ruling does not exist. The author expressed this by saying 'the ruling revolves around it in existence and non-existence'.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof stating that istibra' is not required when a slave girl returns to her original owner after a period of absence, regardless of potential impurity. The cause ('illa) for istibra' is the acquisition of ownership and possession (istihdaath al-milk wa al-yad). In the four cases given—runaway, usurped, leased, and pawned—the slave already belongs to the master; there is no new acquisition. Therefore, the cause is absent, and istibra' is not wajib, even though there is a possibility that someone else had intercourse with her during the absence. The Arabic matn emphasizes that the cause is specific and the ruling is contingent on its existence. The commentary elaborates on each case and concludes with the general principle: when the cause exists, the ruling exists; when it does not, the ruling does not. This is consistent with the earlier rulings that istibra' is only for new acquisitions.

Key Terms
الابقة (al-abiqah): The runaway female slave.
مغصوبة (maghsubah): Usurped property; a slave taken wrongfully.
مواجرة (muajara): A slave given on lease (ijara).
مرهونة (marhunah): A slave given as pawn/pledge (rahn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because of the possibility of pregnancy.
B) No, because there is no new acquisition of ownership.
C) Yes, but only if she menstruates after return.
D) No, unless the owner purchased her again.

Key Takeaway
Istibra' is only wajib when there is a new acquisition of ownership and possession; its absence renders the obligation null, regardless of potential impurity.

Prohibition of Intercourse and Preludes Before Completing Istibra'
Ruling statement on prohibition of intercourse and its means before istibra' is completed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the prohibition of intercourse and its preludes before completing istibra', and explain the underlying principle of sadd al-dhara'i'.

Core Idea
Intercourse and its preludes are prohibited before istibra' is complete — means to haram are haram.

This passage from the Hidayah matn establishes a key precautionary rule in Hanafi fiqh: once a man acquires a slave girl and istibra' becomes obligatory, sexual relations and any actions leading to them are forbidden until istibra' is completed. The reasoning is that the means to a prohibited act are themselves prohibited, a principle known as sadd al-dhara'i'. This lesson will help you memorise and apply this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
Recognise that after acquiring a slave girl, istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle) becomes wajib (obligatory).
2
Identify the prohibited act
Direct sexual intercourse is explicitly haram during this period.
3
Identify the extension
Any actions that may lead to intercourse (dawa'i al-wat'i), such as kissing, touching with desire, etc., are also haram.
4
Understand the reason
Because these actions lead to the prohibited act or risk it occurring outside valid ownership.
5
Connect to principle
This is an application of the Hanafi legal principle sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب استبراء سے پہلے ولی اور دوائی وطی حرام ہیں
واذا ثبت وجوب الاستبراء وحرم الوطى حرم الدواعى لافضائها اليه اولا حتمال وقوعها في غير الملک
Before the obligation of istibra' becomes established, intercourse and its [؟] are prohibited. And when the obligation of istibra' is established, and intercourse is prohibited, the means leading to it are also prohibited, because they lead to it, or because of the possibility that it may occur in other than ownership.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This brief passage states a general ruling: once istibra' becomes wajib (i.e., after a new acquisition of a slave girl), direct sexual intercourse is haram, and by extension, any actions that may lead to intercourse (such as kissing, touching with desire) are also haram. The reason given is that such actions lead to the prohibited act or risk it occurring outside of valid ownership (i.e., before the slave is legally permissible through completed istibra'). This is a standard principle in Hanafi fiqh: the means to a forbidden act are also forbidden. The passage is taken from the matn and serves as a cautionary rule.

Key Terms
دوائی وطی (dawa'i al-wat'i): The means or preludes to sexual intercourse, such as kissing, touching, etc.
ولايت (wilayat): Probably a typo; context suggests 'and' (و) and 'fornication' (?) but the text is unclear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Intercourse and any action that may lead to it
C) Only actions that definitely lead to intercourse
D) Intercourse and conversations about intercourse

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits both intercourse and its preludes before istibra' is completed, applying the principle of blocking the means to evil (sadd al-dhara'i').

Medicinal Intercourse with a Captive Before Istibra'
Ruling with proof from Nawadir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on medicinal intercourse with a captive slave before istibra' according to Imam Muhammad's narration in Nawadir and explain the reasoning based on the rejection of the harbi husband's paternity claim.

Core Idea
Medicinal intercourse with a captive before istibra' is not haram because any resulting pregnancy cannot be claimed by the harbi husband.

The general rule is that intercourse with a captive slave before completing istibra' is impermissible. However, a specific exception arises for medicinal intercourse (duwa'i wati'). While the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah texts are silent on this matter, Imam Muhammad's narration in Nawadir provides a ruling based on a rational consideration that eliminates the usual concern of mixing lineages.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Establish the baseline: intercourse with a captive slave before istibra' is generally prohibited (not permissible). This is the default rule that applies to all intercourse with captives.
The prohibition aims to ensure the slave is not pregnant from a previous owner, thus preserving lineage certainty.
2
Recognize the exception
The passage raises the case of medicinal intercourse. This is intercourse performed for a medical purpose, not for pleasure. The author seeks a specific ruling for this exceptional scenario.
Medicinal intercourse is a rare but legally relevant category.
3
Locate the source of the ruling
The text states that nothing is mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad). However, a narration in Nawadir from Imam Muhammad himself declares that such intercourse is not haram.
Nawadir are rare transmissions; they carry less authority than Zahir al-Riwayah but still provide guidance.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The reasoning is rational (dalil aqli): if pregnancy occurs from medicinal intercourse, the harbi (non-Muslim enemy) husband's claim of paternity will not be recognized in Islamic law. This removes the fear of mixing lineages or uncertainty of ownership, which is the basis for requiring istibra'.
Contrast with a purchased slave-girl where the seller's claim would be heard; here the captor is not vulnerable to such claims.
5
Assess the authority weight
The ruling comes from Nawadir, not Zahir al-Riwayah. The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is not specified in this text. Therefore, a mufti would need to consider the hierarchy of sources before issuing a fatwa on this matter.
The student should recognize that a ruling from Nawadir is not automatically the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح جس عورت کو گرفتار کیا گیا اور وہ کسی مجاہد کے حصہ میں آگئی تو استبراء سے پہلے اس سے وطی کرنا جائز نہیں لیکن دوائی وطی کا کیا حکم ہے اس سلسلے میں ظاہر الرویۃہ میں کچھ مذکور نہیں ہے لیکن نوادر میں امام محمد سے منقول ہے کہ دوائی حرام نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہاں دوائی وطی میں یہ احتمال نہیں ہے کہ وہ غیر کی ملک میں واقع ہو جائیں اسلئے کہ اگر یہاں حمل بھی ظاہر ہو جائے تو اس کے حربی شوہر کا دعوی مسموع نہ ہوگا اور مشتراة میں بائع کا دعوی مقبول اور مسموع ہوگا۔ (کما مر )
Explanation: A woman who is captured and comes into the share of a mujahid, intercourse with her before istibra' is not permissible. But what is the ruling of medicinal intercourse? In this regard, nothing is mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah. However, in Nawadir, it is narrated from Imam Muhammad that medicinal intercourse is not haram, because in medicinal intercourse there is no possibility that it occurs in the ownership of another. This is because if pregnancy becomes apparent here, the claim of her harbi husband will not be heard, whereas in the case of a purchased slave-girl, the seller's claim is accepted and heard (as has passed).
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific ruling regarding a captive woman (sabiyya) who falls to a mujahid's share. Normally, intercourse before istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle to ensure no pregnancy from a previous owner) is prohibited. However, a question arises about medicinal intercourse (like treatment). The author notes that Zahir al-Riwayah is silent, but Imam Muhammad's narration in Nawadir states that medicinal intercourse is not haram. The reasoning is that if pregnancy occurs from medicinal intercourse, the harbi (non-Muslim enemy) husband's claim of paternity is not recognized in Islamic law, unlike the case of a purchased slave-girl where the seller's claim would be accepted. This removes the concern of mixing lineages, thus making it permissible.

Key Terms
استبراء (istibra'): The waiting period a female slave must observe after acquisition before intercourse, to ensure she is not pregnant from a previous owner.
دوائی وطی (duwa'i wati'): Medicinal intercourse, i.e., intercourse for a medical purpose such as treatment, not for pleasure.
نوادر (nawadir): Rare transmissions from Hanafi imams, not part of the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is haram
B) It is not haram
C) It is makruh tahrimi
D) There is no reported opinion

Key Takeaway
Medicinal intercourse with a captive before istibra' is not haram according to Nawadir, due to the invalidity of the harbi husband's paternity claim.

Using Legal Stratagems to Drop Istibra': An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hila for istibra' with conditional resolution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding using a hila to drop istibra', and apply the conditional tarjih based on whether the seller had intercourse.

Core Idea
A hila to drop istibra' is allowed only if the seller did not have intercourse; fatwa varies by knowledge.

This passage from the Hidayah addresses an intra-Hanafi conflict: may a buyer use a legal stratagem (hila) to skip the obligatory waiting period (istibra') for a newly purchased slave-girl? Imam Abu Yusuf permits it, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The resolution hinges on a factual condition: if the buyer knows that the seller never had intercourse with her in her current purity period, Abu Yusuf's view is followed; otherwise, Muhammad's stricter view applies. This shows how Hanafi fiqh balances textual obligation with practical knowledge, and how fatwa can shift based on circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is using a hila to avoid observing istibra' for a slave-girl. The dispute is between two Hanafi luminaries: Abu Yusuf permits it, Muhammad forbids it.
Istibra' is an obligation (wajib) to ensure the womb is clear; the hila aims to circumvent it.
2
Understand the condition for tarjih
The author resolves the conflict conditionally: if the buyer knows the seller did not have intercourse in that tuhur, Abu Yusuf's view is taken; if the seller did have intercourse, Muhammad's view is taken.
Tuhur means the period of purity between menses; intercourse in that period could cause pregnancy.
3
Recognise the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The ruling determines whether the buyer may legally proceed without waiting. Knowing the seller's actions is key to determining which fatwa applies.
The fatwa varies by evidence and context, not by random preference.
4
Relate to the broader principle of hila in Hanafi fiqh
Hanafis sometimes permit hilal to avoid hardship, but not if they lead to prohibition. Here, the hila is allowed only when it does not risk confusion of lineage (the purpose of istibra').
This is not a free license; it is tightly conditioned.
5
Note the source's cross-reference
The author says the proofs were given in Kitab al-Shuf'a. This reminds us that Hidayah often compresses arguments and relies on prior discussions.
If needed, one could review that section for fuller reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بأس بالاحتيال لا سقاط الاستبرأ عندابي يوسف خلافا لمحمد وقد ذكرنا الوجهين في الشفعة والماخوذ قول ابى يوسف فيما اذا علم ان البائع لم يقربها فى طهرها ذلك وقول محمد فيما اذا قربها ترجمہ حضرت مصنف نے فرمایا اور استبراء کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے حیلہ کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اختلاف ہے محمدؐ کا اور ہم نے دونوں وجہوں کو شفعہ میں ذکر کر دیا ہے اور لائق عمل ابو یوسف کا قول ہے اس صورت میں جبکہ معلوم ہو کہ بائع نے اس سے ولی نہیں کی ہے اس کے اس طہر میں اور محمد کا قول ہے اس صورت میں جبکہ اس سے وطی کی ہو۔ تفریح امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسقاط استبراء کے حیلہ میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کتاب الشفعہ میں دونوں کی دلیلیں بیان کر چکے ہیں پھر مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یہ بات معلوم ہو جائے کہ بائع نے اس باندی سے اس طہر میں وطی نہیں کی تو امام ابو یوسف کا قول لیا جائے گا اور نہ امام محمد کا مجمع الا نہر ص ۵۲۳ ج ۲ پر ہے کہ اسی تفصیل پر فتوی دیا جائے گا۔
And there is no harm in using a legal stratagem to drop istibra' according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. And we have mentioned the two views in the chapter of shuf'a. The adopted view is Abu Yusuf's when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with her in that tuhur, and Muhammad's view when he did have intercourse. (Translation) The author said: There is no harm in using a stratagem to drop istibra' according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. And we have mentioned both proofs in the chapter of shuf'a. The acceptable view is Abu Yusuf's when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with her in that tuhur, and Muhammad's view when he did have intercourse. (Explanation) Imam Abu Yusuf sees no harm in a stratagem to drop istibra', and Imam Muhammad does not permit it. The author says that both proofs have been mentioned in Kitab al-Shuf'a. Then the author says: If it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with this slave in that tuhur, then Abu Yusuf's view is taken, not Muhammad's. In Majma' al-Anhur, volume 2, page 523, it is stated that fatwa is given on this detail.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage discusses a legal stratagem (hila) to circumvent the requirement of istibra' for a slave-girl after purchase. Imam Abu Yusuf permits it, while Imam Muhammad does not. The author of the Hidayah states that the proofs for both views were mentioned in the Book of Shuf'a (Pre-emption). The resolution is based on knowledge: if the buyer knows that the seller did not have intercourse with the slave in that particular tuhur (pure period after menses), then Abu Yusuf's view (allowing the stratagem) is adopted because there is no risk of pregnancy. However, if the seller did have intercourse, then Muhammad's view (disallowing the stratagem) is taken to avoid confusion of lineage. The fatwa is given according to this detailed ruling, as confirmed by Majma' al-Anhur.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): A legal stratagem to avoid a binding obligation while technically staying within the law.
استبراء (istibra'): Waiting period for a female slave before intercourse to ensure no pregnancy.
تفصیل (tafsil): Detail; the conditional resolution based on the factual scenario.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the adopted fatwa in this passage, when is Abu Yusuf's view on dropping istibra' by a hila applied?
A) In all cases, because he is the senior disciple
B) Only when the buyer knows that the seller did not have intercourse in that tuhur
C) Only when the seller confirms he did have intercourse
D) Never, because Muhammad's view is always stronger

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school conditionally permits a hila to drop istibra' based on knowledge of the seller's actions, balancing obligation with practicality.

The Hanafi Dispute on Using a Hila to Drop Istibra'
Opening section on the permissibility of hila for istibra' and intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding using a hila to drop istibra', identify the condition that determines the mufta bihi, and apply the distinction to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf permits hila to drop istibra' only if the seller never had intercourse; otherwise, Muhammad's prohibition applies.

Istibra' is a wajib waiting period for a new master to ensure a slave girl is not pregnant from the previous owner. But can this obligation be avoided through a lawful stratagem? Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad disagreed. The author of Al-Hidayah presents their views and a condition that reconciles them: the permissibility depends on whether the seller had intercourse during the relevant purity period. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Using a legal trick (hila) to drop the requirement of istibra'. Determine the hukm level according to each imam: Abu Yusuf says permissible (la ba'sa), Muhammad says not permissible.
The act is not the trick itself but the ruling on its permissibility.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
State the two positions: Abu Yusuf permits, Muhammad prohibits. Recognize that this is a legitimate difference within the school.
The author references Kitab al-Shuf'a for the full proofs.
3
Identify the distinguishing condition
The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) depends on whether the seller had intercourse in that purity period. If it is known he did not, Abu Yusuf's view is taken; if he did, Muhammad's view applies.
This condition is crucial: it limits the permissibility to cases of certainty.
4
Trace the tarjih and authority
The author and later commentators (e.g., Majma' al-Anhar) state that the fatwa is given according to this detail. Understand that the weight of authority shifts based on the condition.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah; tarjih by author.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the seller's intercourse is uncertain, the buyer must follow Muhammad's view and not use the trick, meaning he must observe istibra'.

استبراء کے اسقاط کیلئے حیلہ کا حکم
ولا بأس بالاحتيال لإسقاط الاستبراء عند أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد، وقد ذكرنا الوجهين في الشفعة، والمأخوذ قول أبي يوسف فيما إذا علم أن البائع لم يقربها في طهرها ذلك، وقول محمد فيما إذا قربها.
ترجمہ: حضرت مصنف نے فرمایا اور استبراء کو ساقط کرنے کیلئے حیلہ کرنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے ابو یوسف کے نزدیک، خلاف ہے محمد کا، اور ہم نے دونوں وجہوں کو شفعہ میں ذکر کر دیا ہے، اور لائق عمل ابو یوسف کا قول ہے اس صورت میں جبکہ معلوم ہو کہ بائع نے اس سے وطی نہیں کی ہے اس کے اس طہر میں، اور محمد کا قول ہے اس صورت میں جبکہ اس سے وطی کی ہو۔
تفریح: امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک اسقاط استبراء کے حیلہ میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور امام محمد کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کتاب الشفعہ میں دونوں کی دلیلیں بیان کر چکے ہیں پھر مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر یہ بات معلوم ہو جائے کہ بائع نے اس باندی سے اس طہر میں وطی نہیں کی تو امام ابو یوسف کا قول لیا جائے گا اور نہ امام محمد کا۔ مجمع الانہر ص ۵۲۳ ج ۲ پر ہے کہ اسی تفصیل پر فتوی دیا جائے گا۔

پہلا حیلہ
والحيلة إذا لم تكن تحت المشتری حرة أن يتزوجها قبل الشراء ثم يشتريها
ترجمہ: اور حیلہ جب کہ مشتری کے تحت میں کوئی آزاد عورت نہ ہو یہ ہے کہ وہ اس باندی سے خریدنے سے پہلے نکاح کر لے پھر اس کو خرید لے۔
تشریح: مصنف نے یہاں دو حیلے بیان کیئے ہیں، یہ پہلا حیلہ ہے کہ اگر مشتری کے نکاح میں کوئی حرہ نہ ہو تو اس کو چاہئے کہ وہ پہلے اس باندی سے نکاح کرلے۔ پھر اس کو خریدے، خریدتے ہی نکاح ختم ہو گیا اور استبراء واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اپنی منکوحہ کوخریدنے سے استبراء واجب نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ اور نکاح میں حرہ ہونے کی قید اسلئے لگائی کہ اگر نکاح میں حرہ ہو تو پھر باندی سے نکاح جائز نہیں، اسی طرح اگر اس کے نکاح میں چار باندی ہوں تب بھی یہ حیلہ کارگر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس باندی سے نکاح جائز نہ ہوگا۔

دوسرا حیلہ
ولو كانت فالحيلة أن يزوجها البائع قبل الشراء أو المشتری قبل القبض ممن يوثق به ثم يشتريها ويقبضها أو يقبضها ثم يطلق الزوج، لأن عند وجود السبب وهو استحداث الملك المؤكد بالقبض إذا لم يكن فرجها حلالاً له لا يجب الاستبراء، وإن حل بعد ذلك لأن المعتبر إنما هو وجود السبب، كما إذا كانت معتدة الغير.
ترجمہ: اور اگر (نکاح میں حرہ) ہو تو حیلہ یہ ہے کہ بائع شراء سے پہلے اس کا نکاح کر دے یا مشتری قبضہ سے پہلے اس آدمی کے ساتھ جس پر اعتماد کیا جاتا ہو پھر مشتری اس کو خریدے اور قبضہ کرے (پہلی صورت میں) یا اس پر قبضہ کرے (دوسری صورت میں) پھر شوہر اس کو طلاق دے، اسلئے کہ سبب کے پائے جانے کے وقت اور وہ اس ملک کا استحداث ہے جو قبضہ سے مؤکد ہے، جب اس کی شرمگاہ اس کیلئے حلال نہیں تھی تو استبراء واجب نہ ہوگا، اگرچہ اس کے بعد حلال ہوگئی، اس لئے کہ معتبر سبب کے پائے جانے کا وقت ہے، جیسا کہ جبکہ وہ غیر کی معتدہ ہو۔
تشریح: یہ دوسرا حیلہ ہے کہ جس شخص پر اعتماد ہو کہ یہ اس کو طلاق دے دے گا اور اس سے وطی نہیں کرے گا تو بائع شراء سے پہلے اس سے اس کا نکاح کر دے یا مشتری قبضہ سے پہلے اس سے اس کا نکاح کر دے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں استحداث ملک وید کے وقت مشتری کیلئے اس کی شرمگاہ حلال نہیں ہے، تو مشتری پر استبراہ بھی واجب نہ ہو گا پھر اس کا شوہر اس کو طلاق دے دے، چونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول ہے اسلئے عدت بھی واجب نہ ہوگی اور نہ مولیٰ پر استبراء واجب ہو گا، اس لئے کہ استحداث ملک وید کے وقت شرمگاہ کے حلال نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے استبراء واجب نہیں ہوا تھا اور اب اسلئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ اس وقت ملک اور ید کا استحداث نہیں ہے، اور اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے کہ کسی نے ایک باندی خریدی جو کسی کی منکوحہ تھی اور اس کے شوہر نے اس کو طلاق دے دی تھی، جس کی وہ عدت گزار رہی تھی کہ مولیٰ نے اس کو فروخت کر دیا تو مشتری اس سے وطی نہیں کرے گا جب تک کہ اس کی عدت نہ گذر جائے، پھر عدت کے گزرنے کے بعد کیا مشتری پر استبراء واجب ہے؟ فرمایا کہ نہیں، کیونکہ باندی جب خریدی تھی اس وقت باندی کی شرمگاہ اس کیلئے حلال نہیں تھی
Ruling on the trick to drop istibra'. There is no harm in using a trick to drop istibra' according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. We have mentioned both aspects in Shuf'a. The taken [position] is the saying of Abu Yusuf when it is known that the seller did not approach her in that purity period, and the saying of Muhammad when he approached her. Translation: The author said: There is no harm in using a trick to drop istibra' according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, and we have mentioned both aspects in the book of Shuf'a. The acting-upon [position] is the saying of Abu Yusuf in the case when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with her in that purity period, and the saying of Muhammad when he had intercourse. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Yusuf, there is no harm in the trick to drop istibra', and according to Imam Muhammad it is not permissible. The author says that we have stated both proofs in the book of Shuf'a. Then the author says that if it becomes known that the seller did not have intercourse with that slave girl in that purity period, then the saying of Abu Yusuf is taken, not that of Imam Muhammad. In Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 523, it is said that the fatwa is given according to this detail.

First trick: And the trick, when the buyer has no free woman under him, is that he marries her before the purchase, then buys her. Translation: And the trick, when there is no free woman under the buyer, is that he marries this slave girl before buying, then buys her. Explanation: The author has stated two tricks here. This is the first trick: if the buyer has no free woman in his marriage, he should first marry this slave girl, then buy her. Upon buying, the marriage ends, and istibra' will not be obligatory because buying one's own wife does not require istibra'. The condition of having no free woman in marriage is placed because if he has a free wife, then marrying a slave girl is not permissible. Similarly, if he has four slave wives, then also this trick will not work because marrying this slave girl will not be permissible.

Second trick: And if she [a free woman] exists, then the trick is that the seller marries her before the purchase, or the buyer [marries her] before possession to someone trustworthy, then he buys her and takes possession, or takes possession, then the husband divorces her, because at the time of the existence of the cause, which is the acquisition of ownership confirmed by possession, when her private part was not lawful for him, istibra' is not obligatory, even if it becomes lawful afterwards, because consideration is only the existence of the cause, just as when she is in the idda of another. Translation: And if (there is a free woman in marriage), then the trick is that the seller marries her before the purchase, or the buyer before possession to a person who is trusted, then the buyer buys her and takes possession, or takes possession, then the husband divorces her, because when the cause exists, which is the acquisition of ownership confirmed by possession, when her private part was not lawful for him, istibra' is not obligatory, even if it becomes lawful afterwards, because consideration is only the time of existence of the cause, like when she is in the idda of another. Explanation: This is the second trick: that a person who is trusted to divorce her and not have intercourse with her, the seller marries her to him before the purchase, or the buyer before possession [marries her to him]. In both cases, at the time of acquisition of ownership and possession, her private part is not lawful for the buyer. Therefore, istibra' is not obligatory upon the buyer. Then her husband divorces her. Since the divorce is before consummation, no idda is obligatory, and no istibra' is obligatory upon the master, because at the time of acquisition of ownership and possession, due to her private part not being lawful, istibra' was not obligatory, and now it will not become obligatory because there is no new acquisition of ownership and possession. The example is exactly like someone buying a slave girl who was the wife of another and her husband divorced her, and she was observing idda, then the master sold her; the buyer will not have intercourse until her idda passes. Then after the idda passes, is istibra' obligatory upon the buyer? He said: No, because when the slave girl was bought, her private part was not lawful for him.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Karahiyah addresses the ruling on using a legal trick (hila) to drop the requirement of istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle) when purchasing a slave girl. There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Yusuf permits such a trick, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The author, al-Marghinani, states that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf, but only when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with the slave girl during the purity period in question; if he did have intercourse, then Muhammad's view (disallowing the trick) is followed. Then two specific tricks are detailed. The first trick applies when the buyer has no free wife: he may marry the slave girl before purchasing her. Upon purchase, the marriage automatically ends (since a man cannot own his wife), and since one's own wife does not require istibra', the requirement is dropped. However, if the buyer already has a free wife, he cannot marry a slave girl concurrently, so this trick fails. Similarly, if he has four slave wives, he cannot marry another slave. The second trick applies when a free wife exists: the buyer or seller marries the slave girl to a trusted third party before the purchase or before possession. The buyer then purchases and takes possession of the slave girl while she is married to someone else, so at the moment of acquiring ownership and possession, her private part is not lawful to him, hence no istibra' is required. Afterwards, the husband (the third party) divorces her before consummation, so no idda is required either. The commentator illustrates this with an analogy: if a buyer purchases a slave girl who is in the idda of another man (e.g., after divorce), he must wait for her idda, but after it ends, no istibra' is required because at the time of purchase her private part was not lawful. The key principle is that the obligation of istibra' is tied to the moment of acquiring ownership and possession; if at that moment the woman's private part is not lawful to the buyer (due to marriage to another or idda), then istibra' is not required, even if it becomes lawful later.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): A legal trick or stratagem used to achieve a permissible result by circumventing a prohibition or obligation through a lawful means.
استبراء (istibra'): The waiting period of one menstrual cycle required for a slave girl purchased by a new master to ensure she is not pregnant from the previous owner.
مشتری (mushtari): The buyer of the slave girl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi, when is it permissible to use a hila to drop istibra'?
A) Whenever the buyer wants to avoid the waiting period
B) Only when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse in that purity period
C) Only when the buyer has a free wife
D) Only if the seller sold the slave girl before the purity period ended

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of using a hila to drop istibra' is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, and the operative ruling depends on whether the seller had intercourse.

Two Specific Legal Tricks for Dropping Istibra'
Description of two hila methods for dropping istibra'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two hila methods for dropping istibra' described in Al-Hidayah, identify the conditions for each, and apply the underlying legal principle to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Both tricks work by ensuring that at the moment of ownership, the slave's private part is not halal, thus removing the basis for istibra'.

After presenting the ruling on using a hila to drop istibra', the author of Al-Hidayah provides two practical methods. The first applies when the buyer has no free wife; the second when he does. Both rely on a key principle: istibra' is not required if at the time of acquiring ownership and possession, the woman's private part is not lawful to the new owner, even if it becomes lawful later. This lesson unpacks these methods and their conditions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first scenario: buyer has no free wife
The first trick is available when the buyer has no free woman (or more than four slave wives) in his marriage. The buyer marries the slave girl before purchasing her.
A man cannot marry a slave if he has a free wife; hence the condition.
2
Detail the first trick: marry then buy
The buyer marries the slave girl, then immediately purchases her. Upon purchase, the marriage dissolves (a man cannot own his wife). At the moment of ownership, the girl is still his wife, so her private part was not halal to him at ownership (it was already halal through marriage? Wait: the trick works because at the moment of ownership, she is his wife, so her private part is already halal. But the text says buying one's own wife does not require istibra'. Actually, istibra' is not required when a man buys his own wife because he already had lawful access. So the trick works because the marriage predates ownership.
The ruling: istibra' is not required if the woman is already lawful to the buyer at ownership.
3
Identify the limitation for the first trick
This trick only works if the buyer has no free wife (or does not already have four slave wives). Otherwise, marrying the slave is not permissible, so the trick cannot be executed.
4
Understand the second scenario: buyer has a free wife
When the buyer has a free wife (or the first trick is not possible), a second trick is used: the seller or buyer marries the slave girl to a trusted third party before the purchase or before possession, then the buyer purchases and takes possession.
The third party must be trusted to divorce her without intercourse.
5
Detail the second trick: marry to a third party
The slave girl is married to a reliable person (by the seller before sale, or by the buyer before possession). The buyer then buys her and takes possession. At ownership, she is married to the third party, so her private part is not halal to the buyer. Thus no istibra' is required. Later, the husband divorces her before consummation, so no idda.
The key is that at the moment of ownership, the private part is unlawful to the buyer.
6
Analyze the general principle
Both tricks rely on the principle that istibra' is based on the cause of ownership. If at the time of ownership (ownership confirmed by possession) the woman's private part is not lawful to the man, istibra' is not required, even if it becomes lawful later. This is analogous to buying a slave girl in idda of another: at purchase, her private part is unlawful, so after her idda ends, no istibra' is required.
The principle is 'al-ibratu bi wujudi al-sabab' (consideration is the existence of the cause).

والحيلة إذا لم تكن تحت المشتری حرة أن يتزوجها قبل الشراء ثم يشتريها
ترجمہ: اور حیلہ جب کہ مشتری کے تحت میں کوئی آزاد عورت نہ ہو یہ ہے کہ وہ اس باندی سے خریدنے سے پہلے نکاح کر لے پھر اس کو خرید لے۔
تشریح: مصنف نے یہاں دو حیلے بیان کیئے ہیں، یہ پہلا حیلہ ہے کہ اگر مشتری کے نکاح میں کوئی حرہ نہ ہو تو اس کو چاہئے کہ وہ پہلے اس باندی سے نکاح کرلے۔ پھر اس کو خریدے، خریدتے ہی نکاح ختم ہو گیا اور استبراء واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اپنی منکوحہ کوخریدنے سے استبراء واجب نہیں ہوا کرتا۔ اور نکاح میں حرہ ہونے کی قید اسلئے لگائی کہ اگر نکاح میں حرہ ہو تو پھر باندی سے نکاح جائز نہیں، اسی طرح اگر اس کے نکاح میں چار باندی ہوں تب بھی یہ حیلہ کارگر نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس باندی سے نکاح جائز نہ ہوگا۔

دوسرا حیلہ
ولو كانت فالحيلة أن يزوجها البائع قبل الشراء أو المشتری قبل القبض ممن يوثق به ثم يشتريها ويقبضها أو يقبضها ثم يطلق الزوج، لأن عند وجود السبب وهو استحداث الملك المؤكد بالقبض إذا لم يكن فرجها حلالاً له لا يجب الاستبراء، وإن حل بعد ذلك لأن المعتبر إنما هو وجود السبب، كما إذا كانت معتدة الغير.
ترجمہ: اور اگر (نکاح میں حرہ) ہو تو حیلہ یہ ہے کہ بائع شراء سے پہلے اس کا نکاح کر دے یا مشتری قبضہ سے پہلے اس آدمی کے ساتھ جس پر اعتماد کیا جاتا ہو پھر مشتری اس کو خریدے اور قبضہ کرے (پہلی صورت میں) یا اس پر قبضہ کرے (دوسری صورت میں) پھر شوہر اس کو طلاق دے، اسلئے کہ سبب کے پائے جانے کے وقت اور وہ اس ملک کا استحداث ہے جو قبضہ سے مؤکد ہے، جب اس کی شرمگاہ اس کیلئے حلال نہیں تھی تو استبراء واجب نہ ہوگا، اگرچہ اس کے بعد حلال ہوگئی، اس لئے کہ معتبر سبب کے پائے جانے کا وقت ہے، جیسا کہ جبکہ وہ غیر کی معتدہ ہو۔
تشریح: یہ دوسرا حیلہ ہے کہ جس شخص پر اعتماد ہو کہ یہ اس کو طلاق دے دے گا اور اس سے وطی نہیں کرے گا تو بائع شراء سے پہلے اس سے اس کا نکاح کر دے یا مشتری قبضہ سے پہلے اس سے اس کا نکاح کر دے تو ان دونوں صورتوں میں استحداث ملک وید کے وقت مشتری کیلئے اس کی شرمگاہ حلال نہیں ہے، تو مشتری پر استبراہ بھی واجب نہ ہو گا پھر اس کا شوہر اس کو طلاق دے دے، چونکہ طلاق قبل الدخول ہے اسلئے عدت بھی واجب نہ ہوگی اور نہ مولیٰ پر استبراء واجب ہو گا، اس لئے کہ استحداث ملک وید کے وقت شرمگاہ کے حلال نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے استبراء واجب نہیں ہوا تھا اور اب اسلئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ اس وقت ملک اور ید کا استحداث نہیں ہے، اور اس کی مثال بالکل ایسی ہے کہ کسی نے ایک باندی خریدی جو کسی کی منکوحہ تھی اور اس کے شوہر نے اس کو طلاق دے دی تھی، جس کی وہ عدت گزار رہی تھی کہ مولیٰ نے اس کو فروخت کر دیا تو مشتری اس سے وطی نہیں کرے گا جب تک کہ اس کی عدت نہ گذر جائے، پھر عدت کے گزرنے کے بعد کیا مشتری پر استبراء واجب ہے؟ فرمایا کہ نہیں، کیونکہ باندی جب خریدی تھی اس وقت باندی کی شرمگاہ اس کیلئے حلال نہیں تھی
Ruling on the trick to drop istibra'. There is no harm in using a trick to drop istibra' according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad. We have mentioned both aspects in Shuf'a. The taken [position] is the saying of Abu Yusuf when it is known that the seller did not approach her in that purity period, and the saying of Muhammad when he approached her. Translation: The author said: There is no harm in using a trick to drop istibra' according to Abu Yusuf, contrary to Muhammad, and we have mentioned both aspects in the book of Shuf'a. The acting-upon [position] is the saying of Abu Yusuf in the case when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with her in that purity period, and the saying of Muhammad when he had intercourse. Explanation: According to Imam Abu Yusuf, there is no harm in the trick to drop istibra', and according to Imam Muhammad it is not permissible. The author says that we have stated both proofs in the book of Shuf'a. Then the author says that if it becomes known that the seller did not have intercourse with that slave girl in that purity period, then the saying of Abu Yusuf is taken, not that of Imam Muhammad. In Majma' al-Anhar, vol. 2, p. 523, it is said that the fatwa is given according to this detail.

First trick: And the trick, when the buyer has no free woman under him, is that he marries her before the purchase, then buys her. Translation: And the trick, when there is no free woman under the buyer, is that he marries this slave girl before buying, then buys her. Explanation: The author has stated two tricks here. This is the first trick: if the buyer has no free woman in his marriage, he should first marry this slave girl, then buy her. Upon buying, the marriage ends, and istibra' will not be obligatory because buying one's own wife does not require istibra'. The condition of having no free woman in marriage is placed because if he has a free wife, then marrying a slave girl is not permissible. Similarly, if he has four slave wives, then also this trick will not work because marrying this slave girl will not be permissible.

Second trick: And if she [a free woman] exists, then the trick is that the seller marries her before the purchase, or the buyer [marries her] before possession to someone trustworthy, then he buys her and takes possession, or takes possession, then the husband divorces her, because at the time of the existence of the cause, which is the acquisition of ownership confirmed by possession, when her private part was not lawful for him, istibra' is not obligatory, even if it becomes lawful afterwards, because consideration is only the existence of the cause, just as when she is in the idda of another. Translation: And if (there is a free woman in marriage), then the trick is that the seller marries her before the purchase, or the buyer before possession to a person who is trusted, then the buyer buys her and takes possession, or takes possession, then the husband divorces her, because when the cause exists, which is the acquisition of ownership confirmed by possession, when her private part was not lawful for him, istibra' is not obligatory, even if it becomes lawful afterwards, because consideration is only the time of existence of the cause, like when she is in the idda of another. Explanation: This is the second trick: that a person who is trusted to divorce her and not have intercourse with her, the seller marries her to him before the purchase, or the buyer before possession [marries her to him]. In both cases, at the time of acquisition of ownership and possession, her private part is not lawful for the buyer. Therefore, istibra' is not obligatory upon the buyer. Then her husband divorces her. Since the divorce is before consummation, no idda is obligatory, and no istibra' is obligatory upon the master, because at the time of acquisition of ownership and possession, due to her private part not being lawful, istibra' was not obligatory, and now it will not become obligatory because there is no new acquisition of ownership and possession. The example is exactly like someone buying a slave girl who was the wife of another and her husband divorced her, and she was observing idda, then the master sold her; the buyer will not have intercourse until her idda passes. Then after the idda passes, is istibra' obligatory upon the buyer? He said: No, because when the slave girl was bought, her private part was not lawful for him.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Karahiyah addresses the ruling on using a legal trick (hila) to drop the requirement of istibra' (waiting for one menstrual cycle) when purchasing a slave girl. There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Yusuf permits such a trick, while Imam Muhammad prohibits it. The author, al-Marghinani, states that the relied-upon position is that of Abu Yusuf, but only when it is known that the seller did not have intercourse with the slave girl during the purity period in question; if he did have intercourse, then Muhammad's view (disallowing the trick) is followed. Then two specific tricks are detailed. The first trick applies when the buyer has no free wife: he may marry the slave girl before purchasing her. Upon purchase, the marriage automatically ends (since a man cannot own his wife), and since one's own wife does not require istibra', the requirement is dropped. However, if the buyer already has a free wife, he cannot marry a slave girl concurrently, so this trick fails. Similarly, if he has four slave wives, he cannot marry another slave. The second trick applies when a free wife exists: the buyer or seller marries the slave girl to a trusted third party before the purchase or before possession. The buyer then purchases and takes possession of the slave girl while she is married to someone else, so at the moment of acquiring ownership and possession, her private part is not lawful to him, hence no istibra' is required. Afterwards, the husband (the third party) divorces her before consummation, so no idda is required either. The commentator illustrates this with an analogy: if a buyer purchases a slave girl who is in the idda of another man (e.g., after divorce), he must wait for her idda, but after it ends, no istibra' is required because at the time of purchase her private part was not lawful. The key principle is that the obligation of istibra' is tied to the moment of acquiring ownership and possession; if at that moment the woman's private part is not lawful to the buyer (due to marriage to another or idda), then istibra' is not required, even if it becomes lawful later.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hila): A legal trick or stratagem used to achieve a permissible result by circumventing a prohibition or obligation through a lawful means.
استبراء (istibra'): The waiting period of one menstrual cycle required for a slave girl purchased by a new master to ensure she is not pregnant from the previous owner.
مشتری (mushtari): The buyer of the slave girl.
قبض (qabd): Possession or taking delivery of the purchased item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the second trick, why is no idda required after the divorce?
A) Because the marriage was for a limited time
B) Because the divorce occurs before consummation (nikah ghayr dakhul)
C) Because the buyer is the new owner
D) Because the third party is trustworthy

Key Takeaway
Two lawful tricks to drop istibra' exist, each with specific conditions, based on the principle that istibra' is not required if at ownership the woman's private part is not halal.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
6 min
Stratagems to Avoid Istibra When Buying a Slave Woman
Explanation of two legal stratagems to avoid istibra

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi stratagems for avoiding istibra when buying a slave woman, explain why each works, and apply them to new scenarios.

Core Idea
Istibra is avoided if, at the moment of acquisition, the slave woman's private part is not lawful for the buyer.

Istibra is a waiting period to ensure a slave woman is not pregnant, required upon acquisition for intercourse. However, the Hanafi school permits legal stratagems to avoid this obligation. This passage from the Book of Disliked Matters explains two stratagems: marrying the slave woman before purchase or arranging a third-party marriage. Understanding these requires grasping the principle that istibra is linked to the moment of acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Principle of Istibra
Istibra is wajib when ownership and possession combine and the woman is lawful for the owner. The critical factor is the permissibility of intercourse at the moment of acquisition (milk wa yad).
2
First Stratagem: Marry Before Purchase
If the buyer has no free wife, he may marry the slave woman, then buy her. The marriage ends automatically upon purchase, and no istibra is needed because at acquisition she was already his wife.
Condition: no free wife and no four slave wives.
3
Second Stratagem: Third-Party Marriage
If the buyer has a free wife, a trustworthy third party marries the slave woman before the buyer takes possession. At the moment of acquisition, she is not lawful to the buyer, so istibra is not required. The husband then divorces her before consummation.
The third party must be trustworthy (will not consummate and will divorce).
4
Apply the Analogy
The ruling is supported by analogy to a slave woman bought during her waiting period from a previous marriage: at acquisition, she was not lawful, so no istibra is needed even after she becomes lawful.
This analogy (qiyas) confirms the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولو كانت فالحيلة ان يزوتجها البائع قبل الشرأ او المشترى قبل القبض ممن يوثق به ثم يشتريها ويقبضها اويقبضها ثم يطلق الزوج لان عند وجود السبب وهو استحداث الملك المؤكد بالقبض اذا لم يكن فرجها حلا لاله لا يـجـب الاستبرأ وان حل بعد ذلك لان المعتبرا وان وجود السبب كما اذا كانت معتدة الغير
ترجمہ اور اگر ہو تو حیلہ یہ ہے کہ بائع شراء سے پہلے اس کا نکاح کر دے یا مشتری کردے قبضہ سے پہلے اس آدمی کے ساتھ جس پر اعتماد کیا جاتا ہو پھر مشتری اس کو خریدے اور قبضہ کرے ( پہلی صورت میں ) یا اس پر قبضہ کرے ( دوسری صورت میں ) پھر شوہر اس کو طلاق دے اسلئے کہ سبب کے پائے جانے کے وقت اور وہ اس ملک کا استحداث ہے جو قبضہ سے مؤکد ہے جب اس کی شرمگاہ اس کیلئے حلال نہیں تھی تو استبراء واجب نہ ہوگا اگر چہ اس کے بعد حلال ہوگئی اس لئے کہ معتبر سبب کے پائے جانے کا وقت ہے۔ جیسا کہ جبکہ وہ غیر کی معتدہ ہو۔

The stratagem, if the buyer does not have a free woman under his authority, is that he marries her before purchase, then buys her. Explanation: The author mentions two stratagems. This is the first: if the buyer has no free wife in his nikah, he should marry the slave woman first. Then when he buys her, the marriage ends and istibra is not obligatory, because buying one's own wife does not require istibra. The condition of having a free wife is because if he has a free wife, marrying a slave woman is not permissible; similarly if he has four slave wives, this stratagem does not work. The second stratagem: If he has a free wife, the stratagem is that the seller marries her before the sale, or the buyer marries her before taking possession, to someone trustworthy, then the buyer buys and takes possession (in the first case) or takes possession (in the second case), then the husband divorces her. Because at the time the cause exists—which is the acquisition of ownership confirmed by possession—if her private part was not lawful for him, istibra is not obligatory, even if it becomes lawful afterwards, because the consideration is the time of the existence of the cause. Just as when she is in the waiting period of another. Explanation: This is the second stratagem: a trustworthy person who will divorce her and not have intercourse with her. The seller marries her before the sale, or the buyer marries her before taking possession. In both cases, at the time of acquiring ownership and possession, her private part is not lawful for the buyer, so istibra is not obligatory. Then her husband divorces her; since it is a divorce before consummation, no waiting period is obligatory, and no istibra is obligatory on the master, because at the time of acquiring ownership and possession, istibra was not obligatory due to the unlawfulness, and now it is not obligatory because there is no new acquisition of ownership and possession. The example is exactly like someone buying a slave woman who was the wife of another and her husband divorced her, and she is observing her waiting period. The master sells her; the buyer cannot have intercourse until her waiting period ends. After the waiting period ends, is istibra obligatory on the buyer? He said no, because when the slave woman was bought, her private part was not lawful for him, and when it became lawful, there was no new acquisition of ownership and possession.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Disliked Matters discusses two legal stratagems (hila) to avoid the obligation of istibra when purchasing a slave woman. Istibra is a waiting period to ensure the womb is empty, required when a person acquires a slave woman. The first stratagem applies when the buyer has no free wife: he may marry the slave woman before purchasing her. Upon purchase, the marriage terminates automatically, and no istibra is needed because buying one's own wife does not require istibra. This stratagem is valid only if the buyer has no free wife and no four slave wives, as marrying a slave woman is not permissible in those cases. The second stratagem applies when the buyer has a free wife: a trustworthy third party (the seller or the buyer before taking possession) marries the slave woman, then the buyer purchases and takes possession. Since at the moment of acquiring ownership and possession her private part was not lawful for him (she was married to another), istibra is not obligatory. After the marriage ends by divorce (before consummation, so no waiting period), she becomes lawful, but no istibra is required because the obligation is linked to the moment of acquisition, which has passed. The author supports this with an analogy: if a slave woman is bought while in another man's waiting period, istibra is not required because at acquisition she was unlawful.

Key Terms
حیلہ (hīlah): A legal stratagem to achieve a permissible result while avoiding a prohibited or obligatory rule.
استبراء (istibrā’): A waiting period for a female slave after acquisition to ensure she is not pregnant.
ملک وید (milk wa yad): Ownership and possession; the basis for the obligation of istibra.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for the first stratagem (marrying the slave woman before purchase) to be valid?
A) The buyer must have a free wife.
B) The buyer must have no free wife and no four slave wives.
C) The buyer must marry her after purchase.
D) The seller must be the one to marry her.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits avoiding istibra through valid marriages that ensure at the moment of acquisition the slave woman's private part is not lawful for the buyer.

Selling Animal Dung and Human Excrement: Dispute with Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on sale of najis al-'ayn items

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling animal dung and human excrement, explain the Shafi'i objection, and apply the Hanafi istihsan-based response to resolve the dispute.

Core Idea
Animal dung is permissible to sell due to benefit; human excrement is makruh pure but permissible mixed — impurity alone does not bar sale if customary benefit exists.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the sale of intrinsically impure (najis al-'ayn) items. While the Shafi'i school prohibits the sale of animal dung and human excrement due to their impurity, the Hanafi school distinguishes based on customary benefit (istihsan). Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi fiqh balances textual impurity rules with practical need.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its basis
Identify the ruling for animal dung (permissible) and human excrement (makruh pure, permissible mixed). Note the primary basis: benefit (manfa'ah) qualifies an item as property (mal).
The text uses 'la ba'sa' for animal dung and 'makruh' for pure human excrement.
2
Identify the opponent and their argument
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i prohibits both because they are najis al-'ayn, using qiyas to human excrement and dead animal skin before tanning.
The Shafi'i argument is based on strict analogy (qiyas) on the effective cause of impurity.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to animal dung
The Hanafi school differentiates: animal dung is beneficial without mixing, so it is property (mal) and thus subject to sale. This overrides the impurity analogy through istihsan (juristic preference based on custom).
The text states: 'It is thrown on land to increase produce, so it is property.'
4
Analyze the Hanafi ruling on human excrement
Pure human excrement is makruh because it is najis al-'ayn, but when mixed with soil/ash it becomes permissible to sell and use, analogized to olive oil mixed with impurity.
This is the narration from Imam Muhammad and is declared the correct (sahih) view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: Hanafi allows buying/selling animal dung and mixed human excrement; Shafi'i does not. The Hanafi view is mufta bihi, with later scholars even permitting sale of pure human excrement if beneficial.
See commentary references: 'Ayni and Zayli permit pure human excrement.

Chapter on sale. He (Muhammad) said: There is no harm in selling animal dung (sirqin), but selling human excrement ('adhirah) is makruh. Al-Shafi'i said: Selling animal dung is also not permissible because it is najis al-'ayn, so it resembles human excrement and the skin of a dead animal before tanning. Our proof is that benefit is taken from it: it is thrown on land to increase produce, so it is property (mal), and property is subject to sale. Contrary to human excrement, because benefit is taken from it only when mixed. The sale of mixed (human excrement) is permissible. This is the narration from Muhammad (al-Shaybani) and it is the correct view. Similarly, benefit from mixed (human excrement) is permissible, not from unmixed, according to the correct view. The mixed (human excrement) is like olive oil that has been mixed with impurity. Commentary: The sale of human excrement is makruh because it is najis al-'ayn, but it is thrown on land mixed with soil or ash or fertilizer. Sale of animal dung is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i considered it impermissible, analogizing animal dung to human excrement and dead animal skin before tanning. Our proof is that it is property because it is pure property used to strengthen land, and all property is subject to sale. Therefore sale of animal dung, manure, etc. is permissible. Benefit from human excrement is derived when it is mixed, and sale of mixed is permissible as narrated from Imam Muhammad, and this is the correct view. The ruling of mixed human excrement is like olive oil mixed with impurity — benefit from it is permissible, so its sale is also permissible. Note: If benefit from pure human excrement is deemed permissible, then its sale would also be permissible. (Majma' al-Anhur, p. 524, vol. 2) Also, Allamah 'Ayni and Zayli have corrected that benefit from pure human excrement is permissible. (Sikk al-Anhur, p. 474, vol. 2; Durr al-Mukhtar, p. 246, vol. 5)
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute on the sale of animal dung (sirqin) and human excrement ('adhirah). The Hanafi position: selling animal dung is permissible (la ba'sa) because it is beneficial as fertilizer, making it valid property (mal). Selling pure human excrement is makruh (disliked) because it is najis al-'ayn, but if it is mixed with soil or ash, it becomes permissible to sell and use. This is the view of Imam Muhammad and the correct position. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that animal dung is also not permissible, analogizing it to human excrement and dead animal skin, both of which are intrinsically impure. The Hanafi response: animal dung is different because it is beneficial without mixing, thus it is completely property. The commentary adds that later scholars like 'Ayni and Zayli even permitted sale of pure human excrement if benefit can be derived. This shows a nuanced approach considering customary benefit.

Key Terms
سِرْقِين (sirqin): Animal dung, especially used as fertilizer.
عَذِرَة ('adhirah): Human excrement, considered najis al-'ayn (intrinsically impure).
مَال (mal): Property; something of value that can be transacted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, impurity does not automatically prohibit sale; customary benefit (manfa'ah) qualifies an item as property, and istihsan may override strict analogy.

The Acceptance of a Single Person's Statement in Transactions
Ruling statement with a furu' example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a single sane person's statement is sufficient in mu'amalat and apply it to a transaction scenario.

Core Idea
One sane person's word suffices in transactions—practicality over formalism.

In daily transactions, we often rely on a single person's information, such as when a seller claims to be an agent. Hanafi fiqh validates this practice based on general custom and trust. This lesson explores the principle that in mu'amalat, the statement of one sane individual is acceptable, even if the person is not a qualified witness for testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act
The act is accepting the statement of a single individual in a transaction (mu'amalat). This is not testimony (shahadat) but a basis for action in buying, selling, etc.
2
Determine the hukm level
The ruling is mubah (permissible) and legally binding in the sense that one may act upon it. The text says 'it is permissible for him to buy and have intercourse' – indicating permissibility and validity.
It is not obligatory to accept; one may also decline.
3
List conditions for acceptance
Two conditions from the text: (1) The informant must be sane (aqil); (2) The report must be sound with no contestant (no one disputes the claim).
Gender, religion, or moral character do not affect acceptance in mu'amalat.
4
Apply to the furu' example
The author applies the principle: If you know a slave-girl belongs to Zaid, and another person sells her claiming to be Zaid's agent, you may buy her because the agent's single statement is accepted as a sound report with no contestant.
This shows the practical flexibility of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Distinguish from testimony
Testimony (shahadat) requires two just witnesses or one man plus two women, but in mu'amalat, one person's word suffices. This reflects the lesser evidentiary standard for transactions.
This distinction is crucial to avoid confusion.

Source Text

مذکورہ قاعدہ پر متفرع ہونے والا ایک مسئلہ
قال ومن علم بجارية انها لرجل فراى اخر يبيعها وقال وكلنى صاحبها ببيعها فانه يسعه ان يبتعها ويطأ ها لانه اخبر بخبر صحيح لا منازع له وقول الواحد المعاملات مقبول على اى وصف كان لما مر من قبل وكذا اذا
A sub-issue branching from the above-mentioned principle: He (the author) said: If someone knows that a slave-girl belongs to a man, then sees another person selling her and the seller says, 'The owner appointed me as agent to sell her,' then it is permissible for him to buy her and have intercourse with her, because he has given a sound report with no contestant. And the statement of one individual in transactions is accepted regardless of his description, as mentioned before. Similarly, if...
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents a general principle of Hanafi fiqh: in matters of transactions (mu'amalat), the statement of a single individual is acceptable and binding, provided he is sane (aqil). The person may be male or female, Muslim or non-Muslim, just or sinful. This is because transactions are built on general custom and trust, unlike legal testimony (shahadat), which requires strict conditions. The author then applies this principle to a specific example: if a person knows a slave-girl belongs to Zaid, and then sees another person selling her, claiming to be Zaid's agent, the buyer may trust that statement and proceed to purchase and even have intercourse with her (since she becomes his property). The basis is that it is a sound report (khabr sahih) with no one challenging it. This shows the practical flexibility of Hanafi law in everyday dealings.

Key Terms
معاملات (mu'amalat): Transactions, contracts, and dealings between people, as opposed to worship or testimony.
قول واحد (qawl al-wahid): The statement of a single individual, which is accepted in transactions.

Selling Dung and Human Waste: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling on sale of impure solids with Shafi'i rebuttal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling dung and human waste, explain the Hanafi proof based on utility, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection using the madhhab dispute map.

Core Idea
Impurity does not invalidate property when there is benefit.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents one of the classic inter-madhhab disputes: can impure substances like dung and human waste be sold? The Hanafi school, drawing on the principle that wealth (مال) is defined by utility, permits the sale of dung and mixed human waste, while the Shafi'i school prohibits them due to intrinsic impurity. Understanding this dispute reveals how each school weighs different legal indicators — here, impurity vs. benefit.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the rulings for dung (سرقين) and human waste (عذرة) as given in the matn: dung is permissible (لا بأس), human waste is disliked (يكره).
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State Imam al-Shafi'i's argument: both are najis al-ayn, so they resemble carrion hide before tanning, making their sale impermissible.
The opposing school uses qiyas (analogy) to established impermissible items.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Explain why dung is considered property (مال): it is beneficial as fertilizer, thus it is a legitimate subject of sale. This is a rational (aqli) proof based on utility.
The Hanafi definition of property includes any useful, non-prohibited thing.
4
Distinguish pure vs. mixed human waste
Pure human waste is not beneficial on its own, so its sale is disliked. When mixed with earth, it becomes useful, and its sale becomes permissible (narrated from Imam Muhammad).
Mixed human waste is analogized to olive oil contaminated with impurity – still usable.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow trade in dung (e.g., manure market), Shafi'is prohibit it entirely, affecting farmers and fertilizer industries.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and both positions have strong proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكراهية

فصل في البيع قال ولاباس ببيع السرقين ويكره بيع العذرة وقال الشافعى لا يجوز بيع السرقين ايضا لانه نجس العين فشابه العذرة وجلد المية قبل الدباغ ولنا انه منتفع به لا نه يلقى في الاراضى لاستكثار الريع فكان مالا والمال محل للبيع بخلاف العذرة لا نه ينتفع بها مخلوطا ويجوز بيع المخلوط هو المروى عن محمد وهو الصحيح وكذا لا يجوز الانتفاع بالمخلوط لا بغير المخلوط في الصحيح والمخلوط بمنزلة زيت خالطه النجاسة.
