اللہ کی رحمت سے دور ہونا اور یتیم فقط کفار کیلئے مخصوص ہے۔ - ابزار اور مقام صائین سے دور ہونا۔ اور یہاں یہی معنی مراد ہے اسلئے کہ اہل حق کے نزدیک بندہ گناہ کبیر کے ارتکاب کی محدسے ایمان سے خارج نہیں ہوتا۔ بہر حال احتکار جبکہ وہ اہل شہر کیلئے مضر ہو تو مکروہ تحریمی ہے اور اگر اہل شہر کو مضر نہ ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اس کے ساتھ عوام الناس کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے تو اس کو نہ بیچنے سے عوام کے حق کا ابطال اور ان کو پریشان کرنا ہے تو بصورت مضرت یہ مکروہ ہے اور اگر اس کی وجہ سے ضرر لاحق نہ ہو تو کر وہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ مالک نے اپنی ملکیت کو روکا ہے جس کا اس کو حق ہے اور بغیر کسی کو نقصان پہنچائے ہوئے روکا ہے۔ مذکورہ بالاحکم تلقی جلب میں بھی ہے وكذا التلقى على هذا التفصيل لان النبي عليه السلام نهى عن تلقى الجلب وعن تلقى الركبان قالوا هذا اذا لم يلبس المتلقى على التجار سعر البلدة فان لبس فهو مكروه في الوجهين لانه غادر بهم ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی تلقی اسی تفصیل پر ہے اسلئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے تلقی جلب اور قافلہ سے ملنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ متعلقی تاجروں پر شہر کے بھاؤ نہ چھپائے۔ پس اگر اس نے چھپایا تو یہ مکروہ ہے دونوں صورتوں میں اسلئے کہ یہ ان کو دھوکہ دینے والا ہے۔ تشریح احتکار میں جو تفصیل ہے وہی تلقی جلب میں ہے اگر یہ تلقی اہل شہر کو مضر ہو تو مکروہ ہے ورنہ نہیں ، اور کراہت کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے جو یہاں مذکور ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ یہ مذکورہ تفصیل اس وقت ہے جبکہ متلی تجار پرشہر کا بھاؤ نہ چھپائے اور اگر بھاؤ کچھ ہے اور دھوکہ دے کر کم بھاؤ میں لے لے تو یہ بہر صورت مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اب مختلفی دھوکہ باز ہے۔ مصنف نے جو حدیث نقل کی ہے یہ اصل میں دو حدیثیں ہیں پہلی حدیث نھی عن تلقى الجلب یہ الگ ہے جس کی تخریج مسلم نے کی ہے اور نھی عن تلقی الرکبان الگ ہے یہ متفق علیہ ہے اور مطلب دونوں کا ایک ہے۔
He said: Hoarding is disliked in the provisions of humans and animals, when that is in a town where hoarding harms its people, and likewise meeting caravans. But if it does not harm, then there is no harm in it. The basis for this is his saying (peace be upon him): 'The importer is blessed, and the hoarder is cursed.' And because the right of the general public is attached to it. Refraining from selling nullifies their right and constricts matters for them, so it is disliked when it harms them, such as when the town is small. Unlike when it does not harm, such as when the city is large, because he is detaining his property without harming others. Translation: Al-Quduri said: Hoarding (detaining grain waiting for high prices) is disliked in human food and animal fodder, when it is in a town where hoarding harms its inhabitants, and likewise meeting caravans. So when hoarding is not harmful, there is no harm in it. The proof is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The importer (who brings grain from outside and sells in the city) is blessed, and the hoarder is cursed.' And because the right of the general public has become attached to this food, and preventing sale nullifies their right and constricts their affair, so it is disliked when it harms them, in the manner that the town is small; unlike when it does not harm, in the manner that the city is large, because he is detaining his property without harming others. Explanation: Hoarding means holding grain or grass to sell when prices rise. Talqi means meeting the caravan people who come with grain and produce to the city, buying from them outside the city, intending to hold it and sell when prices rise. The mentioned hadith is in Ibn Majah. 'Jalib' is the one who buys grain from outside and brings it to the city to sell; he is blessed because people benefit from him, so the blessings of the Muslims' prayers reach him. 'Muhtakir' is the one who buys grain to withhold and cause harm to people. 'Mal'un' is of two types: being far from Allah's mercy (for disbelievers) and being far from the place of safety. Here the latter meaning is intended, because according to Ahl al-Haqq, a person who commits a major sin does not leave faith. In any case, hoarding is tahrimi makruh when harmful to the people of the city, and not disliked when not harmful, because the public's right is attached to it, so not selling nullifies their right and causes distress. So with harm it is disliked; if no harm arises, then not disliked because the owner detains his property, which he has the right to do, without harming anyone. The above ruling also applies to meeting caravans: 'And likewise meeting caravans according to this detail, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade meeting caravans and meeting riders. They said: This is when the one meeting does not conceal the city's price from the merchants. If he conceals, then it is disliked in both cases because he is deceiving them.' Translation: And likewise meeting caravans is according to this detail, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade meeting caravans and meeting riders. The scholars said: This is when the one meeting does not conceal the city's price from the merchants. If he conceals, then it is disliked in both cases because he is deceiving them. Explanation: The detail in hoarding applies similarly to meeting caravans. If this meeting harms the city people, it is disliked; otherwise not. And the proof of dislike is the hadith mentioned here. The scholars said that this detail applies when the one meeting does not conceal the city's price from the merchants; if he conceals and deceives to buy at a low price, then it is disliked in all cases because he is a deceiver. The hadiths narrated by the author are actually two hadiths: the first 'He forbade meeting caravans' is separate and narrated by Muslim, and 'He forbade meeting riders' is separate and agreed upon; the meaning of both is the same.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on hoarding (ihtikar) and meeting caravans (talqi). The author states that hoarding is makruh (disliked) in human food and animal fodder when it harms the people of the town. The key condition is harm: if the town is small and hoarding causes harm, it is makruh; if the city is large and hoarding does not cause harm, it is not disliked. The proof is the hadith: 'The importer is blessed, and the hoarder is cursed.' The commentary explains that hoarding means withholding goods to sell at a higher price. Talqi (meeting caravans) is similar: if it harms the public, it is disliked; if not, it is permissible. However, if the one meeting conceals the city's price or deceives the merchants, it is always disliked. The passage emphasizes the principle that the public's right is attached to essential goods, and withholding them harms the community. The ruling is within the Hanafi school, with the relied-upon position that hoarding is makruh tahrimi when harmful.

Key Terms
احتکار (iḥtikār): Hoarding: withholding food or fodder to sell at a higher price when the market becomes tight.
تلقی (talaqqī): Going out of the city to meet arriving caravans to buy goods before they reach the market.
جالب (jālib): One who brings goods from outside to sell in the city; considered blessed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is hoarding (ihtikar) not disliked according to the Hanafi school?
A) When the hoarder is a Muslim
B) When the city is large and no harm is caused to the public
C) When the goods are gold or silver
D) When the hoarder intends to give charity

Key Takeaway
Hoarding is only makruh tahrimi when it harms the public; without harm, it is permissible because the owner has the right to detain his property.

The Scope of Hoarding (Ihtikār): An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on items subject to hoarding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the scope of ihtikār and identify the muftā bihī position with its rationale.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school restricts hoarding to foodstuffs; the dispute turns on which harm is considered.

Hoarding (ihtikār) is makrūh taḥrīmī, but what items fall under this ruling? The three founding imams of the Hanafi school—Abū Ḥanīfa, Abū Yūsuf, and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī—disagree on the scope. This lesson unpacks their arguments and shows why the relied-upon position limits ihtikār to basic food provisions (aqwāt).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The contested legal question: which types of goods, when withheld from sale, constitute unlawful hoarding (ihtikār)?
2
State each imam's position
Abū Ḥanīfa: only foodstuffs (aqwāt) like wheat, barley, dried figs, and fodder. Abū Yūsuf: anything whose detention harms the public, including gold, silver, and clothes. Muḥammad: no hoarding in clothes.
All three agree ihtikār is blameworthy, but differ on coverage.
3
Understand each imam's rationale
Abū Ḥanīfa focuses on customary harm (ḍarar ma‘hūd muta‘ārif) – historically, food shortages cause public harm. Abū Yūsuf focuses on actual harm (ḥaqīqat al-ḍarar) – any item causing public hardship qualifies. Muḥammad likely sees clothes as non-essential.
The methodological difference: type of harm considered.
4
Determine the relied-upon view
The muftā bihī is Abū Ḥanīfa's position – ihtikār is restricted to food provisions. This is the Zāhir al-Riwāyah and the view preferred by later authorities like al-Marghinānī.
Fatwā practice follows Abū Ḥanīfa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
احتکار کن چیزوں میں ہوتا ہے... اقوال فقہاء وتخصيص الاحتكار بالاقوات كالحنطة والشعير والتين والقت قول ابى حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف كل ما اضر بالعامة حبسه فهو احتكار وان كان ذهبا أو فضة اوثوبا وعن محمد انه قال لا احتكار في الثياب فابو يوسف اعتبر حقيقة الضرر اذ هوا لمؤثر فى الكراهة و ابو حنيفة اعتبر الضرر المعهود المتعارف ترجمہ اور احتکار کو خاص کر دینا غذاؤں کے ساتھ جیسے گیہوں اور جو اور بھوسا اور اسپست ابوحنیفہ کا قول ہے اور فرمایا ابو یوسف نے ہر وہ چیز جس کار کو نا عوام کو مضر ہو پس وہ احتکار ہے اگر چہ وہ سونا ہو یا چاندی یا کپڑا، اور محمد سے منقول ہے انہوں نے کہا کہ کپڑوں میں احتکار نہیں ہے۔ پس ابو یوسف نے حقیقی ضرر کا اعتبار کیا اس لئے کہ کراہت میں یہی مؤثر ہے اور ابو حنیفہ نے اس ضرر کا اعتبار کیا جو معہود و متعارف ہے۔ تشریح احتکار فقط انسان اور چوپاؤں کی غذاء میں ہی ہوتا ہے یہ امام صاحب کا فرمان ہے اور امام ابو یوسف کا فرمان یہ ہے کہ جس چیز کے روکنے سے بھی عوام کوضر رملتا ہو۔ پس وہ احتکار ہے خواہ وہ کچھ بھی ہو امام محمد کا فرمان یہ ہے کہ کپڑوں میں احتکار نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ
Dispute: On what items does hoarding occur? Statements of the jurists. 'Specializing hoarding with provisions like wheat, barley, dried figs, and fodder is the saying of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: Everything the detention of which harms the public is hoarding, even if it is gold, silver, or clothes. And from Muhammad it is reported: There is no hoarding in clothes.' So Abu Yusuf considered the actual harm, as it is effective in dislike, and Abu Hanifa considered the customary and well-known harm. Translation: Restricting hoarding to foodstuffs like wheat, barley, fodder, and bhusa is the saying of Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf said: Everything the detention of which harms the public is hoarding, even if gold, silver, or clothes. And from Muhammad it is reported: There is no hoarding in clothes. So Abu Yusuf considered the actual harm, because it is effective in dislike, and Abu Hanifa considered the customary and well-known harm. Explanation: Hoarding occurs only in human and animal food, this is Imam Abu Hanifa's saying. Imam Abu Yusuf's saying: Whatever thing's detention harms the public is hoarding, whatever it may be. Imam Muhammad's saying: There will be no hoarding in clothes.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scope of items subject to hoarding (ihtikar). Three positions are presented: (1) Abu Hanifa restricts hoarding to provisions (foodstuffs) like wheat, barley, dried figs, and fodder. (2) Abu Yusuf expands it to anything whose detention harms the public, including gold, silver, and clothes. (3) Muhammad al-Shaybani excludes clothes from hoarding. The author provides the reasoning: Abu Yusuf considers actual harm (haqiqat al-darar), which is the effective cause of dislike. Abu Hanifa considers customary harm (al-darar al-mu'tad), i.e., the type commonly known to cause hardship, which is food. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that hoarding is specific to foodstuffs, as per Abu Hanifa. This dispute highlights the methodological difference: Abu Yusuf takes a literal approach based on the presence of harm, while Abu Hanifa restricts it to the typical context of the hadith and common practice.

Key Terms
اقوات (aqwāt): Provisions, foodstuffs that sustain humans and animals.
ضرر معہود متعارف (ḍarar maʿhūd mutaʿārif): Customary, well-known harm, typically from food shortages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, hoarding (ihtikār) applies to which items?
A) Any item that harms the public when withheld
B) Only foodstuffs like wheat, barley, and fodder
C) Food and clothes
D) Gold and silver

Key Takeaway
The muftā bihī Hanafi position restricts hoarding to foodstuffs, based on customary harm, despite broader views from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

The Conditional Ruling on Hoarding (Ihtikar)
States ruling on ihtikar with harm condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ihtikar and identify the condition that determines its hukm (makruh tahrimi or not).

Core Idea
Hoarding is makruh tahrimi only when it harms the public; otherwise, the owner's right prevails.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on ihtikar (hoarding). The text distinguishes between two scenarios based on harm to the public. We will unpack the condition that flips the ruling and understand the underlying principle of competing rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Conditional Ruling
First, note that the act is ihtikar (hoarding essential goods). The ruling is not absolute; it depends on a condition. State the two possible rulings: makruh tahrimi when harmful, and not makruh when harmless.
The text uses 'مکروہ تحریمی' for the harmful case.
2
Distinguish the Two Scenarios
Contrast the two scenarios: when hoarding is 'مضر' (harmful) to the people of the city versus when it is not. Understand that the presence or absence of harm is the decisive factor.
Harm is defined in relation to the townspeople (اهل شہر).
3
Analyze the Legal Principle (Talil)
The text provides a reason: when harmful, the public's right becomes attached, so withholding nullifies that right. When harmless, the owner merely exercises his property right. Identify the balancing of public interest versus individual ownership.
This is a clear example of talil (reasoning) based on harm.
4
Apply the Condition to a Hypothetical
Consider a scenario: a merchant hoards wheat during a famine (harmful) vs. hoarding spices when plenty is available (harmless). Apply the ruling to each, stating whether it is makruh or not.
This helps internalize the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بہر حال احتکار جبکہ وہ اہل شہر کیلئے مضر ہو تو مکروہ تحریمی ہے اور اگر اہل شہر کو مضر نہ ہو تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ اس کے ساتھ عوام الناس کا حق وابستہ ہو گیا ہے تو اس کو نہ بیچنے سے عوام کے حق کا ابطال اور ان کو پریشان کرنا ہے تو بصورت مضرت یہ مکروہ ہے اور اگر اس کی وجہ سے ضرر لاحق نہ ہو تو کر وہ نہیں ہے اسلئے کہ مالک نے اپنی ملکیت کو روکا ہے جس کا اس کو حق ہے اور بغیر کسی کو نقصان پہنچائے ہوئے روکا ہے۔
In any case, hoarding (ihtikar), when it is harmful to the people of the city, is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). And if it is not harmful to the people of the city, then it is not makruh. This is because the right of the general public has become attached to it; so by not selling it, the right of the public is nullified and they are distressed. Therefore, in the case of harm, it is makruh. And if no harm results from it, then it is not makruh, because the owner has withheld his property, which he has a right to do, and he has withheld it without causing harm to anyone.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage is a direct ruling statement on ihtikar (hoarding). The author distinguishes between two scenarios: when hoarding harms the townspeople, it is makruh tahrimi; when it does not cause harm, it is not disliked. The reasoning is based on balancing rights: the public has a right to essential goods, so withholding them when harmful violates that right. If no harm, the owner's property right prevails. This is a clear Hanafi position that connects the ruling to the presence or absence of harm.

Key Terms
احتکار (iḥtikār): Hoarding essential goods for resale at higher prices, causing harm to the public.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is ihtikar (hoarding) considered makruh tahrimi according to this text?
A) Always, regardless of harm
B) Only when it causes harm to the people of the city
C) Only when the hoarder is a merchant
D) Only when the goods are non-essential

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on ihtikar is conditional: it is makruh tahrimi only when it causes harm to the public; otherwise, it is not disliked.

Talaqqi al-Jalb: The Ruling on Intercepting Incoming Merchants
Extends the ruling of ihtikar to talaqqi with a similar condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talaqqi al-jalb and apply the condition of concealment of market price to determine when it is makruh.

Core Idea
Talaqqi is makruh when it involves deception; otherwise it follows the ruling of ihtikar.

This passage extends the detailed ruling of ihtikar (hoarding) to talaqqi (meeting incoming traders). While the Prophet forbade this practice, the Hanafi school conditions the ruling on whether the interceptor conceals the city's market price, thereby deceiving the merchants. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the prohibition in various market scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is talaqqi al-jalb – going out to meet incoming caravans carrying goods for sale before they reach the city market. The ruling is makruh under certain conditions.
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's prohibition, but conditioned by Hanafi scholars.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'نهى عن تلقى الجلب وعن تلقى الركبان' – the Prophet forbade meeting the caravans and the riders.
This is an ahad hadith with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Trace the condition
The scholars explain that the prohibition applies specifically when the interceptor conceals the city's market price from the merchants. If he does not conceal, then talaqqi follows the same detail as ihtikar: makruh if it harms the townspeople, otherwise permissible.
Concealment is the key factor that makes it always makruh due to deceit.
4
Understand the consequence
If the interceptor conceals the price, talaqqi is makruh in all cases because of deception. If no concealment, the ruling depends on whether the act harms the townspeople – if harmful, makruh; if not, permissible.
The harm condition mirrors ihtikar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذا التلقى على هذا التفصيل لان النبي عليه السلام نهى عن تلقى الجلب وعن تلقى الركبان قالوا هذا اذا لم يلبس المتلقى على التجار سعر البلدة فان لبس فهو مكروه في الوجهين لانه غادر بهم ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی تلقی اسی تفصیل پر ہے اسلئے کہ نبی علیہ السلام نے تلقی جلب اور قافلہ سے ملنے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ متعلقی تاجروں پر شہر کے بھاؤ نہ چھپائے۔ پس اگر اس نے چھپایا تو یہ مکروہ ہے دونوں صورتوں میں اسلئے کہ یہ ان کو دھوکہ دینے والا ہے۔ تشریح احتکار میں جو تفصیل ہے وہی تلقی جلب میں ہے اگر یہ تلقی اہل شہر کو مضر ہو تو مکروہ ہے ورنہ نہیں ، اور کراہت کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے جو یہاں مذکور ہے۔ مشائخ نے فرمایا کہ یہ مذکورہ تفصیل اس وقت ہے جبکہ متلی تجار پرشہر کا بھاؤ نہ چھپائے اور اگر بھاؤ کچھ ہے اور دھوکہ دے کر کم بھاؤ میں لے لے تو یہ بہر صورت مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اب مختلفی دھوکہ باز ہے۔
And similarly, talaqqi (meeting incoming traders) follows this same detail, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade meeting the caravans (talaqqi al-jalb) and meeting the riders (talaqqi al-rukban). They (the scholars) said: This applies when the one who meets does not conceal the city's market price from the merchants. If he conceals it, then it is makruh in both cases, because he is deceiving them. Translation: And similarly, talaqqi is on this same detail, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade meeting caravans and meeting the riders. The scholars said: This is when the one who meets does not conceal the city's market price from the merchants. So if he conceals, it is makruh in both cases, because he is a deceiver. Commentary: The detail that is in ihtikar is the same in talaqqi al-jalb. If this talaqqi is harmful to the people of the city, it is makruh; otherwise not. And the proof of karahah is this hadith mentioned here. The scholars said that this mentioned detail is when the one who meets does not conceal the city's market price from the merchants. And if the price is something and he deceives and takes it at a lower price, then it is makruh in both cases because now he is a deceiver.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage extends the ruling of ihtikar to talaqqi (meeting incoming traders before they reach the city). The passage type is a ruling with proof. The proof is the Prophet's prohibition of talaqqi al-jalb and talaqqi al-rukban. The key condition: if the person meeting the traders hides the city's market price from them, it is makruh in all cases because of deceit. If he does not hide the price, then the ruling follows the same detail as ihtikar: makruh if it harms the townspeople. The commentary further clarifies that concealing the price always makes it makruh, regardless of harm, because it involves deception. The hadith is cited as the basis for the prohibition.

Key Terms
تلقي الجلب (talaqqī al-jalb): Going out to meet incoming caravans carrying goods for sale before they reach the city market.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Talaqqi is not inherently prohibited; its ruling depends on whether the interceptor conceals market price or causes harm to the townspeople.
